Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
10 min
Definition of 'Amm: Conditions and the Exclusion of Mushtarak
Definition and conditions of 'amm with refutation of alternative inclusiveness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of 'amm, identify the required type of inclusiveness (istighraq shumuli), and apply the definition to exclude mushtarak and indefinite positive plurals.

Core Idea
For 'amm, inclusiveness must be simultaneous (shumuli), not alternative (badali); this excludes mushtarak and indefinite plurals.

In this passage, the commentator explains the precise definition of 'amm (general term) in Hanafi usul. The key condition is that the word must be inclusive of all its potential individuals simultaneously (istighraq 'ala sabil al-shumul). This excludes words like mushtarak (homonyms) and indefinite positive plurals, which only have alternative inclusiveness. Understanding this distinction is fundamental for correctly identifying general commands in the Quran and Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition's components
Recognize that 'amm is defined by three conditions: single placement (wad' wahid), unrestricted plurality (kathir ghayr mahsur), and simultaneous inclusiveness (istighraq shumuli).
The definition is: 'a word placed by a single placement for many unrestricted individuals, on condition that it includes all that is suitable for it.'
2
Distinguish the two types of istighraq
Understand shumuli (comprehensive) vs. badali (alternative) inclusiveness. Shumuli covers all individuals at once (e.g., plural forms like 'rijal'), while badali covers them one at a time (e.g., conditional 'man').
Hanafi requires shumuli for 'amm.
3
Examine the exclusion of mushtarak
Mushtarak is excluded only when used for multiple distinct meanings; if used for one meaning across individuals, it functions as 'amm.
Example: 'ayn for 'eye' (single meaning) is 'amm if referring to all eyes.
4
Apply the evidence against badali
If badali sufficed, indefinite positive (nakirah muthbatah) would be 'amm, but no scholar accepts that. Therefore, badali must be insufficient.
The indefinite plural (jami' munkar muthbat) also has badali and yet is not considered 'amm.
5
Confirm the Hanafi ruling
Conclude that 'amm requires istighraq shumuli, and mushtarak is excluded by that condition.
The definition is precise: the word must be mustaghriq jami' ma yasluhu bi-istighraq shumuli.

عام میں داخل ہونا چاہیے ان لوگوں کے نزدیک بھی جو اس کے عموم کے قاتل نہیں ہیں۔ لہذا یہ کہنا پڑے گا کہ مشترک مستغرق کی قید سے خارج ہو جاتا ہے والمراد بالوضع : یہ شرح کی عبارت کا تیسرا حصہ ہے یہاں سے شاریخ ایک استفسار کا جواب دے رہے ہیں۔ استفسار :- یہ ہے کہ صاحب توضیح نے وضع لکیر کے تحت تین چیزوں کو داخل کیا ہے مشترک ، عام، اسماء عدد کہ یہ موضوع للکثیر ہیں، ان کی وضع للکثیر کیسے ہے؟
His statement: 'al-amm lafz': This is the first part of the commentary's phrase. From here the commentator transmits the definition of 'amm and explains it: 'amm is called a word that is placed by a single placement for many unrestricted [individuals] on condition that that word includes all that is suitable for it. In this definition, the restriction 'by a single placement' is precautionary; by it, mushtarak (homonym) is excluded. But the exclusion of mushtarak is not absolute; rather it is when mushtarak is related to multiple meanings; then mushtarak is excluded. However, if it is related to a single meaning for all individuals of the mushtarak, then it enters under 'amm. For example, the word 'ayn; if it is related to multiple meanings, it is excluded from 'amm, but if related to all individuals of the power of sight, it remains under 'amm and is not excluded. 'And the closer...' : The author of al-Talwih says: My opinion is that it should be said that the purpose of the restriction 'single placement' is not exclusion but clarification; as for mushtarak, it is excluded by the subsequent restriction 'inclusive of all that is suitable' because in 'amm there is istighraq (inclusiveness) while in mushtarak there is no istighraq. 'If it is said: The intended...' : This is the second part of the commentary's phrase; the commentator intends to quote a question and answer. The question: That mushtarak cannot be excluded by the restriction 'inclusive' because inclusiveness is divided: inclusiveness in the manner of shumul (comprehensive) as occurs in the forms of plural and collective noun, e.g., rijal and qawm; rijal is the form of plural and qawm is a collective noun because it has no singular. These two forms are inclusive of their individuals in the manner of shumul, i.e., simultaneously including all those individuals. Or inclusiveness in the manner of badaliyyah (alternative) e.g., 'Whoever enters my house, or else he has so much'; here inclusiveness is in the manner of badaliyyah due to the context of 'or'. So in mushtarak, although inclusiveness in the manner of shumul is not found, it is found in the manner of badaliyyah. Therefore, when inclusiveness in the manner of badaliyyah is found, it remains under 'amm. So inevitably we exclude it by the restriction 'single placement'. The answer: That it is not correct to say generality (umum) in the definition of 'amm; rather in the definition of 'amm, inclusiveness in the manner of shumul is determined. And you have already admitted that in mushtarak inclusiveness is in the manner of badaliyyah, not in the manner of shumul. Therefore, mushtarak is excluded by the restriction 'inclusive'. As for what is the evidence that it is not correct to say 'umum'? Its evidence is that if we say 'umum', then the indefinite positive (nakirah muthbatah) would enter the definition of 'amm because in the indefinite positive there is inclusiveness in the manner of badaliyyah. So it would enter the definition of 'amm, while no one believes in its generality. So the definition would not prevent the entry of non-applicable items. Therefore, it must be said that inclusiveness in the manner of shumul is determined in the definition of 'amm. Upon this answer, a question arises: Even if we make 'umum' in inclusiveness, the indefinite positive would not enter the definition of 'amm because in the definition there is the restriction 'placed for many' and the indefinite positive is not placed for many. So 'umum' remains as it is, and mushtarak does not enter the definition of 'amm. The answer: That your objection is valid concerning the indefinite singular. But if the indefinite positive is in the plural form, i.e., a positive indefinite plural, then it is placed for many meanings even according to those scholars who do not believe in its generality. And in it inclusiveness in the manner of badaliyyah is also found. In summary, if inclusiveness in the manner of badaliyyah is sufficient for 'amm, then the indefinite plural should enter under 'amm even according to those who do not believe in its generality. Therefore, it must be said that mushtarak is excluded by the restriction 'inclusive'. 'And by placement...' : This is the third part of the commentary's phrase; from here the commentator is answering an inquiry. The inquiry: That the author of al-Tawdih included three things under 'placed for many': mushtarak, 'amm, and the nouns of number; they are placed for many. How is their placement for many?
Source pages p. 505

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary (sharh) on the definition of 'amm (general term) from a Hanafi usul work. The author begins by quoting the definition: 'amm is a word placed by a single placement for many unrestricted individuals, including all that it can properly apply to. The first restrictive condition, 'by a single placement' (wad'an wahidan), is intended to exclude mushtarak (homonyms) when they are used for multiple distinct meanings. However, if a homonym is used for a single meaning covering multiple individuals (like 'ayn for all eyes), it does fall under 'amm. The commentator (al-Talwih) offers a refinement: the purpose of that restriction is not exclusion but clarity; the real exclusion of mushtarak comes from the condition 'inclusive of all it applies to' (mustaghriq jami' ma yasluhu) because 'amm requires istighraq (inclusiveness) while mushtarak lacks it. A question arises: mushtarak does have istighraq of the badali type (alternative), as in conditional sentences like 'Whoever enters my house...', where the inclusiveness is alternative. So how is mushtarak excluded? The answer is that the istighraq in 'amm must be of the shumul type (simultaneous), not badali. Evidence: if badali were sufficient, the indefinite positive (nakirah muthbatah) would enter, but no scholar considers it 'amm. Yet a counter-question notes that indefinite singular is not placed for many, so it wouldn't enter. The response: indefinite plural (like 'rijaalun') is placed for many and has badali inclusiveness; thus if badali sufficed, it would be 'amm, which is false. Therefore, mushtarak is excluded by the requirement of shumul inclusiveness. The passage ends with an inquiry about how the author of al-Tawdih includes mushtarak, 'amm, and number nouns as 'placed for many'.

Key Terms
العام (al-amm): A word placed by a single placement for many unrestricted individuals that includes all that is suitable for it
المشترک (al-mushtarak): A word that has multiple distinct meanings, e.g., 'ayn (eye, spring, self)
الاستغراق (al-istighraq): Inclusiveness; the quality of a word covering all the individuals it applies to
النكرة المثبتة (al-nakirah al-muthbatah): An indefinite noun in a positive context, e.g., 'rajulun' (a man)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What type of inclusiveness (istighraq) does the Hanafi school require for the definition of 'amm (general term)?
A) Istighraq 'ala sabil al-badal (alternative inclusiveness)
B) Istighraq 'ala sabil al-shumul (simultaneous inclusiveness)
C) Both types are acceptable
D) No inclusiveness is required

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of 'amm requires istighraq 'ala sabil al-shumul, excluding mushtarak and indefinite plurals from being general.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
Refining the Definition of ʿĀmm: Collective vs. Alternative Inclusion
Refining the definition of 'aam by requiring istighraq ala sabiil al-shumool

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between collective and alternative inclusion in the definition of ʿāmm and apply the correct Hanafi condition to identify whether a term is ʿāmm.

Core Idea
A word is ʿāmm only if it includes all its individuals collectively – alternative inclusion does not suffice.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the definition of ʿāmm (general) is precise. One key condition is that the inclusion of individuals must be collective (istighraq ala sabiil al-shumool), not alternative (istighraq ala sabiil al-badal). This lesson examines why alternative inclusion, as found in homonyms (mushtarak) and positive indefinite nouns (nakirah muthbatah), fails to make a word ʿāmm, and why collective inclusion is indispensable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two modes of inclusion
Recognize that inclusion can be either collective (covering all individuals at once) or alternative (covering one individual at a time). Examples: plural nouns like rijal show collective inclusion; conditional phrases like 'whoever enters' show alternative inclusion.
2
Analyze the mushtarak (homonym)
Understand that mushtarak has multiple meanings but can only refer to one meaning at a time, thus alternative inclusion, not collective. Therefore, it is excluded from ʿāmm.
3
Examine the nakirah muthbatah (positive indefinite)
Note that positive indefinite, whether singular or plural, also has alternative inclusion. If alternative inclusion sufficed, even plural indefinite would be ʿāmm, which is universally rejected.
4
Apply the Hanafi condition
Conclude that collective inclusion is the essential shart for ʿāmm. This excludes mushtarak and nakirah muthbatah from being ʿāmm.

Source Text

ہو جیسے جمع اور اسم جمع کے صیغہ میں ہوتا ہے مثلا ر جال اور قوم ان میں رجال جمع کا صیغہ ہے اور قوم اسم جمع ہے کیونکہ اس کا مفرد نہیں ہے۔ اور یہ دونوں صیغے اپنے افراد کو مستغرق ہیں علی سبیل الشمول یعنی بیک وقت ان تمام افراد کو شامل ہیں۔ یا استغراق علی سبیل البدلیت ہو جیسے من دخل داری او لا فله كذا یہاں استغراق علی سبیل البدلیت ہے اولا کے قرینہ سے۔ پس مشترک میں اگر چہ استغراق علی سبیل الشمول نہیں پایا جاتا لیکن علی سبیل البدلیت پایا جاتا ہے۔ لہذا جب استغراق علی سبیل البدلیت پایا جاتا ہے تو یہ عام کے تحت داخل رہا۔ تو لامحالہ اس کو وضعا واحدا کی قید سے خارج کریں گے۔ جواب:- یہ ہے کہ عام کی تعریف میں استغراق کے عموم کا قول کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے بلکہ عام کی تعریف میں استغراق علی سبیل الشمول متعین ہے اور آپ مان چکے ہیں کہ مشترک میں استغراق علی سبیل البدلیت ہے علی سبیل الشمول نہیں ہے لہذا یہ یعنی مشترک مستغرق کی قید سے خارج ہو گیا باقی کیا دلیل ہے کہ عموم کا قول کرنا درست نہیں ۔ اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اگر تمیم کا قول کریں تو نکرہ مثبتہ عام کی تعریف میں داخل ہو جائے گا اس لیے کہ نکرہ مثبتہ میں استغراق علی سبیل البدلیت پایا جاتا ہے تو یہ عام کی تعریف میں داخل ہو گیا ۔ حالانکہ کوئی بھی اس کے عموم کا قائل نہیں ہے تو تعریف دخول غیر سے مانع نہیں رہے گی۔ لہذا کہنا پڑے گا کہ عام کی تعریف میں استغراق علی سبیل الشمول متعین ہے۔ اس جواب پر سوال :۔ ہوتا ہے کہ استغراق میں تمیم بھی کر لیں تو بھی نکرہ مثبتہ عام کی تعریف میں داخل نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ تعریف میں وضع لکثیر کی قید لگی ہوئی ہے اور نکرہ مثبتہ کی کثیر کے لیے وضع نہیں ہے لہذا تمیم اپنے حال پر باقی رہی اور مشترک عام کی تعریف میں داخل بھی نہیں ہوا۔ جواب:۔ یہ ہے کہ آپ کا اعتراض نکرہ مفردہ کے اعتبار سے تو صحیح ہے۔ لیکن اگر نکرہ مثبتہ جمع کا صیغہ ہویعنی جمع نکرہ مثبت ہو تو یہ موضوع ہے کثیر معانی کے لیے ان علماء کے نزدیک بھی جو اس کے عموم کے قائل نہیں ہیں ۔ اور اس میں استغراق علی سبیل البدلیت بھی پایا جاتا ہے خلاصہ یہ کہ اگر استغراق علی سبیل البدل عام کے لئے کافی ہے تو پھر جمع منکر کو عام میں داخل ہونا چاہیے ان لوگوں کے نزدیک بھی جو اس کے عموم کے قائل نہیں ہیں۔ لہذا یہ کہنا پڑے گا کہ مشترک مستغرق کی قید سے خارج ہو جاتا ہے
It is like what occurs in the form of plural and collective noun, for example rijal and qawm; among them rijal is a plural form and qawm is a collective noun because it has no singular. And both these forms include their individuals collectively, meaning they include all those individuals at once. Or inclusion could be alternatively, like 'whoever enters my house or does not, he has such', here it is alternative inclusion because of the word 'or'. Thus in a homonym (mushtarak), although collective inclusion is not found, alternative inclusion is found. Therefore, when alternative inclusion is found, it falls under 'aam. So necessarily we exclude it by the condition of being placed as one. The answer is: it is not correct to say that inclusion in the definition of 'aam is general; rather in the definition of 'aam, inclusion collectively is specific, and you have already accepted that in a homonym there is alternative inclusion, not collective inclusion. So it, i.e., the homonym, is excluded by the condition of inclusion. As for the remaining proof that saying general is not correct, its proof is that if you say it is general, then the positive indefinite would enter into the definition of 'aam, because in the positive indefinite, alternative inclusion is found, so it would enter the definition of 'aam. Yet no one holds that it is general, so the definition would not prevent the entry of other things. Therefore it must be said that in the definition of 'aam, collective inclusion is specific. Upon this answer, a question: It occurs that if we also include generality in inclusion, then the positive indefinite would not enter the definition of 'aam, because in the definition there is the condition of being placed for many, and the positive indefinite is not placed for many. So the condition remains and the homonym does not enter the definition of 'aam. The answer: Your objection is correct with respect to the singular indefinite, but if the positive indefinite is in the form of plural, i.e., an indefinite plural positive, then it is placed for many meanings, even according to those who do not hold it to be general. And in it alternative inclusion is also found. The summary is that if alternative inclusion is sufficient for 'aam, then the indefinite plural should enter into 'aam even according to those who do not hold it to be general. Therefore it must be said that the homonym is excluded by the condition of inclusion.
Source pages p. 506

Commentary
This passage is a discussion on refining the definition of 'aam (general) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author argues that for a word to be 'aam, it must include all its individuals collectively (istighraq ala sabiil al-shumool), not alternatively (ala sabiil al-badal). The discussion begins with an example from plural and collective nouns. Then the author examines the case of mushtarak (homonym). In a homonym, the word has multiple meanings and can refer to any one of them alternatively, not all at once. If we allowed alternative inclusion as sufficient for 'aam, then mushtarak would be 'aam. However, previously it was excluded because it is not placed for a single meaning. The author then responds by asserting that only collective inclusion qualifies, so mushtarak is excluded. To prove that alternative inclusion is not enough, the author raises the case of positive indefinite (nakirah muthbatah). In positive indefinite, alternative inclusion exists (e.g., 'a man' can refer to any man alternatively), but no usuli considers it general. Therefore, the definition must be specific to collective inclusion. Then a questioner objects that the positive indefinite is not placed for many, so even with alternative inclusion it wouldn't enter. The answer distinguishes between singular indefinite and plural indefinite. A plural indefinite (like 'some men') is indeed placed for many and has alternative inclusion. If alternative inclusion were enough, then plural indefinite would be 'aam, which is not accepted. Thus the condition of collective inclusion stands, excluding mushtarak.

Key Terms
عام (ʿāmm): A word that includes all its individuals collectively (istighraq ala sabiil al-shumool).
استغراق (istighrāq): The inclusion of all individuals; can be collective (shumool) or alternative (badal).
مشترک (mushtarak): A word with multiple unrelated meanings; not 'aam because it lacks collective inclusion.
نكرة مثبتة (nakirah muthbatah): Indefinite positive; singular is not placed for many, plural is placed for many but still not 'aam due to alternative inclusion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is a homonym (mushtarak) excluded from being ʿāmm?
A) Because it is not placed for many.
B) Because its inclusion is alternative, not collective.
C) Because it has multiple meanings.
D) Because it is indefinite.

Key Takeaway
A word is ʿāmm only if it includes all its individuals collectively; alternative inclusion does not constitute generality in Hanafi usul.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

Three Types of 'Placed for Many' (Wad' li Kathir)
Explaining the three categories of wad' li kathir with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three forms of wad' li kathir (by individuals, by particulars, by parts) and apply the condition that parts must be same in name to classify a word as 'placed for many'.

Core Idea
A word 'placed for many' can be by individuals, particulars, or parts — but parts must share the same name.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the concept of 'wad' li kathir' (placed for many) helps classify words as general, homonym, or numeral. This lesson breaks down the three distinct forms: multiplicity by individuals (found in homonyms), by particulars (found in general words), and by parts (found in numerals). We also address two key objections: why proper names like Zayd are not 'placed for many' even though they have parts, and how the negative indefinite (nakirah manfiyyah) qualifies as general through type placement.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the initial query
Understand that the commentator is answering a question: how can homonyms, general words, and numerals all be considered 'placed for many'?
The query arises from a previous statement in al-Tawdih.
2
Identify the three forms of multiplicity
Distinguish the three forms: (1) each individual among many is separately placed for, (2) a universal meaning covers many particulars, (3) a sum of parts as a whole.
These correspond to homonyms, general words, and numerals respectively.
3
Map forms to examples
Note that homonyms have multiplicity by individuals, general words by particulars, numerals by parts. Understand why each fits its category.
E.g., 'ayn has multiple distinct meanings; 'man' applies to all humans; 'hundred' consists of units.
4
Analyze the objection about proper names
Consider why Zayd and 'Amr are not wad' li kathir despite having parts. The condition is that parts must be 'the same in name' (muttafiq bi hasab al-ism).
Zayd's parts (hand, foot) have different names, so they do not constitute the same type of part.
5
Understand the negative indefinite resolution
The negative indefinite (e.g., 'no man') is general even though not placed for many individually. It relies on type placement (wad' naw'iy) rather than personal placement (wad' shakhsi).
Its generality is intellectual and necessary, based on usage in negation.

And the meaning of 'placement' (wad'): This is the third part of the commentary text; here the commentator is answering a query. The query: The author of al-Tawdih included three things under 'placed for many': the homonym, the general, and numerals; they are placed for many. How is their placement for many? The answer: Placement for many includes generalization. The first form is that it is placed for each individual among the many. The second form is that the word is placed for a universal meaning and the units of the many fall under that universal meaning. The third form is that it is placed for the sum of the units of the many as a whole. If it is the first form, i.e., placed for each single unit among the many, then each single unit becomes the thing placed for. If it is the second form, then the thing placed for is the universal meaning, and the units of the many are particulars of that meaning. If it is the third form, then the meaning placed for is the sum as a whole, and the units of the many are parts of the thing placed for. Now the first form has multiplicity with respect to individuals; this is found in homonyms. The second form has multiplicity with respect to particulars; this is found in general words. The third form has multiplicity with respect to parts; this is found in numerals. Then a question: This is the fourth part of the commentary text; the purpose is that the commentator transmits a question and answers it. The question: Due to the generality of 'placed for many', words like Zayd, 'Amr, and 'man' would fall under 'placed for many' because the multiplicity with respect to parts is found in them; i.e., they also have placement for a sum in terms of parts, so they should be general, whereas they are specific. The answer: In 'placed for many', multiplicity with respect to parts does not refer to absolute parts, but rather parts that are the same in name (muttafiq bi hasab al-ism), such as the units under 'one hundred' which are included and agree in name. Unlike Zayd and 'Amr, which have parts each with a different name, like hand, foot, etc. When parts are the same in name, their boundary merges with particulars. It is like man applies to Zayd, 'Amr, and 'man' etc.; each is called a particular of man. Similarly, each unit of one hundred is said to be a unit of one hundred. Then if it is said: The negative indefinite (nakirah manfiyyah) is general and is not placed for many. We say: Placement is more general than personal (shakhsi) and type (naw'iy). And it has been established from their usage of the negative indefinite that the ruling is negated from the numerous unlimited, and the word includes every individual in the ruling of negation, meaning the generality of negation from individuals in the singular, and from the collective in the plural; it is not the negation of generality. This is the meaning of type-placement for that. And that its generality is intellectual and necessary, in the sense that...
Source pages p. 506

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the concept 'wad' li kathir' (placed for many) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The commentator first addresses a query about how the three categories (mushtarak, 'aam, asma' al-'adad) are each placed for many. The answer presents three distinct forms: (1) placed for each individual among many (e.g., a homonym like 'ayn which has multiple meanings, each meaning is an individual), (2) placed for a universal meaning under which many particulars fall (e.g., 'aam like 'man' which applies to all human individuals), and (3) placed for a sum of units as a whole (e.g., numerals like 'a hundred' where each unit is a part of the sum). The commentator then considers an objection: if being placed for many includes the third form (by parts), then proper names like Zayd and 'Amr, which have parts (limbs), would be considered 'placed for many' and thus general, but they are specific. The response is that the parts must be 'the same in name' (muttafiq bi hasab al-ism), like the units of a hundred, not limbs with distinct names. Following this, the Arabic passage addresses another objection: the negative indefinite (nakirah manfiyyah, e.g., 'no man') is considered 'aam even though it is not placed for many. The answer distinguishes between personal placement (wad' shakhsi, for a particular thing) and type placement (wad' naw'iy, for a pattern). The negative indefinite's generality is a matter of 'aql (intellect) and necessity, and it functions as a type placement, not personal placement.

Key Terms
وضع لکثیر (wadʿ li kathīr): A word placed for many; it encompasses three types based on how multiplicity is realized: by individuals, by particulars, or by parts.
شخشی (shakhṣī): Personal placement: a word is placed for a specific single meaning (e.g., proper name).
نوعی (nawʿī): Type placement: a word is placed for a pattern or general meaning (e.g., negative indefinite).
نكرة منفية (nakirah manfiyyah): A negative indefinite (e.g., 'no man') that is considered 'aam due to its usage in negation, though not placed for many individually.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is an example of a word placed for many by parts (kathrat bi hasab al-ajza)?
A) The word 'Zayd' because it has a hand, foot, etc.
B) The word 'man' because it applies to many individuals.
C) The word 'hundred' because each unit is a part of the same name.
D) The word 'eye' (عین) because it has multiple meanings.

Key Takeaway
The three forms of wad' li kathir — by individuals, by particulars, and by parts — require precise conditions; especially, parts must be same in name for the third form.

Three Forms of Wad' for Kathir and the Definition of 'Amm
Analyzing wad' for multitude and its three types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three forms of wad' for kathir and apply the Hanafi definition of 'amm to classify words as general or not.

Core Idea
Wad' for multitude takes three forms: per individual, per common meaning, per aggregate; only the second yields 'amm.

This passage from a Hanafi usul text explains how words can be coined for a multitude in three distinct ways. Understanding these forms is crucial for correctly identifying whether a word is truly general ('amm) or falls under another category like homonyms or number nouns. We will walk through each form and then see how the definition of 'amm must include the condition of unrestricted comprehensiveness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three forms of wad' for kathir
List the three forms as described: wad' for each individual separately, wad' for a single meaning with particulars, and wad' for the aggregate as a whole.
These are foundational categories in Hanafi usul.
2
Map each form to its corresponding term category
First form yields mushtarak (homonyms), second yields 'amm (general), third yields number nouns.
This mapping is explicitly stated in the passage.
3
Analyze the definition of 'amm
Break down 'al-lafz al-mustaghriq li-ma yasluhu lahu min ghayr hasr': lafz (word), mustaghriq (comprehensive), ma yasluhu lahu (what it is suitable for), ghayr hasr (unrestricted).
Each component excludes certain word types.
4
Apply the condition of ghayr mahsur to exclude number nouns
Number nouns like 'hundred' specify a number, thus they have hasr. Plural forms like 'rijal' do not specify a count, so they qualify as 'amm.
The passage uses the example of 'heavens' being restricted but it is general.
5
Understand how istighraq is achieved via mutabaqa or tadammun
For plurals like 'rijal', indication is by mutabaqa (all individuals); for number nouns, indication is by tadammun (parts), but they are not 'amm because of the hasr condition.
This clarifies the coverage of the definition.

Source Text

فان قیل: یہ شرح کی عبارت کا چوتھا حصہ ہے غرض شارع سوال نقل کر کے اس کا جواب دینا ہے۔
سوال :۔ یہ ہے کہ وضع لکثیر کی تمیم کی وجہ سے زید عمر ورجل وغیرہ یہ وضع کثیر کے تحت داخل ہو جائیں گے کثرت بحسب الاجزاء کے پائے جانے کی وجہ سے یعنی ان میں بھی اجزاء کے اعتبار سے مجموع کے لئے وضع پائی جا رہی ہے تو ان کو عام ہوتا چاہیے حالانکہ یہ تو خاص ہیں؟
جواب : یہ ہے کہ وضع للکثیر میں کثرت بحسب الاجزاء سے مطلق اجزاء مراد نہیں بلکہ ایسے اجزاء مراد ہیں کہ جو متفق بحسب الاسم ہوں جیسے مائہ کے تحت سوا کا ئیاں داخل ہیں اور بحسب الاسم متفق ہیں بخلاف زید عمر د وغیرہ کے کہ ان میں ایسے اجزاء ہیں کہ ہر ایک کا الگ الگ نام ہے جیسے ید، رجل و غیر ذلک اور جب اجزاء متفق بحسب الاسم ہوں تو ان کی سرحد مل جاتی ہے جزئیات کے ساتھ یہ ایسے ہے جیسے انسان کا صدق زید عمرور جل وغیرہ سب پر ہوتا ہے ہر ایک کو کہتے ہیں کہ یہ انسان کی جزئی ہے اسی طرح مانیہ کی ہر ہرا کائی پر یہ بات صادق آتی ہے کہ یہ مائنہ کی اکائی ہے۔
فَإِنْ قِيلَ النَّكِرَةُ المَنْفِيَّةُ عَام وَلَمْ تُوضَعُ لِلْكَفَرَةِ قُلْنَا الْوَضْعُ أَعَمُّ مِنْ الشَّخْصِيّ ، وَالنَّوْعِيِّ ، وَقَدْ ثَبَتَ مِنْ اسْتِعْمَالِهِمْ لِلنَّكِرَةِ الْمَنْفِيَّةِ أنَّ الحُكْمَ مَنفِى عَن الكَثِيرِ الْغَيْرِ الْمَحْصُورٍ ، وَاللفظ مُسْتَغْرق لِكُلِّ فَرْدٍ فِي حُكْمِ النَّفَى بِمَعْنَى عُمُومِ النَّفَي عَن الْآحَادِ فِى الْمُفْرَدِ ، وَعَنْ الْمَجُمُوعِ فِى الْجَمْعِ لَا نَفْيَ الْعُمُومِ ، وَهَذَا مَعْنَى الْوَضْعِ النَّوَعِيِّ لِذَلِكَ ، وَكَوْنُ عُمُومِهَا عَقْلِيًّا ضَرُورِيًّا بِمَعْنَى أَنَّ انْتِفَاء فَرْدٍ مُبْهَم لَا يُمْكِنُ إِلَّا بِانْتِفَاء كُلَّ فَرْدٍ لَا يُنَافِي ذَلِكَ لَا يُقَالُ النَّكِرَةُ الْمَنْفِيَّةُ مَجَاز ، وَالتَّعْرِيفُ لِلْعَامِّ الْحَقِيقِيّ ؛ لِأَنَّا نَقُولُ لَا نُسَلِّمُ أَنَّهَا مَجَازٌ كَيْفَ وَلَمْ تُسْتَعْمَلُ إِلَّا فِيمَا وُضِعَتْ لَهُ بِالْوَضْعِ الشَّخْصِي وَهُوَ فَرْدٌ مُبْهَمْ ، وَقَدْ صَرَّحَ الْمُحَقِّقُونَ مِنْ شَارِحِى أُصُولِ ابْنِ الْحَاجِب بِأَنَّهَا حَقِيقَةٌ ، وَمَعْنَى كَوْنِ الْكَثِيرِ غَيْرُ مَخصُورٍ أَنْ لَا يَكُونَ فِي اللَّفْظِ دَلَالَةٌ عَلَى انْحِصَارِهِ فِي عَدَدٍ مُعَيَّنٍ وَإِلَّا فَالْكَثِيرُ المُتَحَقِّقُ مَحْصُورٌ لَا مَحَالَةَ لَا يُقَالُ الْمُرَادُ بِغَيْرِ الْمَحْصُورِ مَا لَا يَدْخُلُ تَحْتَ الضَّبْطِ وَالْعَدْ بِالنَّظَرِ إِلَيْهِ ؛ لأنَّا نَقُولُ فَحِينَئِذٍ يَكُونُ لَفْظُ السَّمَاوَاتِ مَوْضُوعًا لِكَثِيرِ مَحْصُورٍ وَلَفْظُ أَلْفِ مَوْضُوعًا لِكَثِيرٍ غَيْرِ مَحُصُورٍ وَالْأَمْرُ بِالْعَكْسِ ضَرُورَةَ أن الأوَّلَ عَامٌ ، وَالثَّانِيَ اسْمُ عَدَدٍ لَا يُقَالُ هَذَا الْقَيدُ مُسْتَدْرَكٌ ؛ لأنَّ الِاحْتِرَازَ عَنْ أَسْمَاء الْعَدَدِ حَاصِلٌ بِقَيْدِ الِاسْتِعْرَاقِ لِمَا يَصْلُحُ لَهُ ضَرُورَةٌ أَنَّ لَفَظَ الْمِائَةِ مَثلا إنَّمَا يَصْلُحُ لِجُزَنِيَّاتِ الْمِائَةِ لَا لِمَا يَتَضَمَّنُهَا الْمِائَةُ مِنَ الْآحَادِ ؛ لِأَنَّا نَقُولُ أَرَادَ بِالصُّلُوحٍ صُلُوحَ اسْمِ الْكُلّى لِجُزنِيَّاتِهِ أَوْ الكُلِّ لِأجْزَائِهِ فَاعْتَبَرَ الدَّلَالَةَ مُطَابِقَةٌ أَوْ تَضَمُّنَّا وَبِهَذَا الاعْتِبَارِ صَارَ صِيَعُ الْجُمُوع ، وَأَسْمَاؤُهَا ، مِثْلُ الرِّجَالِ وَالْمُسْلِمِينَ وَالرَّهْطِ وَالْقَوْمِ بِالنِّسْبَةِ إِلَى الْآحَادِ مُسْتَغْرِقَةٌ لِمَا تَصْلُحُ لَهُ فَدَخَلَتْ فِي الْحَدِّ ، وَقَوْلُهُ مُسْتَغْرِق مَرْفُوعٌ صِفَةً لَفْطٍ وَمَعْنَى اسْتِغْرَاقِهِ لِمَا يَصْلُحُ لَهُ تَنَاوُلُهُ لِذَلِكَ بِحَسَبِ الدَّلَالَةِ .
ترجمہ: پس اگر اعتراض کیا جائے کہ نکرہ منفیہ عام ہے اور نہیں وضع کیا گیا کثیر کے لیے ۔ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ وضع عام ہے شخصی سے اور نومی سے اور تحقیق ثابت ہے ان کے استعمال میں سے نکرہ منفیہ کے لیے کہ بے شک حکم منفی ہوتا ہے کثیر غیر محصور ہے اور لفظ مستغرق ہوتا ہے ہر فرد کو نفی کے حکم میں عموم نفی کے معنی میں مفرد میں ہر ہر فرد سے اور جمع میں مجموعہ سے نہ کی نفی عموم کے معنی میں اور یہی وضع نوعی کا معنی ہے اس کے لیے، اور ہونا اس کے عموم کا عقلی ضروری اس معنی میں ہے کہ بے شک فرد مہم کا انتظام نہیں۔
Answer: That wad' for multitude includes generalization. The first form is that it is placed for each individual of the individuals of the multitude. Second form: that the word is placed for one common meaning and the units of the multitude fall under that common meaning. Third form: that it is placed for the totality of the units of the multitude as a whole. If the first form, then every single unit is the object of placing. If the second, then the object of placing is the common meaning and the units of the multitude are particulars of that meaning. If the third, then the object of placing is the aggregate as a whole and the units are its parts. Now in the first form, the multitude is according to individuals; this occurs in common nouns (mushtarak). Second form: multitude according to particulars; occurs in general terms ('amm). Third form: multitude according to parts; occurs in number nouns. If it is said: ... Question: Because of the generalization in wad' lilkathir, words like Zayd, 'Amr, and rajul would fall under wad' lilkathir due to the existence of multitude according to parts, i.e., in them also there is placing for the aggregate in terms of parts, so they should be general, whereas they are specific? Answer: In wad' lilkathir, multitude according to parts does not mean absolute parts, but parts that are uniform in name, like the units of hundred (mi'a) are uniform in name, unlike Zayd and 'Amr where each part has a separate name. When parts are uniform in name, their boundary merges with particulars. This is like the application of 'insan' to all individuals. If it is said: The negated indefinite is general and it was not placed for multitude? We say: Wad' is more general than personal and generic. And it is established from their usage of the negated indefinite that the ruling is negated from an unrestricted multitude, and the lafz is comprehensive for every individual in the ruling of negation, meaning the generality of negation from individuals in the singular, and from the aggregate in the plural, not the negation of generality. This is the meaning of generic wad' for that. And that its generality is rational and necessary, meaning that the negation of an ambiguous individual is only possible by the negation of every individual, this does not contradict that it is not said that the negated indefinite is metaphorical and the definition is for real general; because we say we do not accept that it is metaphorical, how so, when it is only used in what it was placed for by personal wad', i.e., an ambiguous individual. And the verifiers among the commentators of Ibn al-Hajib's Usul have stated that it is real. And the meaning of the multitude being unrestricted is that there is no indication in the lafz of its limitation to a specific number. Otherwise, the actual multitude is necessarily restricted. It cannot be said that by 'unrestricted' is meant what cannot be grasped and counted by looking at it; because then the word 'heavens' would be placed for a restricted multitude and the word 'thousand' for an unrestricted multitude, while the opposite is the case. It cannot be said that this condition is redundant, because the exclusion of number nouns is achieved by the condition of istighraq (comprehensiveness) for what it is suitable for; necessarily, the word 'hundred' for example is only suitable for the particulars of a hundred, not for the individuals contained in the hundred. Because we say: He meant by 'suitable' the suitability of a universal noun for its particulars or of a whole for its parts, so he considered indication by mutabaqa or tadammun. By this consideration, plural forms and their names, like 'rijal', 'muslimin', 'raht', 'qawm' become comprehensive relative to individuals for what they are suitable for, so they enter the definition. And his statement 'mustaghriq' is nominative as an adjective of 'lafz', and the meaning of its comprehensiveness for what it is suitable for is its coverage of that according to indication. Urdu translation: So if an objection is made that the negated indefinite is general and was not placed for multitude, we say that wad' is more general than personal and generic. And it is established from their usage of the negated indefinite that the ruling is negated from unrestricted multitude, and the lafz is comprehensive for every individual in the ruling of negation, meaning generality of negation from each individual in the singular, and from the aggregate in the plural, not negation of generality. And this is the meaning of generic wad' for that. And its generality being rational and necessary means that the negation of an ambiguous individual is not possible except by negation of every individual. That does not contradict that the negated indefinite is metaphorical and the definition is for real general, because we say we do not accept that it is metaphorical. How so? It is only used for what it was placed for by personal wad' — an ambiguous individual. And the verifiers from the commentators of Ibn al-Hajib's principles have stated that it is real. And the meaning of the multitude being unrestricted is that there is no indication in the lafz of its limitation to a specific number. Otherwise the actual multitude is necessarily restricted. It cannot be said that by 'unrestricted' is meant what cannot be grasped and counted by looking at it, because then the word 'heavens' would be placed for a restricted multitude and the word 'thousand' for an unrestricted multitude, while the opposite is the case. It cannot be said that this condition is redundant because the exclusion of number nouns is achieved by the condition of comprehensiveness for what it is suitable for, necessarily for the word 'hundred' for example is only suitable for the particulars of a hundred, not for the individuals contained in the hundred. Because we say: He meant by 'suitable' the suitability of a universal noun for its particulars or of a whole for its parts, so he considered indication by correspondence or inclusion. By this consideration, plural forms and their names, like 'men', 'muslims', 'group', 'people' become comprehensive relative to individuals for what they are suitable for, so they enter the definition. And his statement 'mustaghriq' is nominative as an adjective of 'lafz', and the meaning of its comprehensiveness for what it is suitable for is its coverage of that according to indication.

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion on the types of wad' (coimage) for multitude (kathir) and its relationship to the definition of 'amm (general term). The author first explains three forms of wad' for kathir: (1) For each individual of the multitude separately (e.g., common nouns that are ambiguous? Actually he says this occurs in mushtarak, i.e., words with multiple meanings? Wait, 'mushtarak' is homonym, but here first form is wad' for each individual of the multitude? That seems confusing. Actually reading carefully: First form: wad' for each individual separately. He says this is found in mushtarak (common nouns? No, mushtarak is homonym, but perhaps he means common nouns like 'ayn? Actually the text says 'mushtarak' which usually means homonym, but here it might be a mistake or a different usage. Better to rely on the classification: second form is for a common meaning with particulars – that is 'amm. Third form is for the aggregate as a whole – that is number nouns. So the first form must be something else, perhaps proper names? Because the objection mentions that Zayd and 'Amr (proper names) would then be 'amm, but the answer says they are not because their parts have different names. So first form likely applies to proper names or specific individuals. But the author says first form is for each individual of the multitude – that seems to be for words that are coined for multiple specific individuals? Actually it's for each individual, like a common noun that applies to each? But he says it's found in mushtarak, which is a word with multiple distinct meanings. So perhaps the first form is for a word that is coined for multiple separate meanings (like 'ayn for eye, spring, etc.). Then the second form is coining for a single meaning that applies to many particulars (the general term). The third form is coining for a composite whole (like 'hundred' meaning the aggregate of units). Then the objection: proper names like Zayd and 'Amr and even 'rajul' (man) have parts? The objection suggests that if we consider the parts (like letters or components), they too have a kind of multitude, so they should be 'amm. The answer: the multitude in wad' lilkathir refers to parts that are uniform in name. In proper names and 'rajul', the parts (e.g., hand, foot) are not uniform in name; they are different. So they are not general. Then the discussion moves to the negated indefinite (nakira manfiyya). An opponent objects that the negated indefinite is 'amm, but it is not coined for multitude (since it is a single indefinite). The author responds by distinguishing wad' shakhsi (personal coinage) and wad' naw'i (generic coinage). The negated indefinite is coined by personal coinage for a single ambiguous individual, but by generic coinage, it is understood that negation applies to all individuals of that kind. So its 'umum (generality) is not from the lafz directly but from a rational necessity: you cannot negate an ambiguous individual without negating all individuals. Thus, it is haqiqa (real) in its usage, not majaz. The verifiers from among the commentators of Ibn al-Hajib's Usul confirm this. The author then clarifies the condition of 'ghayr mahsur' (unrestricted) in the definition of 'amm: it means the lafz does not indicate a specific number. So number nouns are excluded because they specify a number, but common plural forms like 'rijal' are general because they do not specify a count. The condition of istighraq (comprehensiveness) prevents number nouns because a number noun like 'hundred' is only suitable for its specific enumerated units, not for all individuals. The definition includes plural forms like 'rijal' and 'muslimun' because they are comprehensive for their individuals by way of mutabaqa (correspondence) or tadammun (inclusion).

Key Terms
الوضع (al-wad'): تخصيص اللفظ بالمعنى (coining a word for a meaning)
العام (al-'amm): اللفظ المستغرق لما يصلح له من غير حصر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT a form of wad' for kathir?
A) Wad' for each individual separately
B) Wad' for a single meaning with particulars
C) Wad' for an aggregate of parts uniform in name
D) Wad' for the entirety of a specific individual

Key Takeaway
The three forms of wad' for kathir help classify words as mushtarak, 'amm, or number nouns, with 'amm specifically the second form, defined by unrestricted comprehensiveness.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
10 min
The Negated Indefinite as 'Amm: Rational Generality vs. Metaphorical Speech
Analyzing wad' for multitude and its three types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school considers the negated indefinite (النكرة المنفية) as 'amm with haqiqa usage and evaluate the opposing view that it is majaz.

Core Idea
The negated indefinite is literal in its personal wad', but its generality is a rational necessity, not linguistic.

This lesson tackles a key usul dispute: is the negated indefinite (e.g., لا رجل) truly general ('amm) or metaphorical when used to mean 'no man at all'? The Hanafi position defends its haqiqa status by distinguishing personal wad' from generic wad' and arguing that the generality is a rational consequence. We will follow the argument, the rebuttal of the opposition, and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
State the objection
The opponent claims that the negated indefinite is 'amm but it was not coined for a multitude (since it is coined for a single ambiguous individual), so it should be considered majaz.
2
Distinguish personal wad' from generic wad'
Personal wad' coins the word for a specific instance; generic wad' captures the pattern of usage that the negation applies to all individuals.
The author says: الوضع أعم من الشخصي والنوعي.
3
Explain the rational necessity
Negating an ambiguous individual (نفي فرد مبهم) necessitates negating all individuals, because you cannot pinpoint which individual is negated without covering all.
This is 'aqlī ḍarūrī.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the claim of majaz
The word is used in its personal wad' meaning (an ambiguous individual), so it is haqiqa. The generality is not from the lafz but from reason, so it does not make the usage metaphorical.
The author cites muhaqqiqun from Ibn al-Hajib's commentators.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Under the opposing view, nakira manfiyya would not be included in the definition of 'amm; under Hanafi, it is included.
This affects how general verses are interpreted (e.g., لا إله إلا الله).

جواب:۔ یہ ہے کہ وضع للکثیر میں تعمیم ہے پہلی صورت یہ ہے کہ کثیر کے افراد میں سے ہر فرد کے لئے وضع ہو دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ لفظ ایک امریکی کے لئے وضع ہو اور کثیر کے وحد ان اس امرکی کے تحت داخل ہو جائیں تیسری صورت یہ ہے کہ کثیر کے وحدان کے مجموع من حیث المجموع کے لئے موضوع ہو اگر پہلی صورت ہو یعنی کثیر کے وحدان میں سے ہر ہر واحد کے لئے وضع ہو تو ہر ہر واحد موضوع لہ بنے گا اور اگر دوسری صورت ہو تو موضوع لہ امریکی ہو گا اور کثیر کے وحدان اس معنی موضوع لہ کی جزئیات ہوگی اور اگر تیسری صورت ہو تو معنی موضوع لہ مجموع من حیث المجموع ہوگا۔ اور کثیر کے وحدان موضوع لہ کے اجزاء ہوں گے اب پہلی صورت میں کثیر بحسب الافراد ہے یہ مشترک میں پائی جاتی ہے دوسری صورت میں کثیر بحسب الجزئیات ہے ۔ عام میں پائی جاتی ہے اور تیسری صورت میں کثرت بحسب الا جزاء ہے یہ اسماء عدد میں پائی جاتی ہے۔
فان قیل: یہ شرح کی عبارت کا چوتھا حصہ ہے غرض شارع سوال نقل کر کے اس کا جواب دینا ہے۔
سوال :۔ یہ ہے کہ وضع لکثیر کی تمیم کی وجہ سے زید عمر ورجل وغیرہ یہ وضع کثیر کے تحت داخل ہو جائیں گے کثرت بحسب الاجزاء کے پائے جانے کی وجہ سے یعنی ان میں بھی اجزاء کے اعتبار سے مجموع کے لئے وضع پائی جا رہی ہے تو ان کو عام ہوتا چاہیے حالانکہ یہ تو خاص ہیں؟
جواب : یہ ہے کہ وضع للکثیر میں کثرت بحسب الاجزاء سے مطلق اجزاء مراد نہیں بلکہ ایسے اجزاء مراد ہیں کہ جو متفق بحسب الاسم ہوں جیسے مائہ کے تحت سوا کا ئیاں داخل ہیں اور بحسب الاسم متفق ہیں بخلاف زید عمر د وغیرہ کے کہ ان میں ایسے اجزاء ہیں کہ ہر ایک کا الگ الگ نام ہے جیسے ید، رجل و غیر ذلک اور جب اجزاء متفق بحسب الاسم ہوں تو ان کی سرحد مل جاتی ہے جزئیات کے ساتھ یہ ایسے ہے جیسے انسان کا صدق زید عمرور جل وغیرہ سب پر ہوتا ہے ہر ایک کو کہتے ہیں کہ یہ انسان کی جزئی ہے اسی طرح مانیہ کی ہر ہرا کائی پر یہ بات صادق آتی ہے کہ یہ مائنہ کی اکائی ہے۔
فَإِنْ قِيلَ النَّكِرَةُ المَنْفِيَّةُ عَام وَلَمْ تُوضَعُ لِلْكَفَرَةِ قُلْنَا الْوَضْعُ أَعَمُّ مِنْ الشَّخْصِيّ ، وَالنَّوْعِيِّ ، وَقَدْ ثَبَتَ مِنْ اسْتِعْمَالِهِمْ لِلنَّكِرَةِ الْمَنْفِيَّةِ أنَّ الحُكْمَ مَنفِى عَن الكَثِيرِ الْغَيْرِ الْمَحْصُورٍ ، وَاللفظ مُسْتَغْرق لِكُلِّ فَرْدٍ فِي حُكْمِ النَّفَى بِمَعْنَى عُمُومِ النَّفَي عَن الْآحَادِ فِى الْمُفْرَدِ ، وَعَنْ الْمَجُمُوعِ فِى الْجَمْعِ لَا نَفْيَ الْعُمُومِ ، وَهَذَا مَعْنَى الْوَضْعِ النَّوَعِيِّ لِذَلِكَ ، وَكَوْنُ عُمُومِهَا عَقْلِيًّا ضَرُورِيًّا بِمَعْنَى أَنَّ انْتِفَاء فَرْدٍ مُبْهَم لَا يُمْكِنُ إِلَّا بِانْتِفَاء كُلَّ فَرْدٍ لَا يُنَافِي ذَلِكَ لَا يُقَالُ النَّكِرَةُ الْمَنْفِيَّةُ مَجَاز ، وَالتَّعْرِيفُ لِلْعَامِّ الْحَقِيقِيّ ؛ لِأَنَّا نَقُولُ لَا نُسَلِّمُ أَنَّهَا مَجَازٌ كَيْفَ وَلَمْ تُسْتَعْمَلُ إِلَّا فِيمَا وُضِعَتْ لَهُ بِالْوَضْعِ الشَّخْصِي وَهُوَ فَرْدٌ مُبْهَمْ ، وَقَدْ صَرَّحَ الْمُحَقِّقُونَ مِنْ شَارِحِى أُصُولِ ابْنِ الْحَاجِب بِأَنَّهَا حَقِيقَةٌ ، وَمَعْنَى كَوْنِ الْكَثِيرِ غَيْرُ مَخصُورٍ أَنْ لَا يَكُونَ فِي اللَّفْظِ دَلَالَةٌ عَلَى انْحِصَارِهِ فِي عَدَدٍ مُعَيَّنٍ وَإِلَّا فَالْكَثِيرُ المُتَحَقِّقُ مَحْصُورٌ لَا مَحَالَةَ لَا يُقَالُ الْمُرَادُ بِغَيْرِ الْمَحْصُورِ مَا لَا يَدْخُلُ تَحْتَ الضَّبْطِ وَالْعَدْ بِالنَّظَرِ إِلَيْهِ ؛ لأنَّا نَقُولُ فَحِينَئِذٍ يَكُونُ لَفْظُ السَّمَاوَاتِ مَوْضُوعًا لِكَثِيرِ مَحْصُورٍ وَلَفْظُ أَلْفِ مَوْضُوعًا لِكَثِيرٍ غَيْرِ مَحُصُورٍ وَالْأَمْرُ بِالْعَكْسِ ضَرُورَةَ أن الأوَّلَ عَامٌ ، وَالثَّانِيَ اسْمُ عَدَدٍ لَا يُقَالُ هَذَا الْقَيدُ مُسْتَدْرَكٌ ؛ لأنَّ الِاحْتِرَازَ عَنْ أَسْمَاء الْعَدَدِ حَاصِلٌ بِقَيْدِ الِاسْتِعْرَاقِ لِمَا يَصْلُحُ لَهُ ضَرُورَةٌ أَنَّ لَفَظَ الْمِائَةِ مَثلا إنَّمَا يَصْلُحُ لِجُزَنِيَّاتِ الْمِائَةِ لَا لِمَا يَتَضَمَّنُهَا الْمِائَةُ مِنَ الْآحَادِ ؛ لِأَنَّا نَقُولُ أَرَادَ بِالصُّلُوحٍ صُلُوحَ اسْمِ الْكُلّى لِجُزنِيَّاتِهِ أَوْ الكُلِّ لِأجْزَائِهِ فَاعْتَبَرَ الدَّلَالَةَ مُطَابِقَةٌ أَوْ تَضَمُّنَّا وَبِهَذَا الاعْتِبَارِ صَارَ صِيَعُ الْجُمُوع ، وَأَسْمَاؤُهَا ، مِثْلُ الرِّجَالِ وَالْمُسْلِمِينَ وَالرَّهْطِ وَالْقَوْمِ بِالنِّسْبَةِ إِلَى الْآحَادِ مُسْتَغْرِقَةٌ لِمَا تَصْلُحُ لَهُ فَدَخَلَتْ فِي الْحَدِّ ، وَقَوْلُهُ مُسْتَغْرِق مَرْفُوعٌ صِفَةً لَفْطٍ وَمَعْنَى اسْتِغْرَاقِهِ لِمَا يَصْلُحُ لَهُ تَنَاوُلُهُ لِذَلِكَ بِحَسَبِ الدَّلَالَةِ .
ترجمہ: پس اگر اعتراض کیا جائے کہ نکرہ منفیہ عام ہے اور نہیں وضع کیا گیا کثیر کے لیے ۔ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ وضع عام ہے شخصی سے اور نومی سے اور تحقیق ثابت ہے ان کے استعمال میں سے نکرہ منفیہ کے لیے کہ بے شک حکم منفی ہوتا ہے کثیر غیر محصور ہے اور لفظ مستغرق ہوتا ہے ہر فرد کو نفی کے حکم میں عموم نفی کے معنی میں مفرد میں ہر ہر فرد سے اور جمع میں مجموعہ سے نہ کی نفی عموم کے معنی میں اور یہی وضع نوعی کا معنی ہے اس کے لیے، اور ہونا اس کے عموم کا عقلی ضروری اس معنی میں ہے کہ بے شک فرد مہم کا انتظام نہیں۔
Answer: That wad' for multitude includes generalization. The first form is that it is placed for each individual of the individuals of the multitude. Second form: that the word is placed for one common meaning and the units of the multitude fall under that common meaning. Third form: that it is placed for the totality of the units of the multitude as a whole. If the first form, then every single unit is the object of placing. If the second, then the object of placing is the common meaning and the units of the multitude are particulars of that meaning. If the third, then the object of placing is the aggregate as a whole and the units are its parts. Now in the first form, the multitude is according to individuals; this occurs in common nouns (mushtarak). Second form: multitude according to particulars; occurs in general terms ('amm). Third form: multitude according to parts; occurs in number nouns. If it is said: ... Question: Because of the generalization in wad' lilkathir, words like Zayd, 'Amr, and rajul would fall under wad' lilkathir due to the existence of multitude according to parts, i.e., in them also there is placing for the aggregate in terms of parts, so they should be general, whereas they are specific? Answer: In wad' lilkathir, multitude according to parts does not mean absolute parts, but parts that are uniform in name, like the units of hundred (mi'a) are uniform in name, unlike Zayd and 'Amr where each part has a separate name. When parts are uniform in name, their boundary merges with particulars. This is like the application of 'insan' to all individuals. If it is said: The negated indefinite is general and it was not placed for multitude? We say: Wad' is more general than personal and generic. And it is established from their usage of the negated indefinite that the ruling is negated from an unrestricted multitude, and the lafz is comprehensive for every individual in the ruling of negation, meaning the generality of negation from individuals in the singular, and from the aggregate in the plural, not the negation of generality. This is the meaning of generic wad' for that. And that its generality is rational and necessary, meaning that the negation of an ambiguous individual is only possible by the negation of every individual, this does not contradict that it is not said that the negated indefinite is metaphorical and the definition is for real general; because we say we do not accept that it is metaphorical, how so, when it is only used in what it was placed for by personal wad', i.e., an ambiguous individual. And the verifiers among the commentators of Ibn al-Hajib's Usul have stated that it is real. And the meaning of the multitude being unrestricted is that there is no indication in the lafz of its limitation to a specific number. Otherwise, the actual multitude is necessarily restricted. It cannot be said that by 'unrestricted' is meant what cannot be grasped and counted by looking at it; because then the word 'heavens' would be placed for a restricted multitude and the word 'thousand' for an unrestricted multitude, while the opposite is the case. It cannot be said that this condition is redundant, because the exclusion of number nouns is achieved by the condition of istighraq (comprehensiveness) for what it is suitable for; necessarily, the word 'hundred' for example is only suitable for the particulars of a hundred, not for the individuals contained in the hundred. Because we say: He meant by 'suitable' the suitability of a universal noun for its particulars or of a whole for its parts, so he considered indication by mutabaqa or tadammun. By this consideration, plural forms and their names, like 'rijal', 'muslimin', 'raht', 'qawm' become comprehensive relative to individuals for what they are suitable for, so they enter the definition. And his statement 'mustaghriq' is nominative as an adjective of 'lafz', and the meaning of its comprehensiveness for what it is suitable for is its coverage of that according to indication. Urdu translation: So if an objection is made that the negated indefinite is general and was not placed for multitude, we say that wad' is more general than personal and generic. And it is established from their usage of the negated indefinite that the ruling is negated from unrestricted multitude, and the lafz is comprehensive for every individual in the ruling of negation, meaning generality of negation from each individual in the singular, and from the aggregate in the plural, not negation of generality. And this is the meaning of generic wad' for that. And its generality being rational and necessary means that the negation of an ambiguous individual is not possible except by negation of every individual. That does not contradict that the negated indefinite is metaphorical and the definition is for real general, because we say we do not accept that it is metaphorical. How so? It is only used for what it was placed for by personal wad' — an ambiguous individual. And the verifiers from the commentators of Ibn al-Hajib's principles have stated that it is real. And the meaning of the multitude being unrestricted is that there is no indication in the lafz of its limitation to a specific number. Otherwise the actual multitude is necessarily restricted. It cannot be said that by 'unrestricted' is meant what cannot be grasped and counted by looking at it, because then the word 'heavens' would be placed for a restricted multitude and the word 'thousand' for an unrestricted multitude, while the opposite is the case. It cannot be said that this condition is redundant because the exclusion of number nouns is achieved by the condition of comprehensiveness for what it is suitable for, necessarily for the word 'hundred' for example is only suitable for the particulars of a hundred, not for the individuals contained in the hundred. Because we say: He meant by 'suitable' the suitability of a universal noun for its particulars or of a whole for its parts, so he considered indication by correspondence or inclusion. By this consideration, plural forms and their names, like 'men', 'muslims', 'group', 'people' become comprehensive relative to individuals for what they are suitable for, so they enter the definition. And his statement 'mustaghriq' is nominative as an adjective of 'lafz', and the meaning of its comprehensiveness for what it is suitable for is its coverage of that according to indication.

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion on the types of wad' (coimage) for multitude (kathir) and its relationship to the definition of 'amm (general term). The author first explains three forms of wad' for kathir: (1) For each individual of the multitude separately (e.g., common nouns that are ambiguous? Actually he says this occurs in mushtarak, i.e., words with multiple meanings? Wait, 'mushtarak' is homonym, but here first form is wad' for each individual of the multitude? That seems confusing. Actually reading carefully: First form: wad' for each individual separately. He says this is found in mushtarak (common nouns? No, mushtarak is homonym, but perhaps he means common nouns like 'ayn? Actually the text says 'mushtarak' which usually means homonym, but here it might be a mistake or a different usage. Better to rely on the classification: second form is for a common meaning with particulars – that is 'amm. Third form is for the aggregate as a whole – that is number nouns. So the first form must be something else, perhaps proper names? Because the objection mentions that Zayd and 'Amr (proper names) would then be 'amm, but the answer says they are not because their parts have different names. So first form likely applies to proper names or specific individuals. But the author says first form is for each individual of the multitude – that seems to be for words that are coined for multiple specific individuals? Actually it's for each individual, like a common noun that applies to each? But he says it's found in mushtarak, which is a word with multiple distinct meanings. So perhaps the first form is for a word that is coined for multiple separate meanings (like 'ayn for eye, spring, etc.). Then the second form is coining for a single meaning that applies to many particulars (the general term). The third form is coining for a composite whole (like 'hundred' meaning the aggregate of units). Then the objection: proper names like Zayd and 'Amr and even 'rajul' (man) have parts? The objection suggests that if we consider the parts (like letters or components), they too have a kind of multitude, so they should be 'amm. The answer: the multitude in wad' lilkathir refers to parts that are uniform in name. In proper names and 'rajul', the parts (e.g., hand, foot) are not uniform in name; they are different. So they are not general. Then the discussion moves to the negated indefinite (nakira manfiyya). An opponent objects that the negated indefinite is 'amm, but it is not coined for multitude (since it is a single indefinite). The author responds by distinguishing wad' shakhsi (personal coinage) and wad' naw'i (generic coinage). The negated indefinite is coined by personal coinage for a single ambiguous individual, but by generic coinage, it is understood that negation applies to all individuals of that kind. So its 'umum (generality) is not from the lafz directly but from a rational necessity: you cannot negate an ambiguous individual without negating all individuals. Thus, it is haqiqa (real) in its usage, not majaz. The verifiers from among the commentators of Ibn al-Hajib's Usul confirm this. The author then clarifies the condition of 'ghayr mahsur' (unrestricted) in the definition of 'amm: it means the lafz does not indicate a specific number. So number nouns are excluded because they specify a number, but common plural forms like 'rijal' are general because they do not specify a count. The condition of istighraq (comprehensiveness) prevents number nouns because a number noun like 'hundred' is only suitable for its specific enumerated units, not for all individuals. The definition includes plural forms like 'rijal' and 'muslimun' because they are comprehensive for their individuals by way of mutabaqa (correspondence) or tadammun (inclusion).

Key Terms
النكرة المنفية (al-nakira al-manfiyya): الاسم النكرة في سياق النفي (e.g., لا رجل)
العام (al-'amm): اللفظ المستغرق لما يصلح له من غير حصر
الوضع (al-wad'): تخصيص اللفظ بالمعنى (coining a word for a meaning)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in the passage, why is the negated indefinite considered literal (haqiqa) rather than metaphorical (majaz)?
A) Because it is coined for multitude by generic wad'.
B) Because it is used in its personal wad' meaning (an ambiguous individual) and the generality is a rational necessity.
C) Because early scholars unanimously declared it literal.
D) Because it contains a linguistic marker for generality.

Key Takeaway
The negated indefinite is 'amm and haqiqa; the rationality of its generality does not make it metaphorical, but rather demonstrates the depth of Hanafi usul analysis.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
12 min
The Negated Indefinite: Literal Generality through Generic Designation
Analyzing whether النكرة المنفية is real generality

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school considers the negated indefinite (النكرة المنفية) to be literally general (عام حقيقي) by distinguishing between personal and generic designation.

Core Idea
The negated indefinite is literally general because of generic designation (وضع نوعي), not just rational implication.

In Hanafi usul, one of the key debates is whether the negated indefinite (النكرة المنفية), such as 'ما جاءني رجل' (no man came to me), qualifies as a general term (عام). Some scholars argue its generality is merely metaphorical or rational, not literal. The Hanafi position, however, insists it is literally general. This lesson unpacks the reasoning, focusing on the crucial distinction between personal and generic designation, and shows how the Hanafi school defends the literal generality of the negated indefinite.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of 'general' (العام)
The Hanafi definition: a word designated for a comprehensive multitude (موضوع للكثير مستغرق لما يصح له). Understand what 'designation' (وضع) means and the requirement of comprehensiveness.
Definition is key to the dispute.
2
State the objection against the negated indefinite
The objector argues the negated indefinite is only designated for a vague individual (فرد مهم), not multitude, so it does not fit the definition. This is the core challenge.
The objection assumes only personal designation matters.
3
Explain the Hanafi response: two types of designation
Personal designation (وضع شخصي) assigns a specific word to a specific meaning. Generic designation (وضع نوعي) is a rule or pattern established by customary usage. The negated indefinite has personal designation for a vague individual, but generic designation for multitude because Arabs consistently use it to negate every individual.
This is the innovative solution.
4
Analyze counter-arguments and Hanafi rebuttals
Opponents may claim the generality is metaphorical or merely rational. The Hanafi response: it is literal because generic designation is a real linguistic convention, and rational necessity does not negate conventional reality.
Both are reconciled.
5
Confirm the Hanafi position with authority
The commentators of Ibn al-Hajib (e.g., in Mukhtasar al-Usul) affirm that the generality of the negated indefinite is real (حقيقة), not metaphorical. This gives authoritative weight to the Hanafi view.
Tarjih is supported by later scholarship.

Source Text

ہے ممکن مگر ہر فرد کے انتفاء کے ساتھ نہیں ہے منافی اس کے ۔ نہ اعتراض کیا جائے کہ نکرہ منفیہ مجاز ہے۔ اور تعریف عام حقیقی کی ہے کیونکہ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ ہم تسلیم نہیں کرتے کہ بے شک وہ مجاز ہے۔ کیسے ہو سکتا ہے؟ حالانکہ نہیں استعمال کیا جاتا مگر اسی معنی میں جس کے لیے وضع کیا گیا ہے وضع شخصی کے ساتھ اور وہ فرد مہم ہے اور تحقیق تصریح کی ہے محققین نے اصول بن حاجب کے شارحین میں سے کہ وہ بے شک حقیقی ہے اور معنی کثیر کے غیر محصور ہونے کا یہ مفہوم ہے کہ نہ ہو لفظ میں دلالت اس کے منحصر ہونے پر عدد معین میں سے وگر نہ تو کثیر جو تحقق ہوں محصور ہوتے ہیں لا محالہ نہ کہا جائے کہ مراد غیر محصور سے وہ ہیں کہ جو نہ داخل ہوں ضبط اور شمار کے تحت نظر کرتے ہوئے اس کی طرف کیونکہ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ پس اس وقت ہو گا لفظ سموات موضوع کثیر محصور کے لیے اور لفظ الف موضوع کثیر غیر محصور کے لیے حالانکہ معاملہ اس کے برعکس ہے بوجہ بدیہی ہونے اس بات کے کہ بے شک اول عام ہے اور ثانی اسم عدد ہے۔ نہ کہا جائے کہ یہ قید بیکار ہے کیونکہ اسماء عدد سے احتر از حاصل ہے استغراق لما تصلح لہ کی قید سے بوجہ ضروری ہونے اس بات کے کہ بے شک لفظ ملکہ مثال کے طور پر جز این نیست کہ صلاحیت رکھتا ہے ملکہ کی تمام جزئیات کے لیے نہ اس کے لیے جس کو شامل ہے۔ ملکہ افراد میں سے کیونکہ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ مراد صلاحیت سے اسم کلی کی صلاحیت ہے اپنی جزئیات کے لیے یا کل کی صلاحیت ہے اپنے اجزاء کے لیے پس اعتبار کیا ہے دلالت کا مطابقی ہو یا تضمنی اور اس اعتبار سے ہو گئے صیغے جمع کے اور اسماء جمع کے مثل رجال اور مسلمین اور ربط اور قوم کے نسبت کرتے ہوئے افراد کی طرف مستغرق ما تصلح لہ کو پس داخل ہو گئے تعریف میں ، اس کا قول مستغرق مرفوع ہے صفت ہے لفظ کی اور معنی اس کے ماتصلح لہ کو مستغرق ہونے کا اس کا شامل ہوتا ہے اس کو دلالت کے اعتبار سے۔ تشریح : فان قبیل النكرة :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا پانچواں حصہ ہے یہاں سے شاریع سوال نقل کر کے قلنا سے جواب دے رہے ہیں، سوال :۔ یہ ہے کہ نکرہ منفیہ الفاظ عام میں سے ہے اور عام کے تحت داخل ہے لیکن اس پر عام کی تعریف صادق نہیں آتی کیونکہ نکرہ منفیہ موضوع الکثیر نہیں ہے جبکہ عام موضوع الکثیر ہوتا ہے نکرہ منفیہ میں وضع للکثیر اس لئے نہیں پائی جاتی کہ نکرہ منفیہ فرد مہم کی نفی کے لئے موضوع ہے کثیرین کی نفی کے لئے موضوع نہیں ہے لیکن اس کے باوجود یہ عام کے افراد میں سے ہے۔ جواب:۔ کون کہتا ہے کہ نکرہ منفیہ کثیر کے لئے موضوع نہیں ہے بلکہ یہ کثیر کے لئے موضوع ہے باقی رہا کہ اس میں وضع للکثیر کیسے ہے؟ اس لئے کہ وضع کی دو قسمیں ہیں وضع نوعی اور وضع شخصی۔ وضع شخصی: کہتے ہیں کہ مخصوص لفظ کو مخصوص معنی کے لئے وضع کر دیا جائے مثلا کر منفی و وضع کیا گیا ہے فر مجسم کی نفی کے لئے وضع نوعی :۔ کہتے ہیں قاعدہ کو مثلا کل فاعل مرفوع کہا جائے گا کہ اس میں وضع نوعی ہے تو نکرہ مصفیہ اگر چہ وضع شخصی کے اعتبار سے موضوع للکثیر نہیں ہے لیکن وضع نوعی کے اعتبار سے موضوع للکثیر ہے کیونکہ یہ قاعدہ معلوم ہوا ہے کہ فصحاء عرب جب بھی نکرہ منفیہ کو استعمال کرتے ہیں تو وہاں پر حکم کی ہر فرد سے نفی ہوتی ہے اور لفظ ہر ہر فرد سے حکم کی نفی کو شامل ہوتا ہے پس یہ استعمال بمنزل اس قاعدہ کے ہے کہ ہر نکرہ منفیہ نفی کے حکم میں تمام آحاد کو متفرق ہو گا جب وہ نکرہ مفرد ہو اور اگر جمع ہو تو نفی کے حکم میں مجموع کو مستغرق ہو گا یعنی ان دونوں صورتوں میں (نکرہ مفرد ہو یا جمع ہو ) عموم نفی کے لئے ہوگا نفی عموم کے لئے نہیں ہوگا۔ اور یہی مفید ہوتا ہے کثیر کے لئے اور عام کی تعریف میں جو موضوع الکثیر ہے اس میں تعمیم ہے عام ازیں وضع شخصی ہو یا وضع نوعی ہو لہذ انکرہ منفیہ عام کے تحت داخل ہے اس پر ۔ وکون عمومہا:۔ یہاں سے شاریخ نے ایک سوال مقدر کا جواب دیا ہے۔ سوال:۔ ہوتا ہے کہ نکرہ منفیہ کا عموم کے لئے مفید ہونا یہ وضع نوعی کے اعتبار سے نہیں ہے بلکہ یہ تو عقل کا مقتضی ہے اس لئے کہ تکرہ منفیہ موضوع ے فرد مہم کی نفی کے لئے اور فرد ہم سے حکم کی نفی نہیں ہوسکتی جب تک کہ ہر ہر فرد سے کم کی نفی نہیں ہو جاتی پس فرد مبہم سے حکم کی نفی ملزوم اور ہر ہر جز سے نفی کرنا اس کو لا زم ہے۔ جواب:۔ یہ ہے عموم عقلی ہو اور وضع نوعی بھی ہو یہ دونوں باتیں جمع ہوسکتی ہیں کیونکہ دونوں میں کوئی تضاد نہیں ۔ لا یقال : یہ شرح کی عبارت کا چھٹا حصہ ہے یہاں سے شاریخ سوال نقل کر کے جواب دے رہے ہیں۔ سوال :۔ یہ ہے کہ نکرہ منفیہ کا عموم کے لئے مفید ہوتا یہ مجاز ہے اور فرد مہم کے لئے مفید ہونا یہ حقیقت ہے اور تعریف میں تو وہ عام مراد ہے جس کا عموم حقیقی ہو اب اگر نکرہ منفیہ پر تعریف صادق نہیں آتی تو یہ باعث اشکال نہیں ہے۔ جواب:۔ ہم تسلیم نہیں کرتے کہ نکرہ منفیہ کا عموم کے لئے مفید ہونا مجازی ہے بلکہ نکرہ منفیہ موضوع ہے فرد مہم کی نفی کے لئے وضع شخصی کے اعتبار سے اور اس کے ثمرات اور فوائد میں سے یہ ہے کہ اس سے ہر ہر فرد کی نفی ہو گئی یعنی اس نے عموم نفی کا فائدہ دید یا وضع نوعی کے اعتبار سے لہذا اس کا استعمال عموم کے لئے بھی حقیقت ہو گا اس وجہ سے علامہ ابن حاجب کی کتاب مختصر الاصول کے شراح نے تصریح کی ہے کہ نکرہ منفیہ کا عموم مجازی نہیں بلکہ حقیقی ہے یعنی اس کو استعمال کیا گیا ہے موضوع لہ بوضع شخصی میں پھر وضع نوعی کے اعتبار سے اس نے عموم کا بھی فائدہ دے دیا۔ و معنی کون الکثیر :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا ساتواں حصہ ہے فرض دفع دخل مقدر ہے۔
It is possible but not with the negation of every individual, not contradictory to it. Let it not be objected that the negated indefinite is metaphorical, and the definition of general is real, because we say: we do not concede that it is metaphorical. How can it be? While it is not used except in the same meaning for which it was designated, with personal designation, and that is the vague individual. And the investigators among the commentators of Usul Ibn al-Hajib have declared that it is indeed real. And the meaning of 'multitude being unrestricted' is that the word does not indicate its restriction to a specific number; otherwise, a multitude that exists is necessarily restricted. Let it not be said that by 'unrestricted' is meant that which does not enter under control and enumeration, looking at it, because we say: then the word 'heavens' would be designated for a restricted multitude, and the word 'a thousand' for an unrestricted multitude, while the opposite is true due to the obviousness that the first is general and the second is a number word. Let it not be said that this qualification is useless, because there is avoidance of number words by the qualification of 'comprehensive for what it is fit for' due to the necessity that the word 'property', for example, is not capable for all particulars of property, nor for what includes individuals of property. Because we say: what is meant by capability is the capability of a universal term for its particulars, or a whole for its parts. Then consideration is given to indication whether by correspondence or inclusion, and on that basis plural forms and collective nouns like 'men', 'Muslims', 'the covenant', and 'people' are directed towards individuals comprehensively for what they are fit for, so they enter the definition. His saying 'comprehensive' is nominative, an adjective of the word, and its meaning is that it encompasses what it is fit for by way of indication. Elaboration: 'So it is of the type of the indefinite': This is the fifth part of the commentary's expression. From here, the commentator transmits a question and answers with 'qulna'. Question: The negated indefinite is among general words and enters under 'general', but the definition of 'general' does not apply to it because the negated indefinite is not designated for multitude, while the general is designated for multitude. In the negated indefinite, designation for multitude is not found because the negated indefinite is designated for negating a vague individual, not for negating multiple things. Yet despite that, it is among the individuals of 'general'. Answer: Who says that the negated indefinite is not designated for multitude? Rather, it is designated for multitude. As for how it has designation for multitude, there are two types of designation: generic designation and personal designation. Personal designation: a specific word is placed for a specific meaning, e.g., 'from the negative' is designated for negating a corporeal individual. Generic designation: a rule is set, e.g., 'every doer is nominative' is said to have generic designation. So the negated indefinite, although in terms of personal designation it is not designated for multitude, in terms of generic designation it is designated for multitude, because it is known as a rule that whenever the eloquent Arabs use a negated indefinite, the negation of the ruling applies to every individual, and the word encompasses the negation of the ruling from every individual. So this usage is like the rule that every negated indefinite, in the ruling of negation, encompasses all individuals distributively when it is a singular indefinite, and when it is plural, it encompasses the whole collectively in the ruling of negation. That is, in both cases (whether singular indefinite or plural), it is for the generality of negation, not the negation of generality. And this benefits multitude. And in the definition of 'general' which is 'designated for multitude', there is generality, whether the designation is personal or generic. Hence, the negated indefinite falls under 'general'. And the fact that its generality: From here, the commentator answers a presumed question. Question: That the negated indefinite benefits generality is not due to generic designation, but rather it is a requirement of reason, because the negated indefinite is designated for negating a vague individual, and negation of the ruling from a vague individual cannot occur unless the negation of the ruling from every individual occurs. So negation from a vague individual is the necessary condition, and negating from every individual is its necessary consequence. Answer: This is rational generality and there is also generic designation; both can coexist because there is no contradiction between them. 'It cannot be said': This is the sixth part of the commentary's expression. From here, the commentator transmits a question and answers. Question: That the negated indefinite benefits generality is metaphorical, and its benefiting the vague individual is literal, and in the definition, what is meant by 'general' is that whose generality is real. Now if the definition does not apply to the negated indefinite, then this is not problematic. Answer: We do not concede that the negated indefinite's benefiting generality is metaphorical. Rather, the negated indefinite is designated for negating a vague individual by personal designation, and among its fruits and benefits is that it results in negation from every individual, i.e., it gives the benefit of generality of negation by generic designation. Therefore, its use for generality is also literal. For this reason, the commentators of Ibn al-Hajib's book 'Mukhtasar al-Usul' have stated that the generality of the negated indefinite is not metaphorical but real, meaning it is used in what it is designated for by personal designation, then by generic designation it also gives the benefit of generality. 'And the meaning of the fact that the multitude...': This is the seventh part of the commentary's expression, a presumed prevention of an objection.
Source pages p. 509

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul dispute concerning whether the negated indefinite (النكرة المنفية) qualifies as ‘general’ (عام) under the Hanafi definition. The definition of ‘general’ is ‘a word designated for a number of things comprehensively’ (موضوع للكثير مستغرق لما يصح له). The objector argues that the negated indefinite cannot be general because it is designated only for negating a vague individual (فرد مهم), not for a multitude. The author (the commentator) responds by introducing the distinction between two types of designation (وضع): personal designation (وضع شخصي) and generic designation (وضع نوعي). Personal designation assigns a specific word to a specific meaning; generic designation assigns a rule or pattern to a class of usages. The negated indefinite, by personal designation, is for a vague individual, but by generic designation—because the Arabs consistently use it to negate every individual—it is effectively designated for multitude. The commentator further rebuts the claim that this generality is merely rational (عقلي) rather than conventional (وضعي), stating that both can coexist. He also rejects the assertion that the generality of the negated indefinite is metaphorical (مجاز), citing the consensus of commentators on Ibn al-Hajib's Mukhtasar al-Usul that it is literal (حقيقة). The passage highlights a key Hanafi usul principle: a word can have multiple layers of designation, and the negated indefinite’s generality is real, not figurative, thus it falls under the definition of ‘general’. The discussion proceeds in a question-and-answer format typical of a sharh, addressing the fifth, sixth, and seventh sections of the original matn.

Key Terms
النكرة المنفية (an-nakira al-manfiyya): An indefinite noun preceded by a negation particle, e.g., 'ما جاءني رجل' (no man came to me).
الوضع الشخصي (al-wad‘ ash-shakhsī): The act of assigning a specific word to a specific meaning for the first time.
الوضع النوعي (al-wad‘ an-naw‘ī): A general rule or pattern established by customary usage, such as 'every fa'il is marfu‘' or the consistent use of the negated indefinite to negate every individual.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what type of designation (وضع) makes the negated indefinite (النكرة المنفية) literally general?
A) Personal designation (وضع شخصي) only
B) Generic designation (وضع نوعي) only
C) Both personal and generic designation
D) Neither; it is metaphorical

Key Takeaway
The negated indefinite is literally general in Hanafi usul due to generic designation (وضع نوعي), not merely rational implication.
