Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
6 min
Indefinite Negative as General via Type-Based Coinage
Proving that indefinite negative is general through type-based coinage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafi usul considers al-nakirah al-manfiyyah as 'amm (general) through wad' naw'i, and defend this position against the objection that it is metaphorical.

Core Idea
Indefinite negation is general due to type-based coinage (wad' naw'i) – not mere metaphor.

This lesson explores a key Hanafi usul principle: an indefinite noun in a negative context (e.g., 'no man') conveys generality, meaning it negates the ruling from every individual of that type. The author argues that this generality is not metaphorical but real, based on the consistent usage pattern of the Arabs, which establishes a type-based coinage. We will examine the linguistic reasoning and the Hanafi response to counterarguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core terms
Understand the difference between wad' shakhsi (individual coinage) and wad' naw'i (type-based coinage). The former gives a word its primary meaning; the latter derives a systematic meaning from usage patterns.
Example: 'rajul' individually means 'a man' (vague); but in negation, usage shows it means 'any man'.
2
State the Hanafi claim
The claim: al-nakirah al-manfiyyah is 'amm (general) through wad' naw'i. Even though its individual coinage is for a vague individual, the Arab practice of using it to negate every individual creates a secondary real meaning.
This is why 'No man came' means no man at all, not just a specific man.
3
Analyze the objections
The text presents two objections: (1) that the generality is merely rational, not linguistic; (2) that it is metaphorical (majaz) because the primary meaning is specific. Understand each objection's logic.
Objection 1: Reason dictates that to negate a vague individual, you must negate all its instances. Objection 2: The word was coined for a specific individual, so using it for all individuals is a transfer.
4
Follow the Hanafi responses
First, rational generality and type-based coinage can coexist—there is no contradiction. Second, the usage is real (haqiqah) because wad' naw'i operates alongside wad' shakhsi, as affirmed by commentators of Mukhtasar al-Usul.
The key evidence is the consistent Arab pattern; this is not a one-off metaphorical extension.
5
Apply the principle
Now you can identify any indefinite negative in the Quran or Hadith and interpret it as general (amm) using this Hanafi tool.
Example: 'لا ريب فيه' (no doubt in it) covers all types of doubt.

وضع نوعی :۔ کہتے ہیں قاعدہ کو مثلا کل فاعل مرفوع کہا جائے گا کہ اس میں وضع نوعی ہے تو نکرہ مصفیہ اگر چہ وضع شخصی کے اعتبار سے موضوع للکثیر نہیں ہے لیکن وضع نوعی کے اعتبار سے موضوع للکثیر ہے کیونکہ یہ قاعدہ معلوم ہوا ہے کہ فصحاء عرب جب بھی نکرہ منفیہ کو استعمال کرتے ہیں تو وہاں پر حکم کی ہر فرد سے نفی ہوتی ہے اور لفظ ہر ہر فرد سے حکم کی نفی کو شامل ہوتا ہے پس یہ استعمال بمنزل اس قاعدہ کے ہے کہ ہر نکرہ منفیہ نفی کے حکم میں تمام آحاد کو متفرق ہو گا جب وہ نکرہ مفرد ہو اور اگر جمع ہو تو نفی کے حکم میں مجموع کو مستغرق ہو گا یعنی ان دونوں صورتوں میں (نکرہ مفرد ہو یا جمع ہو ) عموم نفی کے لئے ہوگا نفی عموم کے لئے نہیں ہوگا۔ اور یہی مفید ہوتا ہے کثیر کے لئے اور عام کی تعریف میں جو موضوع الکثیر ہے اس میں تعمیم ہے عام ازیں وضع شخصی ہو یا وضع نوعی ہو لہذا نکرہ منفیہ عام کے تحت داخل ہے اس پر ۔

وکون عمومہا:۔ یہاں سے شاریخ نے ایک سوال مقدر کا جواب دیا ہے۔ سوال:۔ ہوتا ہے کہ نکرہ منفیہ کا عموم کے لئے مفید ہونا یہ وضع نوعی کے اعتبار سے نہیں ہے بلکہ یہ تو عقل کا مقتضی ہے اس لئے کہ نکرہ منفیہ موضوع ہے فرد مبہم کی نفی کے لئے اور فرد مبہم سے حکم کی نفی نہیں ہوسکتی جب تک کہ ہر ہر فرد سے حکم کی نفی نہیں ہو جاتی پس فرد مبہم سے حکم کی نفی ملزوم اور ہر ہر جز سے نفی کرنا اس کو لازم ہے۔
جواب:۔ یہ ہے عموم عقلی ہو اور وضع نوعی بھی ہو یہ دونوں باتیں جمع ہوسکتی ہیں کیونکہ دونوں میں کوئی تضاد نہیں ۔

لا یقال : یہ شرح کی عبارت کا چھٹا حصہ ہے یہاں سے شاریخ سوال نقل کر کے جواب دے رہے ہیں۔ سوال :۔ یہ ہے کہ نکرہ منفیہ کا عموم کے لئے مفید ہوتا یہ مجاز ہے اور فرد مبہم کے لئے مفید ہونا یہ حقیقت ہے اور تعریف میں تو وہ عام مراد ہے جس کا عموم حقیقی ہو اب اگر نکرہ منفیہ پر تعریف صادق نہیں آتی تو یہ باعث اشکال نہیں ہے۔
جواب:۔ ہم تسلیم نہیں کرتے کہ نکرہ منفیہ کا عموم کے لئے مفید ہونا مجازی ہے بلکہ نکرہ منفیہ موضوع ہے فرد مبہم کی نفی کے لئے وضع شخصی کے اعتبار سے اور اس کے ثمرات اور فوائد میں سے یہ ہے کہ اس سے ہر ہر فرد کی نفی ہو گئی یعنی اس نے عموم نفی کا فائدہ دید یا وضع نوعی کے اعتبار سے لہذا اس کا استعمال عموم کے لئے بھی حقیقت ہو گا اس وجہ سے علامہ ابن حاجب کی کتاب مختصر الاصول کے شراح نے تصریح کی ہے کہ نکرہ منفیہ کا عموم مجازی نہیں بلکہ حقیقی ہے یعنی اس کو استعمال کیا گیا ہے موضوع لہ بوضع شخصی میں پھر وضع نوعی کے اعتبار سے اس نے عموم کا بھی فائدہ دے دیا۔
Type-based coinage: They say the rule, for example, 'every doer is nominative' is said, and in it there is type-based coinage. So the indefinite [noun] in a negative context, even if according to individual coinage it is not coined for the many, but according to type-based coinage it is coined for the many, because this rule is known: whenever the eloquent Arabs use an indefinite in a negative context, there the negation of the ruling applies to every individual, and the word includes the negation of the ruling from every individual. So this usage is like the rule that every indefinite in a negative context will distribute over all individuals in the case of the negative ruling when it is a singular indefinite, and if it is plural, it will encompass the whole in the case of the negative ruling. That is, in both cases (whether the indefinite is singular or plural) it will be for the generality of negation, not for the negation of generality. And this conveys the meaning of multitude, and in the definition of 'general' (al-amm) which is coined for the many, there is generalization; whether it is individual coinage or type-based coinage, therefore the indefinite in a negative context falls under 'general' (al-amm). So upon this. 

And its being general: From here the commentator has answered a presupposed question. Question: The benefit of the indefinite negative for generality is not due to type-based coinage, but rather it is a requirement of reason, because the indefinite negative is coined for the negation of a vague individual, and the negation of the ruling from a vague individual cannot occur unless the negation of the ruling from every individual occurs. So the negation of the ruling from a vague individual is the necessary condition, and negating from every individual is its necessary concomitant. 
Answer: This is that it is both rational generality and type-based coinage; these two things can combine because there is no contradiction between them. 

It is not said: This is the sixth part of the commentary. Here the commentator transmits a question and gives an answer. Question: The benefit of the indefinite negative for generality is metaphorical (majaz), and its benefit for a vague individual is real (haqiqah), and in the definition, 'general' is meant as that whose generality is real. Now if the indefinite negative does not apply to the definition, then this is not problematic. 
Answer: We do not accept that the benefit of the indefinite negative for generality is metaphorical. Rather, the indefinite negative is coined for the negation of a vague individual from the perspective of individual coinage, and among its results and benefits is that from it the negation of every individual occurred, meaning it gave the benefit of the generality of negation, whether from the perspective of type-based coinage. Therefore, its usage for generality is also real. For this reason, the commentators of Ibn al-Hajib's Mukhtasar al-Usul have explicitly stated that the generality of the indefinite negative is not metaphorical but real, i.e., it is used for what it is coined for in individual coinage, then from the perspective of type-based coinage it also gives the benefit of generality.
Source pages p. 510

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the definition of 'amm (general), specifically addressing the status of al-nakirah al-manfiyyah (the indefinite in a negative context). The author explains that although an indefinite word individually (wad' shakhsi) is coined for a single vague individual, it acquires generality through type-based coinage (wad' naw'i) because the usage pattern of the Arabs shows that when they use an indefinite in a negative context, the negation applies to every individual of that kind. For example, 'I did not see a man' implies no man at all. This is a rule of language. The commentator then answers two objections: first, that this generality is merely rational and not linguistic; he says both can coexist. Second, that such generality is metaphorical; he refutes this by citing the commentators of Ibn al-Hajib who affirm it is real (haqiqah) due to type-based coinage.

Key Terms
نکرہ منفیہ (al-nakirah al-manfiyyah): An indefinite noun (like 'a man') used in a negative context (such as 'there is no man').
وضع نوعی (wad' naw'i): Type-based coinage: the linguistic principle that a word is considered to have a systematic meaning based on the pattern of its usage in the language, as opposed to its individual coinage.
وضع شخصی (wad' shakhsi): Individual coinage: the original meaning of a word as coined for a specific concept or individual instance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why does an indefinite noun in a negative context (nakirah manfiyyah) convey generality?
A) Because of its individual coinage (wad' shakhsi).
B) Because of its type-based coinage (wad' naw'i) based on Arab usage.
C) Because of a rational necessity that has no linguistic basis.
D) Because it is always metaphorical.

Key Takeaway
The indefinite negative (nakirah manfiyyah) is considered general (amm) in Hanafi usul through type-based coinage (wad' naw'i), not metaphor, because Arab usage consistently applies negation to every individual.

Meaning of Kathir Ghayr Mahsur in Amm Definition
Correcting the definition of 'uncountable multitude' in the definition of 'amm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct meaning of 'kathir ghayr mahsur' and apply it to distinguish general words from number nouns in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Ghayr mahsur means the word itself does not specify a number, not infinite or uncountable.

This lesson tackles a common confusion in Hanafi usul: what exactly does 'uncountable' mean in the definition of 'amm? The text clarifies that it is a linguistic condition, not a mathematical one. We will examine why two popular interpretations fail and why the third is correct, using concrete examples.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term under scrutiny
Locate the phrase 'kathir ghayr mahsur' in the definition of 'amm. Understand that it is a condition (shart) for a word to be considered general.
2
Recall the three proposed meanings
List the three interpretations given: (1) infinite, (2) not falling under counting/enumeration, (3) not indicating a specific number by its linguistic form.
3
Analyze the rejection of the first meaning
Understand why 'infinite' is wrong: the definition would never apply to any actual word, making it useless.
Infinite multitudes do not exist; thus 'amm would have no instances.
4
Analyze the rejection of the second meaning
Understand why 'not falling under counting' fails: it would exclude genuinely general words like 'samawat' (heavens) which are countable, and include number words like 'alf' (thousand) which are not typically counted, thereby violating comprehensiveness and exclusivity.
This meaning makes the definition not jami' mani'.
5
Accept the correct meaning
Affirm the third interpretation: the word itself must not indicate restriction to a particular number. Apply to examples: 'rijal' is general, 'asharah' is not.
This meaning preserves both jami' and mani'.

و معنى كون الكثير :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا ساتواں حصہ ہے فرض دفع دخل مقدر ہے۔

سوال: یہ ہے کہ بظاہر غیر محصور کا معنی ہے غیر متناہی اور اس کا تعدد ہی محال ہے کیونکہ اس کا تو وجود ہی نہیں ہے؟
جواب:۔ یہ ہے کہ غیر محصور کا معنی غیر متناہی نہیں ہے بلکہ اس کا معنی ہے لفظوں کے اعتبار سے کثیر کے عدد معین کے اندر بند ہونے پر دلالت نہ ہو اس کی مثال مطابقی جیسے رجال کا لفظ ہے اس کی عدد معین پر بند ہونے پر دلالت نہیں ہے اور مثال احترازی جیسے عشرہ کا لفظ ہے یہ ہے کثیر پر لیکن ایسے کثیر پر دال ہے جو لفظوں کے اعتبار سے بند ہیں عدد معین پر ۔ بعض حضرات نے کثیر غیر محصور کا معنی یہ کیا ہے کہ جو ضبط و شمار کے تحت داخل نہ ہو ۔ شارخ فرماتے ہیں کہ کثیر غیر محصور کا یہ معنی غلط ہے کیونکہ اس صورت میں تعریف جامع مانع نہیں رہے گی کہ جو لفظ عام ہے وہ عام نہیں رہے گا اور جو خاص ہیں وہ عام بن جائیں گے مثلا سماوات کا لفظ یہ تحت الشمار داخل ہونے کی وجہ سے خاص کے تحت داخل ہو جائے گا حالانکہ یہ عام ہے نیز الف یہ عربوں کے اعتبار سے داخل تحت الشمار نہیں ہے تو پھر یہ عام ہونا چاہیے حالانکہ یہ خاص ہے اور اسم عدد ہے۔ خلاصہ: یہ نکلا کہ غیر محصور کے تین معنی ہیں (۱) غیر محصور کہتے ہیں کہ جو غیر متناہی ہو یہ معنی غلط ہے کیونکہ اس صورت میں عام کی تعریف عام کے کسی فرد پر بھی صادق نہیں آئے گی (۲) غیر محصور کہتے ہیں جو شمار اور ضبط کے تحت داخل نہ ہو یہ بھی غلط ہے کیونکہ اس صورت میں تعریف جامع مانع نہیں رہے گی (۳) غیر محصور کہتے ہیں کہ لفظوں کے اعتبار سے کثیر کے عدد معین میں بند ہونے پر دلالت نہ ہو یہ معنی صحیح ہے اور یہاں یہی معنی مراد ہے۔
And the meaning of 'the multitude': This is the seventh part of the commentary; it is an assumption to repel a presupposed objection.

Question: Apparently, 'uncounted' (ghayr mahsur) means infinite, and its multitude is impossible because it has no existence?
Answer: That is not the meaning of ghayr mahsur as infinite; rather its meaning is that from the perspective of words, it does not indicate that the multitude is restricted to a specific number. Its example of compatibility is like the word 'men' (rijal) which does not indicate restriction to a specific number. And its example of exclusivity is like the word 'ten' ('asharah) which indicates a multitude, but indicates a multitude that is, from the perspective of words, restricted to a specific number. Some people have interpreted 'kathir ghayr mahsur' as that which does not come under counting and enumeration. The commentator says that this meaning of ghayr mahsur is wrong because in that case the definition would not be comprehensive and exclusive: a general word would not remain general, and specific words would become general. For example, the word 'heavens' (samawat) because it falls under enumeration, it would fall under specific, whereas it is general. Also 'alf' (thousand) is not under enumeration according to the Arabs, so it should be general, whereas it is specific and a number word. Summary: It turns out that ghayr mahsur has three meanings: (1) They say ghayr mahsur is that which is infinite = this meaning is wrong, because then the definition of 'amm would not apply to any instance of it. (2) They say ghayr mahsur is that which does not fall under counting and enumeration = this is also wrong, because in that case the definition would not be comprehensive and exclusive. (3) They say ghayr mahsur is that which, from the perspective of words, does not indicate that the multitude is restricted to a specific number = this meaning is correct, and this is the intended meaning here.
Source pages p. 511

Commentary
This passage is a commentary that clarifies the term 'kathir ghayr mahsur' (uncountable multitude) as a condition in the definition of 'amm (the general). Two incorrect meanings are refuted: first, that it means infinite (which would make the definition impossible to apply), and second, that it means not falling under counting (which would exclude actual general words like 'heavens' that are countable, and include number words like 'thousand' that are not counted). The correct meaning is that the word itself, by its linguistic form, does not specify a particular number; e.g., 'men' can mean any number, while 'ten' specifies exactly ten. This is a crucial precision in Hanafi usul to distinguish general words from number nouns.

Key Terms
كثير غير محصور (kathīr ghayr maḥṣūr): A multitude that is not limited to a specific number, in the sense that the word itself does not indicate a particular numeral.
غير محصور (ghayr maḥṣūr): Literally 'uncounted'; technically meaning the word does not specify a number.
تعریف جامع مانع (ta'rīf jāmi' māni'): A definition that includes all members of a category (comprehensive) and excludes all non-members (exclusive).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is the correct meaning of 'kathir ghayr mahsur' in the definition of 'amm?
A) It means infinite in quantity.
B) It means not falling under counting and enumeration.
C) It means the word does not indicate restriction to a specific number.
D) It means the word applies to all individuals without exception.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, 'kathir ghayr mahsur' is a linguistic condition: the word must not specify a number, not a comment on its countability in reality.

Redundancy of 'Kathir Ghayr Mahsur' Condition in 'amm Definition
Refutation of redundancy claim in the definition of 'amm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the objection that the condition 'kathir ghayr mahsur' is redundant in the Hanafi definition of 'amm and explain how the Hanafi school defends its necessity.

Core Idea
Number words lack universal istighraq, so the added condition prevents ambiguity in the definition of 'amm.

Definitions in usul al-fiqh are precise. The Hanafi definition of 'amm includes the condition 'kathir ghayr mahsur' (uncountable multitude) to exclude number words. Some scholars object that this condition is redundant because the requirement of istighraq (comprehensive coverage) already excludes number words. This passage introduces that objection and begins the Hanafi response, though the text is incomplete. Understanding this debate sharpens your ability to distinguish true general words from limited ones.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition element under debate
The Hanafi definition of 'amm includes both 'istighraq' (comprehensive coverage) and 'kathir ghayr mahsur' (uncountable multitude). The objector challenges the latter as redundant.
The condition 'kathir ghayr mahsur' means the individuals covered are not limited to a specific countable number.
2
Understand the objector's argument
The objector claims that number words (e.g., 'mi'ah', 'hundred') are already excluded by the condition of istighraq, because they lack the universal-type coverage that istighraq requires. Therefore, adding 'kathir ghayr mahsur' is superfluous.
Number words encompass a fixed quantity, not all possible individuals in an unrestricted manner.
3
Analyse the concept of istighraq in 'amm
Istighraq in 'amm means the word must encompass all individuals it can apply to, in the same way a universal covers its particulars. Number words do not have that capacity; for example, 'hundred' does not apply to each unit as 'hundred'.
The passage uses the example of 'mi'ah' to illustrate: it includes many ones but not in a universal sense.
4
Trace the beginning of the Hanafi response
The commentator responds by asserting that the istighraq condition is itself general and must be specified. The response is incomplete, but it likely argues that without the extra condition, the broad wording of 'istighraq' might be misinterpreted to include number words.
The text cuts off at 'اپنی' (its own), so the full response is not available.
5
Appreciate the practical impact
If the condition were redundant, definitions of 'amm would be simpler, but Hanafi usul maintains it for precision. This affects how general Quranic verses and hadiths are interpreted, ensuring that only truly general words are treated as 'amm.
For example, 'اقتلوا المشركين' (kill the polytheists) is 'amm because it meets all conditions, including uncountable multitude.

لا یقال :۔ سے سوال نقل کر کے جواب دے رہیں۔ سوال: یہ ہے کہ عام کی تعریف میں کثیر غیر محصور کی قید لگانا لغو ہے کیونکہ اس سے مقصود اس اسماء عدد کو خارج کرتا ہے اور وہ 'مستغرق لجميع ما يصلح لہ' کی قید سے خارج ہو جاتے ہیں باقی رہا کہ کیسے خارج ہوتے ہیں؟ تو اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ عام کی تعریف میں جو استغراق کی قید ہے اس سے مراد یہ ہے کہ عام اپنے تمام افراد پر مشتمل ہونے کی ایسی صلاحیت رکھتا ہو جس طرح کلی اپنی جزئیات پر مشتمل ہونے کی صلاحیت رکھتی ہے اور اسماء اعداد اپنے افراد کو متفرق ہونے کی صلاحیت تو رکھتے ہیں لیکن ایسی صلاحیت نہیں ہوتی جس طرح کلی کو اپنی جزئیات کے استغراق کی صلاحیت ہوتی ہے مثال کے طور پر مالیہ کا لفظ یہ سینکڑوں کے افراد کو شامل ہوگا لیکن جن اجزاء کو مائیہ متضمن ہے ان کو مستغرق نہیں ہے کہ ہر ایک کو یہ نہیں کہ سکتے کہ مائہ ہے لہذا اس میں استغراق نہ پایا گیا فلہذا عام سے خارج ہو گیا لہذا اکثیر کو غیر محصور کی قید کے ساتھ مقید کرنا لغو اور مستدرک ہے۔ جواب :۔ عام کی تعریف میں جو استغراق ہے اس میں تعمیم ہے عام ہے کہ وہ ایسا استغراق ہو جیسا کلی کا استغراق اپنی
It is not said: From here the question is transmitted and answered. Question: The inclusion of the condition 'kathir ghayr mahsur' in the definition of 'amm is redundant because the intended purpose is to exclude number words, and they are excluded by the condition 'mustaghriq li-jami' ma yasluhu lahu' (encompassing all that it is suitable for). The remaining point is how are they excluded? The reason is that in the definition of 'amm, the condition of istighraq (comprehensive inclusion) means that the general word has the capacity to encompass all its individuals just as a universal has the capacity to encompass its particulars. Number words do have the capacity to cover their individuals, but they do not have that capacity in the same way a universal has the capacity for istighraq of its particulars. For example, the word 'one hundred' (mi'ah) includes hundreds of individuals, but it does not encompass the parts that 'one hundred' includes, because one cannot say of each of them that it is 'one hundred'. Therefore, istighraq is not found in it, so it is excluded from 'amm. Hence, restricting 'kathir' with 'ghayr mahsur' is redundant and superfluous. 
Answer: In the definition of 'amm, the istighraq that is mentioned is general, meaning it is that istighraq which is like the universal's istighraq of its...
Source pages p. 511

Commentary
This passage is a commentary that addresses an objection to the definition of 'amm: that the condition 'kathir ghayr mahsur' is redundant because the condition of istighraq (comprehensive coverage) already excludes number nouns like 'ten' and 'hundred'. The objector argues that istighraq requires the word to cover all its individuals in the way a universal covers its particulars. Number words do not have that kind of coverage; for example, 'hundred' does not apply to each of its units. So they are already excluded. Why add the condition about uncountable multitude? The commentator begins to respond by asserting that the istighraq in the definition is general, meaning it is analogous to a universal's coverage. However, the response is incomplete at the end of the page. The full argument would likely show that istighraq alone is ambiguous; hence the additional condition is necessary to clarify.

Key Terms
استغراق (istighrāq): The comprehensive coverage of all individuals that a word can apply to, similar to how a universal concept covers its particulars.
اسماء اعداد (asmā' al-a'dād): Number nouns like 'ten', 'hundred', 'thousand' that specify a precise quantity.
لغو (laghw): Redundant, superfluous; said of a condition that does not add any exclusion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is necessary because it excludes number words.
B) It is redundant because number words are already excluded by the condition of istighraq.
C) It is incorrect because number words should be included as 'amm.
D) It is too vague and needs further explanation.

Key Takeaway
The condition 'kathir ghayr mahsur' in the definition of 'amm is not redundant; it ensures that number words are not mistakenly considered 'amm despite lacking true comprehensive coverage.

Three Meanings of Ghayr Mahsur: Defining 'Amm in Hanafi Usul
Defining and critiquing the three possible meanings of 'ghayr mahsur'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the correct definition of 'ghayr mahsur' and distinguish it from two incorrect interpretations, explaining why they fail the jami' mani' criteria.

Core Idea
Ghayr mahsur means the word's form does not confine plurality to a specific number; it does not mean infinite or uncountable.

In Hanafi usul, the definition of 'amm (general term) hinges on the concept of 'ghayr mahsur' (unconfined). This lesson dissects three possible interpretations, showing why only one is sound. You will learn to avoid common errors that would either exclude legitimate general words or include specific numerical nouns.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three proposed meanings
List the three meanings of 'ghayr mahsur' presented: (1) infinite, (2) not coming under enumeration, (3) the word's form not confining to a specific number.
These are the three interpretations discussed in the passage.
2
Analyze the first meaning (infinite)
Understand why 'infinite' is rejected: an infinite set does not exist in reality, so the definition of 'amm would never apply to any actual word.
The passage states 'its existence is impossible'.
3
Analyze the second meaning (not under enumeration)
Examine why this meaning fails jami' mani': general words like 'samawat' (heavens) are countable and would be excluded, while specific words like 'alf' (thousand) are not easily counted and would be included.
Jami' means comprehensive (includes all 'amm), mani' means exclusive (excludes all khass).
4
Understand the correct meaning
The correct definition: the word itself does not indicate confinement to a specific number. Example: 'rijal' can refer to any number of men.
This meaning is both comprehensive and exclusive.
5
Apply the correct definition to test words
Practice classifying words as 'amm or khass using the correct definition of ghayr mahsur. For each word, ask: Does its form specify a number?
Use examples from the passage: 'samawat' is 'amm, 'ashara' is khass.

سوال: یہ ہے کہ بظاہر غیر محصور کا معنی ہے غیر متناہی اور اس کا تعدد ہی محال ہے کیونکہ اس کا تو وجود ہی نہیں ہے؟ جواب:۔ یہ ہے کہ غیر محصور کا معنی غیر متناہی نہیں ہے بلکہ اس کا معنی ہے لفظوں کے اعتبار سے کثیر کے عدد معین کے اندر بند ہونے پر دلالت نہ ہو اس کی مثال مطابقی جیسے رجال کا لفظ ہے اس کی عدد معین پر بند ہونے پر دلالت نہیں ہے اور مثال احترازی جیسے عشرہ کا لفظ ہے یہ وال ہے کثیر پر لیکن ایسے کثیر پر دال ہے جو لفظوں کے اعتبار سے بند ہیں عدد معین پر ۔ بعض حضرات نے کثیر غیر محصور کا معنی یہ کیا ہے کہ جو ضبط و شمار کے تحت داخل نہ ہو ۔ شارخ فرماتے ہیں کہ کثیر غیر محصور کا یہ معنی غلط ہے کیونکہ اس صورت میں تعریف جامع مانع نہیں رہے گی کہ جو لفظ عام ہے وہ عام نہیں رہے گا اور جو خاص ہیں وہ عام بن جائیں گے مثلا سماوات کا لفظ یہ تحت الشمار داخل ہونے کی وجہ سے خاص کے تحت داخل ہو جائے گا حالانکہ یہ عام ہے نیز الف الف یہ عربوں کے اعتبار سے داخل تحت الشمار نہیں ہے تو پھر یہ عام ہونا چاہیے حالانکہ یہ خاص ہے اور اسم عدد ہے۔ خلاصہ: یہ نکلا کہ غیر محصور کے تین معنی ہیں (۱) غیر محصور کہتے ہیں کہ جو غیر متناہی ہو یہ معنی غلط ہے کیونکہ اس صورت میں عام کی تعریف عام کے کسی فرد پر بھی صادق نہیں آئے گی (۲) غیر محصور کہتے ہیں جو شمار اور ضبط کے تحت داخل نہ ہو یہ بھی غلط ہے کیونکہ اس صورت میں تعریف جامع مانع نہیں رہے گی (۳) غیر محصور کہتے ہیں کہ لفظوں کے اعتبار سے کثیر کے عدد معین میں بند ہونے پر دلالت نہ ہو یہ معنی صحیح ہے اور یہاں یہی معنی مراد ہے۔
Question: That is, apparently 'ghayr mahsur' means infinite, and its multiplicity is impossible because it does not exist? Answer: The meaning of 'ghayr mahsur' is not infinite, but rather it means that the word does not indicate that the numerous (kathir) is confined within a specific number, in terms of (the word's) form. An example of equivalence (mutabaqi) is the word 'rijal' - it does not indicate confinement to a specific number. An example of exclusivity (ihtirazi) is the word 'ashara' - it indicates a large number (kathir), but a large number that is confined to a specific number in terms of its form. Some respected scholars have given the meaning of 'kathir ghayr mahsur' as that which does not come under enumeration and counting (dabt wa shumar). The commentator says that this meaning of 'kathir ghayr mahsur' is incorrect, because in that case the definition would not be comprehensive and exclusive (jami' mani'): a word that is general ('amm) would cease to be general, and words that are specific (khass) would become general. For example, the word 'samawat' (heavens) would fall under specific because it comes under enumeration, whereas it is general. Also 'alf' (thousand) in the usage of the Arabs does not come under enumeration, so it would have to be general, whereas it is specific and a numerical noun. Summary: It emerges that 'ghayr mahsur' has three meanings: (1) 'ghayr mahsur' means infinite - this meaning is wrong because the definition of 'amm would not apply to any instance of 'amm. (2) 'ghayr mahsur' means that which does not come under enumeration and counting - this is also wrong because the definition would not be comprehensive and exclusive. (3) 'ghayr mahsur' means that the word does not indicate confinement to a specific number in terms of its form - this meaning is correct and it is the intended meaning here.
Source pages p. 511

Commentary
This passage is a definitional analysis of the term 'ghayr mahsur' (unconfined) as used in the definition of 'amm (general term). The commentator presents three possible interpretations. First, some might think ghayr mahsur means infinite (ghayr mutanahi), but this is impossible because an infinite number does not exist and thus the definition would not apply to any actual general word. Second, some defined it as 'not coming under enumeration or counting,' but this fails the criteria of jami' mani': the word 'samawat' is countable but is general, while 'alf' is not easily countable but is specific. The third and correct meaning is that ghayr mahsur refers to the word's form not indicating confinement to a specific number. The word 'rijal' is a good example: it can refer to any number of men. The commentator follows the author's order, first stating the question, then giving the correct answer, then refuting the alternative, and finally summarizing the three positions.

Key Terms
غير محصور (ghayr mahsur): A term indicating that the word, in its form, does not confine the plurality (kathir) to a specific number.
كثير (kathir): A multiplicity of individuals, but not necessarily infinite; it is part of the definition of 'amm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the second meaning of 'ghayr mahsur' (that which does not come under enumeration) rejected?
A) Because it would make the definition exclusive and not comprehensive.
B) Because it would make the word 'samawat' (heavens) specific, whereas it is general, and the word 'alf' (thousand) general, whereas it is specific.
C) Because enumeration is impossible in Arabic.
D) Because it contradicts the consensus of scholars.

Key Takeaway
The correct definition of ghayr mahsur is crucial: it is not about infinite or uncountable, but about the word's form not confining plurality to a specific number.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

The Indefinite Plural: 'Amm or Intermediary?
Dispute on indefinite plural status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two competing Hanafi views on the status of an indefinite plural (jamm' munkar) and apply the muhaqqiq's condition of istighraq to classify a given plural as 'amm or wasita.

Core Idea
An indefinite plural is 'amm only if comprehensive; otherwise it is an intermediary.

This passage from a Hanafi usul commentary explores a critical point of disagreement: is an indefinite plural (jamm' munkar, e.g., 'rijalan') automatically general ('amm), or does its status depend on whether it includes all individuals (istighraq)? The author, following the muhaqqiqin, introduces a novel category—wasita (intermediary)—for non-comprehensive plurals, thereby refining the concept of 'amm itself.

Guided Path
1
Understand 'istighraq'
Grasp the meaning of istighraq: a term is comprehensive when it includes every individual it can possibly refer to. For example, 'every man' is comprehensive, but 'some men' is not.
The author defines istighraq as inclusion of all individuals the word is capable of including.
2
Identify the two positions
Fakhr al-Islam and some mashayikh hold that any plural with a common attribute is 'amm, regardless of istighraq. The author (muhaqqiq) requires istighraq for 'amm.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.
3
Recognize the consequence
When istighraq is absent, the indefinite plural becomes an intermediary (wasita) between 'amm and khass, according to the muhaqqiq.
Wasita is a distinct category in Hanafi usul, not recognized by Mutakallimin.
4
Apply to examples
Consider 'رأيت اليوم رجالاً' (I saw men today). The context 'today' indicates it does not cover all men; thus, it is not comprehensive and is wasita. In contrast, 'كل رجال' (every man) would be 'amm.
The passage uses these exact examples.
5
Extend the principle
The author notes that any general term restricted by context becomes an intermediary, not just indefinite plurals. This broadens the scope of wasita.
This is a refinement of the concept of 'amm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And his statement 'mustaghriq': This concerns the vowel marking; it should not be read as an adjective of 'kathir' (thus in the genitive), but rather as an adjective of 'lafz' (word) in the nominative. The meaning of 'istighraq' is that the word includes all individuals that it is capable of including, in terms of language. His statement 'otherwise it is an indefinite plural (jamm' munkar)': The valid principle regarding 'amm according to Fakhr al-Islam and some of the mashayikh is that it includes a collection of named entities (musammayat) with respect to a common attribute, regardless of whether istighraq exists or not. Thus, the indefinite plural is 'amm according to them, whether it is comprehensive or not. And the author, since he stipulated istighraq as per the choice of the verifiers (muhaqqiqin), the indefinite plural becomes an intermediary (wasita) between 'amm and khass according to those who say it does not have istighraq, and 'amm according to those who say it does have istighraq. On this basis, the intended meaning of 'jamm' munkar' in his statement 'otherwise it is an indefinite plural' is the plural that a context (qarina) indicates the lack of its comprehensiveness, like 'I saw men today' and 'In the house there are men.' However, this is not specific to the indefinite plural; rather, every general term that is restricted to a part by evidence of reason or otherwise necessarily becomes an intermediary, whether it is an indefinite plural or the like, according to the author's wording due to its inclusion in his statement 'and if it is not comprehensive then it is an indefinite plural and the like.' Its corruption is evident. His statement 'or with respect to the type (naw'), like 'rajul' and 'faras': This indicates that 'naw'' in the custom of the Law (urf al-shar') may be a logical type like 'faras' (horse) and may not be like 'rajul' (man), for the Law has...
Source pages p. 512

Commentary
This passage contains two sub-discussions. First, the author explains the correct reading of 'mustaghriq' as an adjective of 'lafz' (word) not of 'kathir', and defines istighraq. Then, a major discussion on the status of the indefinite plural (jamm' munkar, e.g., 'rijalan') as general ('amm) or intermediary. According to Fakhr al-Islam and some mashayikh, any plural that signifies a collection of named entities sharing a common attribute is 'amm, regardless of whether it includes all individuals (istighraq) or not. Thus, an indefinite plural is always 'amm in their view. However, the author (the muhaqqiq) stipulates istighraq as a condition for 'amm. Therefore, an indefinite plural that is not comprehensive becomes an intermediary between 'amm and khass. This aligns with those who deny its istighraq, but if it is comprehensive, it is 'amm. The author gives examples: 'I saw men today' or 'In the house there are men' are likely not comprehensive (limited by context). The point is that any general term restricted by evidence becomes an intermediary, not just indefinite plurals. The second part discusses the term 'naw'' (type) in 'urf al-shar', noting that sometimes it is a logical type (like 'faras') and sometimes not (like 'rajul'). The passage emphasizes that the definition of 'naw'' varies between logic and legal usage.

Key Terms
الجمع المنكر (al-jamm' al-munkar): An indefinite plural, e.g., 'rijalan' (men). Its status as 'amm or intermediary depends on whether it has istighraq (comprehensive inclusion) or not, according to the author's view.
واسطة (wasita): An intermediary category between 'amm (general) and khass (specific). An indefinite plural without istighraq is considered wasita.
استغراق (istighraq): Comprehensive inclusion: a term includes all individuals it can possibly refer to.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) When it includes a collection of named entities sharing a common attribute.
B) When it is comprehensive (mustaghriq).
C) When a context indicates that it is not comprehensive.
D) Never; it is always 'amm.

Key Takeaway
An indefinite plural's classification as 'amm or wasita depends on whether it is comprehensive (istighraq) or not, according to the Hanafi muhaqqiqin's refinement of 'amm.

Types of Istighraq and the Hanafi Definition of 'Amm
Defines istighraq types and establishes condition for 'amm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish istighraq mutabiqi from istighraq tadammuni and state the Hanafi condition that 'amm requires istighraq.

Core Idea
A general term is 'amm only if it is mustaghriq; istighraq is either by correspondence or by inclusion.

In this passage, the commentator explains the concept of istighraq and its two types: mutabiqi (correspondence) and tadammuni (inclusion). Understanding these types is essential for recognizing when a term qualifies as 'amm in Hanafi usul. The author, following the muhaqqiqun, insists that a word must be mustaghriq to be considered 'amm, a view that distinguishes the Hanafi approach from others.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of istighraq
Read the opening lines and note the distinction between istighraq mutabiqi (comprehensiveness of the universal for its particulars) and istighraq tadammuni (comprehensiveness of the whole for its parts).
Number words exhibit both types.
2
Understand the grammatical point
The passage clarifies that 'mustaghriq' is read in the nominative as an adjective of the word, not in the genitive describing 'kathir'. This affects the meaning.
Technical detail important for accurate textual understanding.
3
Define istighraq
From the text, extract the definition: istighraq is that a word includes all individuals it is capable of including linguistically.
Core Hanafi usul concept.
4
Derive the Hanafi condition for 'amm
The author states that in defining 'amm, istighraq is required. Thus, a term is 'amm only if it is mustaghriq.
This contrasts with the view of Fakhr al-Islam, who considers indefinite plural as 'amm even without istighraq.

جزئیات کے لئے ہوتا ہے یا ایسا استغراق ہو جیسا کل کا استغراق ہے اپنے اجزاء کے لئے اگر استغراق الکلی للجزئیات ہو تو اس کو استغراق مطابقی سے تعبیر کرتے ہیں اور اگر استغراق الکل ملا جزاء ہو تو اس کو استغراق تضمنی سے تعبیر کرتے ہیں اب ہم یہ کہتے ہیں کہ اسماء عدد میں استغراق مطابقی بھی پایا جاتا ہے استغراق الکلی للجرئیات کے اعتبار سے اور استغراق تضمنی بھی پایا جاتا ہے استغراق الکل للا جزاء کے اعتبار سے پس مالکہ میں جو استغراق ہے یہ استغراق مطابقی ہے باعتبار استغراق الکلی للجرئیات کے اور استغراقی تنظمی بھی ہے استغراق الکل لولا جزاء کے اعتبار سے لبند الفظ مایہ سینکڑوں پر بھی صادق آتا ہے استغراق مطابقی کے اعتبار سے اور ہر ہرا کائی پر بھی صادق آتا ہے استغراق ضمنی کے اعتبار سے لہذا اسماء عدد میں استغراق پایا گیا تو یہ متفرق کی قید سے خارج نہ ہوئے تو لا محالہ ان کو خارج کرنے کے لئے غیر محصور کی قید لگائیں گے۔
و قولہ مستغرق : سے ضبط اعراب کا بیان ہے کہ اس کو کثیر کی صفت بنا کر مجرور نہیں پڑھنا بلکہ اس کو لفظ کی صفت بنا کر مرفوع پڑھنا ہے اور استغراق کا معنی یہ ہے کہ لفظ ان تمام افراد کو شامل ہو جن کو شامل ہونے کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہے لغت کے اعتبار سے ) قَوْلُهُ إِلَّا فَجَمْعٌ مُنكَرُ) الْمُعْتَبَرُ فِي الْعَامٌ عِندَ فَخْرِ الْإِسْلَامِ وَبَعْضِ الْمَشَايِخِ هُوَ انْتِظَامُ جَمْعٍ مِنَ الْمُسَمَّيَاتِ بِاعْتِبَارِ أَمْرٍ يَشْتَرِكُ فِيهِ سَوَاءٌ وُجِدَ الاسْتِغْرَاقُ أَمْ لَا فَالْجَمْعُ الْمُنَكَّرُ عِنْدَهُمْ عَامٌ سَوَاءٌ كَانَ مُسْتَغْرِفًا أَوْ لَا وَالْمُصَنِّفُ لَمَّا اشْتَرَطَ الاسْتِغْرَاقَ عَلَى مَا هُوَ اخْتِيَارُ الْمُحَقِّقِينَ فَالْجَمْعُ الْمُنَكَّرُ يَكُونُ وَاسِطَةٌ بَيْنَ الْعَامِّ وَالْخَاصٌ عِندَ مَنْ يَقُولُ بِعَدَمِ اسْتِغْرَاقِهِ وَعَامَّا عِنْدَ مَنْ يَقُولُ بِاسْتِغْرَاقِهِ وَعَلَى هَذَا التَّقْدِيرِ يَكُونُ الْمُرَادُ بِالْجَمْعِ الْمُنكَرِ فِي قَوْلِهِ وَإِلَّا فَجَمْعٌ مُنكَرٌ الْجَمْعَ الَّذِى تَدُلُّ قَرِينَةٌ عَلَى عَدَمِ اسْتِعْرَاقِهِ ، مِثْلُ رَأيت الْيَوْمَ رِجَالًا وَفِي الدَّارِ رِجَالٌ إِلَّا أَنْ هَذَا غَيْرُ مُخْتَصَّ بِالْجَمْعِ الْمُنَكَّرِ ، بَلْ كُلُّ عَامٌ مَقْصُورٌ عَلَى الْبَعْضِ بِدَلِيلِ الْعَقْلِ أَوْ غَيْرِهِ يَلْزَمُ أَنْ يَكُونَ وَاسِطَةٌ جَمْعًا مُنَكَرًا أَوْ نَحْوَهُ عَلَى مُقْتَضَى عِبَارَةِ الْمُصَنِّفِ لِدُخُولِهِ فِى قَوْلِهِ ، وَإِنْ لَمْ يَسْتَغْرِقْ فَجَمْعٌ مُنَكَّرٌ وَنَحْوُهُ وَفَسَادُهُ بَيِّنٌ ( قَوْلُهُ أَوْ بِاعْتِبَارِ النَّوْعِ كَرَجُلٍ وَفَرَسٍ إِشَارَةٌ إِلَى أَنَّ النَّوْعَ فِي عُرُفِ الشَّرْعِ قَدْ يَكُونُ نَوْعًا مَنْطِقِيًّا كَالْفَرَسِ ، وَقَدْ لَا يَكُونُ كَالرَّجُلِ فَإِنَّ الشَّرُعَ قَدْ يَجْعَلُ الرَّجُلَ وَالْمَرْأَةَ نَوْعَيْنِ مُخْتَلِفَيْنِ نَظَرًا إِلَى اخْتِصَاصِ الرَّجُلِ بِأَحْكَامٍ مِثْلِ النُّبُوَّةِ ، وَالْإِمَامَةِ وَالشَّهَادَةِ فِى الْحَدّ وَالْقِصَاصِ وَنَحْوِ ذَلِكَ .
It is for particulars or such comprehension as the whole's comprehension of its parts. If the comprehension of the universal for particulars, it is called comprehension by correspondence (isti'raq mutabiqi), and if the comprehension of the whole for its parts, it is called comprehension by inclusion (isti'raq tadammuni). Now we say that in number words, both comprehension by correspondence (according to universal-particular) and comprehension by inclusion (according to whole-parts) are found. So the comprehension in 'malikah' is comprehension by correspondence (universal-particular) and also comprehension by inclusion (whole-parts). For the word is applicable to hundreds by correspondence and to each individual by inclusion. Hence comprehension is found in numbers, so they are not excluded by the restriction of 'scattered'; inevitably we add the restriction 'unlimited' to exclude them. And his statement 'mustaghriq': it explains the vowel marks; it should not be read in genitive as an adjective of 'kathir', but rather as predicate in nominative as an adjective of the word. The meaning of istighraq is that the word includes all individuals that it is capable of including linguistically. His statement: 'except that it is an indefinite plural': According to Fakhr al-Islam and some mashayikh, what is considered in 'amm is the assemblage of a plurality of names by virtue of a common attribute, whether comprehension exists or not. So the indefinite plural is 'amm in their view, whether comprehensive or not. But the author (al-musannif) stipulates comprehension, as is the choice of the muhaqqiqun; therefore the indefinite plural is an intermediate between 'amm and khass according to those who deny its comprehension, and it is 'amm according to those who affirm its comprehension. On this basis, the intended meaning of 'indefinite plural' in his statement 'otherwise an indefinite plural' is the plural that a context indicates is non-comprehensive, like 'I saw men today' and 'in the house are men'. But this is not specific to indefinite plural; rather, every 'amm restricted to some by a rational or other evidence must become an intermediate—whether indefinite plural or similar—according to the author's expression, due to its inclusion in his statement: 'and if it does not comprehend, then indefinite plural and the like.' Its corruption is clear. His statement: 'or by consideration of type, like man and horse' indicates that the type in the custom of the Law may be a logical type like horse, and may not be, like man, for the Law makes man and woman two different types considering the specificity of man to rulings such as prophethood, imamate, testimony in hudud and qisas, and the like.
Source pages p. 512

Commentary
This passage from the commentary (sharh) discusses the concept of istighraq (comprehensiveness) and its role in defining 'amm (general term). It first distinguishes two types of istighraq: mutabiqi (correspondence) where the universal covers its particulars, and tadammuni (inclusion) where the whole covers its parts. This distinction is applied to number words, which exhibit both types. Then it addresses the grammatical parsing of 'mustaghriq' and defines istighraq as a word’s inclusion of all individuals it can possibly include linguistically. The core legal discussion is about the definition of 'amm: Fakhr al-Islam and some mashayikh consider any indefinite plural (jama' munakkar) as 'amm, regardless of whether it is comprehensive (mustaghriq) or not. However, the author (al-musannif, Sadr al-Shariah) stipulates istighraq as a condition, following the muhaqqiqun. According to this latter view, a non-comprehensive indefinite plural is an intermediate (wasita) between 'amm and khass, and only a comprehensive one is 'amm. The passage gives an example: 'I saw men today' is non-comprehensive due to context. It also criticizes the view that would make every restricted 'amm an intermediate, showing its absurdity. Finally, it comments on the phrase 'or by consideration of type' explaining that Shariah recognizes types that may not be logical types, e.g., man and woman are treated as distinct types due to differing rulings.

Key Terms
استغراق (istighraq): Comprehensiveness: a word includes all individuals it is capable of including in language.
جمع منكر (jama' munakkar): Indefinite plural: a noun in plural form without definite article, e.g., رجال (men).
عام ('amm): A general term that includes all individuals it can possibly cover if comprehensive.
خاص (khass): A specific term that excludes some individuals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author (al-musannif) in the passage, what is required for a term to be 'amm?
A) Indefiniteness
B) Plurality
C) Istighraq (comprehensiveness)
D) Definiteness

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, according to the muhaqqiqun, a term is 'amm only if it is mustaghriq (comprehensive); an indefinite plural without comprehensiveness is an intermediate between 'amm and khass.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
advanced
10 min
The Status of Indefinite Plural: 'Amm or Intermediate?
Presents internal Hanafi dispute on indefinite plural

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare the two Hanafi views on indefinite plural (Fakhr al-Islam vs. al-musannif) and apply the condition of istighraq to classify a given indefinite plural as 'amm or wasita.

Core Idea
An indefinite plural is 'amm only if comprehensive; otherwise it is an intermediate between 'amm and khass.

This passage presents a key dispute in Hanafi usul: does an indefinite plural automatically qualify as 'amm, or does it require istighraq? Fakhr al-Islam and some mashayikh hold the former view, while the author and the muhaqqiqun require comprehensiveness. Through this dispute, we see how the condition of istighraq affects legal interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
From the text, extract the view of Fakhr al-Islam (indefinite plural is 'amm regardless of istighraq) and the view of the author (istighraq is required).
These are two distinct Hanafi positions.
2
Understand the basis of each view
Fakhr al-Islam considers the mere assemblage of items sharing an attribute sufficient. The author, following the muhaqqiqun, insists on linguistic comprehensiveness.
The basis is the definition of 'amm itself.
3
Apply to an example
Use the example from the text: 'رأيت رجالا اليوم' (I saw men today). According to Fakhr al-Islam, it is 'amm. According to the author, it is not mustaghriq, thus wasita.
Context limits the scope.
4
Understand the criticism of the alternative
The passage criticizes the view that would make every restricted 'amm an intermediate, calling it corrupt. This strengthens the author's position.
The critic argues that the author's definition would force many terms into the intermediate category, which is absurd.

It is for particulars or such comprehension as the whole's comprehension of its parts. If the comprehension of the universal for particulars, it is called comprehension by correspondence (isti'raq mutabiqi), and if the comprehension of the whole for its parts, it is called comprehension by inclusion (isti'raq tadammuni). Now we say that in number words, both comprehension by correspondence (according to universal-particular) and comprehension by inclusion (according to whole-parts) are found. So the comprehension in 'malikah' is comprehension by correspondence (universal-particular) and also comprehension by inclusion (whole-parts). For the word is applicable to hundreds by correspondence and to each individual by inclusion. Hence comprehension is found in numbers, so they are not excluded by the restriction of 'scattered'; inevitably we add the restriction 'unlimited' to exclude them. And his statement 'mustaghriq': it explains the vowel marks; it should not be read in genitive as an adjective of 'kathir', but rather as predicate in nominative as an adjective of the word. The meaning of istighraq is that the word includes all individuals that it is capable of including linguistically. His statement: 'except that it is an indefinite plural': According to Fakhr al-Islam and some mashayikh, what is considered in 'amm is the assemblage of a plurality of names by virtue of a common attribute, whether comprehension exists or not. So the indefinite plural is 'amm in their view, whether comprehensive or not. But the author (al-musannif) stipulates comprehension, as is the choice of the muhaqqiqun; therefore the indefinite plural is an intermediate between 'amm and khass according to those who deny its comprehension, and it is 'amm according to those who affirm its comprehension. On this basis, the intended meaning of 'indefinite plural' in his statement 'otherwise an indefinite plural' is the plural that a context indicates is non-comprehensive, like 'I saw men today' and 'in the house are men'. Commentary
This passage from the commentary (sharh) discusses the concept of istighraq (comprehensiveness) and its role in defining 'amm (general term). It first distinguishes two types of istighraq: mutabiqi (correspondence) where the universal covers its particulars, and tadammuni (inclusion) where the whole covers its parts. This distinction is applied to number words, which exhibit both types. Then it addresses the grammatical parsing of 'mustaghriq' and defines istighraq as a word’s inclusion of all individuals it can possibly include linguistically. The core legal discussion is about the definition of 'amm: Fakhr al-Islam and some mashayikh consider any indefinite plural (jama' munakkar) as 'amm, regardless of whether it is comprehensive (mustaghriq) or not. However, the author (al-musannif, Sadr al-Shariah) stipulates istighraq as a condition, following the muhaqqiqun. According to this latter view, a non-comprehensive indefinite plural is an intermediate (wasita) between 'amm and khass, and only a comprehensive one is 'amm. The passage gives an example: 'I saw men today' is non-comprehensive due to context. It also criticizes the view that would make every restricted 'amm an intermediate, showing its absurdity. Finally, it comments on the phrase 'or by consideration of type' explaining that Shariah recognizes types that may not be logical types, e.g., man and woman are treated as distinct types due to differing rulings.

Key Terms
استغراق (istighraq): Comprehensiveness: a word includes all individuals it is capable of including in language.
جمع منكر (jama' munakkar): Indefinite plural: a noun in plural form without definite article, e.g., رجال (men).
عام ('amm): A general term that includes all individuals it can possibly cover if comprehensive.
خاص (khass): A specific term that excludes some individuals.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate

Definitions of 'Aam, Jam' Munkar, Mushtarak, and Mu'awwal
Commentary on definitions of 'aam, jam' munkar, mushtarak, and mu'awwal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi condition for jam' munkar to be 'aam and distinguish mu'awwal from mufassar based on the nature of evidence.

Core Idea
Jam' munkar is 'aam only if mustaghriq; otherwise it is intermediate between 'aam and khass.

This passage from a detailed commentary expands on four key usul terms: 'aam (general), jam' munkar (indefinite plural), mushtarak (homonym), and mu'awwal (interpreted). The central debate concerns whether jam' munkar is always 'aam, as the jumhur hold, or only when it carries istighraq (comprehensiveness), as the author prefers after the muhaqqiqun. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying general texts in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Term and Its Definition
Read the passage and locate the definitions of 'aam, jam' munkar, mushtarak, and mu'awwal. Note how each is described in the Arabic text and the commentary.
The jam' munkar is an indefinite plural like رجال.
2
Locate the Condition (istighraq) and the Ikhtilaf
Find where the commentator distinguishes between the jumhur (Fakhr al-Islam and some) and the author (matn). The jumhur say jam' munkar is 'aam whether mustaghriq or not; the author says it is 'aam only if mustaghriq, otherwise intermediate.
This ikhtilaf appears at the beginning of the Urdu commentary section.
3
Apply the Definition to Given Examples
Use the example 'رأيت رجالا' (I saw men) from the text. Determine whether this jam' munkar is 'aam or intermediate according to the author's view. Explain why based on presence/absence of qarina indicating istighraq.
The text says the qarina indicates non-istighraq, so it is intermediate.
4
Distinguish Mu'awwal from Mufassar
Read the section on mushtarak and mu'awwal. Understand that mu'awwal is determined by ghalabat al-zann (dominant conjecture) after ijtihad, while mufassar uses qati' evidence. Note the example of 'quru'.
5
Summarize the Thamarah al-Khilaf
Write a concise statement on the practical consequence of the ikhtilaf about jam' munkar. When encountering a jam' munkar in a text, a Hanafi must check for a qarina of istighraq before treating it as 'aam.

عام کے بارے میں جمہور اصولیین اور ماتن کا نکتہ نظر
تشریح:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا پہلا حصہ ہے اس میں شارخ نے عام کے بارے جمہور اصولین اور ماتن کا نکتہ نظر پیش کیا ہے کہ عام کی تعریف میں اختلاف ہے جمہور کے نزدیک عام وہ لفظ ہے جو تمام مسمیات کو مشتمل ہو ایسے امر کے واسطہ سے جو تمام افراد میں مشترک ہو عام ہے کہ استغراق ہو یا نہ ہو یعنی جب لفظ بولا جائے تو تمام افراد کو گھیرے میں لے یا نہ لے یہ مطلب ہے استغراق ہونے نہ ہونے کا۔ بس لفظ اپنے مسمیات پر مشتمل ہو لیکن مصنف نے کہا کہ لفظ تمام مسمیات پر مشتمل ہو اور تمام افراد کو مستغرق بھی ہو یعنی بیک وقت تمام افراد کو شامل ہواب ثمرہ اختلاف ظاہر ہوگا جمع منکر میں کہ جمع منکر میں استغراق ہو یا نہ ہو جمہور کے ہاں یہ عام ہے کیونکہ ان کے ہاں عام کی تعریف میں استغراق کی قید نہیں لیکن ماتن کی تحقیق کے مطابق جمع منکر میں استغراق ہو تو عام ہے ورنہ عام و خاص کے درمیان واسطہ ہوگا۔ وعلی ہذا التقدمیں:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے غرض شاریخ سوال مقدر کا جواب دینا ہے ۔ سوال کو سمجھنے سے قبل ایک تمہید کا جاننا ضروری ہے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ جمع منکر کے بارے میں اصولیین کا اختلاف ہے عند البعض عام ہے اور عند البعض عام نہیں ہے اور یہ اختلاف ایک اور اختلاف پر بھی ہے کہ اس میں استغراق ہے یا نہیں جو کہتے ہیں کہ استغراق ہے وہ عام مانتے ہیں اور جو کہتے ہیں کہ استغراق نہیں ہے وہ عام نہیں کہتے ۔ سوال :۔ جولوگ کہتے ہیں کہ جمع منکر میں استغراق ہے ان کے مذہب کے مطابق مصنف پر سوال ہے کہ جب جمع منکر عام
Translation: His statement 'indefinite plural' is considered general according to Fakhr al-Islam and some scholars - it is a plural of a group of individuals with respect to a common attribute, whether istighraq (comprehensiveness) is found or not. So indefinite plural is general for them, whether mustaghriq or not. And when the author conditioned istighraq, relying on the preferred view of the muhaqqiqun, then indefinite plural becomes intermediate between general and specific for those who hold it is not mustaghriq, and general for those who hold it is mustaghriq. On this assumption, the meaning of indefinite plural in his statement is that plural which indicates a qarina (contextual indicator) of its non-istighraq. Like 'I saw men today' and 'in the house are men', but it is not specific to indefinite plural; rather it includes every general that is restricted to some individuals by rational evidence or the like, necessitating that indefinite plural or similar becomes intermediate. The corruption of his statement 'and if not mustaghriq then indefinite plural and its like' is clear.
His statement 'or by consideration of type': his statement 'by consideration of type' means by type, like 'man' and 'horse'. It points to the fact that in the custom of Shari'ah, sometimes the type is logical type like 'horse', and sometimes not like 'man', because Shari'ah makes 'man' and 'woman' two different types considering the specificity of 'man' with rulings like prophethood, imamate, hadd, testimony, qisas, etc.
His statement 'then the common': his statement 'then the common'. Fakhr al-Islam and others mentioned that according to wording and language, the divisions of expressions are four: specific, general, common, and interpreted (mu'awwal), and the explanation of mu'awwal is that some of its meanings are given preference over others by dominant opinion. And objection was raised that mu'awwal is never from common, and its preference is never by dominant opinion, as mentioned in al-Mizan: indeed khafi, mushkil, mushtarak, and mujmal when clarified by qati' evidence are called mufassar, and when their obscurity is removed by evidence containing doubt like khabar wahid or qiyas, they are called mu'awwal. The first objection was answered: it is not intended as an absolute definition of mu'awwal, but rather the mu'awwal that is from mushtarak, because that is from the divisions according to wording and language. The second objection was answered: indeed dominant opinion means ghalabat al-zann, whether obtained by khabar wahid, qiyas, or pondering on the wording, like in the example of 'three' in 'quru''. And the meaning of its being from the divisions of expression according to wording and language is that the ruling after interpretation is attributed to the wording. It is said that 'dominant opinion' means reflection and ijtihad in the wording itself, and mushtarak and preference by ijtihad and deliberation in the wording are restricted so that its being from the divisions of expression according to wording and language is verified, because mushtarak is placed for multiple meanings, each likely on a substitution basis. When it is applied to one meaning with consideration of the wording, it does not exit from the divisions of expression according to wording and language, i.e., according to wad'. Unlike when it is applied with qati' evidence, then it becomes tafsir, not ta'wil; or with qiyas or khabar wahid, because then it is not from the divisions according to wording and language. Similarly, if it is not mushtarak but khafi, mujmal, or mutashabih, then its obscurity is removed by qati' or zanni evidence.
Source pages p. 514

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the author's matn regarding the classification of words. It first discusses the indefinite plural (jam' munkar), explaining that according to Fakhr al-Islam and some scholars, the indefinite plural is considered general ('aam) whether it includes all individuals (istighraq) or not. The author, however, follows the preferred view of the muhaqqiqun, which conditions istighraq: if the indefinite plural is mustaghriq (comprehensive of all individuals), it is 'aam; if not, it is an intermediate category between 'aam and khass (specific). This view is rooted in the Hanafi usul tradition, where definitions often consider the presence of qarina (contextual indicator). The text then shifts to discussing 'type' in Shari'ah, noting that sometimes the customary type matches logical type (e.g., 'horse') and sometimes not (e.g., 'man' is given a distinct legal status). Finally, the passage examines the four divisions of expressions: khass, 'aam, mushtarak (common/homonym), and mu'awwal (interpreted). It explains that mu'awwal is a word whose preferred meaning is determined by dominant zann (conjecture), as opposed to tafsir which uses qati' evidence. Objections are raised and answered: mu'awwal only applies to mushtarak, and dominant zann can come from khabar wahid, qiyas, or ijtihad on the wording itself. The Urdu section at the end summarizes the disagreement between the jumhur (majority of usuliyyun) and the matn author regarding the definition of 'aam and the status of jam' munkar, emphasizing the practical consequence (thamaratu al-khilaf) that jam' munkar is 'aam only if mustaghriq according to the author.

Key Terms
جمع منکر (jam' munkar): An indefinite plural noun without the definite article, which may or may not be mustaghriq.
عام ('aam): A word that encompasses all its individuals, either with or without istighraq according to jumhur, but with istighraq according to the author.
مشترک (mushtarak): A word with multiple meanings on a substitution basis, used in the context of mu'awwal.
مؤول (mu'awwal): A word whose meaning is determined by dominant conjecture (ghalabat al-zann) after ijtihad, not by qati' evidence.

Checkpoint
According to the author (matn), what is the legal status of a jam' munkar that lacks a qarina indicating istighraq?
A) It is 'aam (general) because indefinite plural covers all individuals.
B) It is khass (specific) because absence of istighraq makes it specific.
C) It is intermediate between 'aam and khass, neither fully general nor fully specific.
D) It is batil (invalid) because the definition is not satisfied.

Key Takeaway
Jam' munkar (indefinite plural) is 'aam only when mustaghriq; otherwise it occupies an intermediate position between general and specific.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
Definition of 'Amm: Jumhur vs Hanafi and the Status of Indefinite Plurals
Usul dispute on definition of 'Amm with objection-response

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two definitions of 'Amm (Jumhur vs Hanafi) and apply them to classify an indefinite plural (jami' munkar) as 'Amm or intermediary, using the condition of istighraq.

Core Idea
Hanafi 'Amm requires istighraq; Jumhur do not, so indefinite plurals are 'Amm only if istighraq present.

The definition of 'Amm (general term) is not uniform across usul traditions. The majority (Jumhur) define it broadly without requiring simultaneous inclusion (istighraq), while the Hanafi matn (al-Tanqih) insists on istighraq. This disagreement has a concrete consequence: how do we classify indefinite plurals (jami' munkar) like 'rijal' (men)? This lesson unpacks the definitions, the objection raised against the Hanafi position, and the defense offered in the commentary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions of 'Amm
State the Jumhur definition: a word covering all its denoted individuals by a common attribute, whether simultaneously or not. Then state the Hanafi (matn) definition: a word that covers all individuals simultaneously (istighraq). Note the key difference is the condition of istighraq.
The Urdu text uses 'استغراق' for simultaneous inclusion.
2
Understand the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Apply both definitions to the indefinite plural (jami' munkar). For Jumhur, all indefinite plurals are 'Amm because istighraq is not required. For Hanafi, only those with istighraq are 'Amm; otherwise they fall in an intermediary category between 'Amm and Khas.
Example: 'ra'aytu rijalan' (I saw men) – without context, Hanafi may not consider it 'Amm if no istighraq.
3
Work through the question and answer about the matn's wording
The matn author lists 'indefinite plural' separately from 'Amm. The question: why exclude it if it is part of 'Amm? Answer: The matn refers specifically to indefinite plurals where a qarina (indication) negates istighraq, e.g., 'ra'aytu al-yawma rijalan' (I saw men today) – 'today' indicates not all men.
This shows the Hanafi position is nuanced: not all indefinite plurals are 'Amm.
4
Analyze the objection regarding 'Amm khass
Objection: If istighraq is required, then a 'Amm that is later specified by an exclusion (takhsis) loses istighraq and should not be called 'Amm. Yet usul scholars still call it 'Amm khass. Response: Excluded individuals were never intended; the remaining individuals still have istighraq. Thus the term 'Amm applies in truth (haqiqah).
This defense preserves the Hanafi definition while accounting for specification.

عام کے بارے میں جمہور اصولیین اور ماتن کا نکتہ نظر
تشریح:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا پہلا حصہ ہے اس میں شارخ نے عام کے بارے جمہور اصولین اور ماتن کا نکتہ نظر پیش کیا ہے کہ عام کی تعریف میں اختلاف ہے جمہور کے نزدیک عام وہ لفظ ہے جو تمام مسمیات کو مشتمل ہو ایسے امر کے واسطہ سے جو تمام افراد میں مشترک ہو عام ہے کہ استغراق ہو یا نہ ہو یعنی جب لفظ بولا جائے تو تمام افراد کو گھیرے میں لے یا نہ لے یہ مطلب ہے استغراق ہونے نہ ہونے کا۔ بس لفظ اپنے مسمیات پر مشتمل ہو لیکن مصنف نے کہا کہ لفظ تمام مسمیات پر مشتمل ہو اور تمام افراد کو مستغرق بھی ہو یعنی بیک وقت تمام افراد کو شامل ہواب ثمرہ اختلاف ظاہر ہوگا جمع منکر میں کہ جمع منکر میں استغراق ہو یا نہ ہو جمہور کے ہاں یہ عام ہے کیونکہ ان کے ہاں عام کی تعریف میں استغراق کی قید نہیں لیکن ماتن کی تحقیق کے مطابق جمع منکر میں استغراق ہو تو عام ہے ورنہ عام و خاص کے درمیان واسطہ ہوگا۔ وعلی ہذا التقدمیں:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے غرض شاریخ سوال مقدر کا جواب دینا ہے ۔ سوال کو سمجھنے سے قبل ایک تمہید کا جاننا ضروری ہے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ جمع منکر کے بارے میں اصولیین کا اختلاف ہے عند البعض عام ہے اور عند البعض عام نہیں ہے اور یہ اختلاف ایک اور اختلاف پر بھی ہے کہ اس میں استغراق ہے یا نہیں جو کہتے ہیں کہ استغراق ہے وہ عام مانتے ہیں اور جو کہتے ہیں کہ استغراق نہیں ہے وہ عام نہیں کہتے ۔ سوال :۔ جولوگ کہتے ہیں کہ جمع منکر میں استغراق ہے ان کے مذہب کے مطابق مصنف پر سوال ہے کہ جب جمع منکر عام میں داخل ہے تو پھر ماتن کا والا لجمع منکر کہنے کا کیا مطلب ہے؟ یعنی جب یہ عام میں داخل ہے تو عام سے استثناء کرنے کا کیا مطلب ہوگا ؟
جواب : والا لجمع منکر سے مراد وہ جمع منکر ہے جہاں قرینہ ہو کہ اس میں استغراق نہیں ہے جیسے رایت الیوم رجالا اب یہاں الیوم پر قرینہ عقلی ہے کہ تمام رجال کو ایک دن میں نہیں دیکھا جا سکتا معلوم ہوا کہ یہاں رجال میں استغراق نہیں ہے لہذا یہ عام میں داخل نہ ہوگا تو استثناء کرنا صحیح ہے۔
الا ان ہذا:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا تیسرا حصہ ہے یہاں سے شاریخ نے ماتن پر اعتراض کیا ہے۔ اعتراض:۔ یہ ہے کہ اگر عام میں استغراق کی شرط لگائی جائے تو وہ عام جو بعض افراد پر بند ہو عام خص عند البعض ) اور بعض افراد کا استثناء ہو دلیل عقلی کی وجہ سے یا خبر مشہور کی وجہ سے یا اجتماع کی وجہ سے یا دلیل نلنی کی وجہ سے یا دلیل قطعی کی وجہ سے بعض افراد کا استثناء ہورہا ہو جب بعض افراد عام سے مستثنی ہوں گے تو اس میں استغراق نہیں ہو گا تو اس کو عام نہیں کہنا چاہیے ۔ حالانکہ اصولی اس کو عام خص عند البعض کہتے ہیں حالانکہ جب استغراق کی شرط موجود نہیں ہے تو اس کو عام نہیں کہنا چاہیے؟ جواب:۔ یہ اعتراض برائے اعتراض ہے جب بعض افراد کو کسی قرینہ کی وجہ سے مستثنی کیا گیا ہو تو وہ افراد عام میں داخل ہی نہیں ہیں اور جو باقی ہیں ان میں استغراق کی شرط موجود ہے جب استغراق ہے تو عام کا اطلاق درست ہے اور یہ عام کا اطلاق حقیقہ ہے عام سے خارج نہیں ہے۔
Regarding 'Amm: The viewpoint of the majority of usul scholars and the author of the matn.
Commentary: This is the first part of the commentator's text. In it, the commentator presents the viewpoint of the majority and the author regarding 'Amm, that there is disagreement in the definition of 'Amm. According to the majority, 'Amm is a word that encompasses all its denoted individuals by virtue of something common to all individuals, whether it includes all individuals simultaneously (istighraq) or not – i.e., whether when the word is uttered it covers all individuals or not. This is the meaning of having or not having istighraq. The word just encompasses its denoted individuals. But the author said that the word must encompass all denoted individuals and also include all individuals simultaneously at once. The consequence of the disagreement appears in the indefinite plural (jami' munkar): whether the indefinite plural has istighraq or not. According to the majority it is 'Amm because in their definition of 'Amm the condition of istighraq is not required. But according to the author's investigation, if the indefinite plural has istighraq it is 'Amm, otherwise it will be an intermediary between 'Amm and Khas.
And upon this: The second part of the commentator's text; the commentator aims to answer a presupposed question. Before understanding the question, a premise is necessary: there is disagreement among usul scholars regarding the indefinite plural: some say it is 'Amm, some say it is not. This disagreement is also based on another disagreement: whether it has istighraq or not. Those who say it has istighraq consider it 'Amm, and those who say it does not have istighraq do not consider it 'Amm.
Question: According to those who say that the indefinite plural has istighraq, there is a question upon the author: if the indefinite plural falls under 'Amm, then what does the author mean by saying 'and the indefinite plural'? That is, if it is included in 'Amm, what is the point of excluding it from 'Amm?.
Answer: What is meant by 'the indefinite plural' is that indefinite plural where there is a contextual indication (qarina) that it does not have istighraq – such as 'I saw men today' (ra'aytu al-yawma rijalan). Here 'today' is a rational indication that all men cannot be seen in one day. So it is known that 'rijal' here does not have istighraq, therefore it is not included in 'Amm, so excluding it is correct.
Except that this: The third part of the commentator's text; from here the commentator raises an objection against the author.
Objection: It is that if istighraq is made a condition for 'Amm, then take a 'Amm that is restricted to some individuals ('Amm khass 'ind al-ba'd) where some individuals are excluded due to a rational proof, or a well-known report (khabar mashhur), or consensus (ijtima'), or a transmitted proof, or a definitive proof – when some individuals are excluded, there will be no istighraq in it, so it should not be called 'Amm. Yet the usul scholars call it 'Amm khass 'ind al-ba'd. When the condition of istighraq is absent, should it not be called 'Amm?
Answer: This objection is baseless. When some individuals are excluded due to some contextual indication, those individuals were never included in the 'Amm. For the remaining individuals, the condition of istighraq is present. Since there is istighraq, applying 'Amm to it is correct, and this application of 'Amm is true (haqiqah), not outside of 'Amm.
Source pages p. 515

Commentary
This passage presents a key usul dispute on the definition of 'Amm (general term). The majority (Jumhur) define 'Amm as a word that encompasses all its denoted individuals without requiring simultaneous inclusion (istighraq). The author of the matn (Sadr al-Shariah) requires istighraq – that the word includes all individuals at once. The practical consequence shows in the indefinite plural (jami' munkar). According to the Jumhur, any indefinite plural is 'Amm because istighraq is not required. But according to the author, only indefinite plurals with istighraq are 'Amm; otherwise, they fall in between 'Amm and Khas. The text then addresses a question: why does the author mention 'indefinite plural' separately in his classification if it is already included in 'Amm? The answer is that the author's statement refers to those indefinite plurals where a qarina indicates no istighraq, so they are not 'Amm. Then an objection is raised about 'Amm khass (general term made specific) – if some individuals are excluded, istighraq is lost, so it should not be called 'Amm. The response clarifies that the excluded individuals were never intended, and the remaining still have istighraq, so the term 'Amm applies.

Key Terms
عام ('Amm): A word that encompasses all its denoted individuals. Jumhur: without requirement of istighraq; Matan: with requirement of istighraq.
استغراق (istighraq): Simultaneous inclusion of all individuals denoted by the word at the moment of utterance.
جمع منکر (jami' munkar): An indefinite plural (e.g., rijal, aqlam). Its status as 'Amm depends on presence of istighraq.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author of the matn (Hanafi position), when is an indefinite plural (jami' munkar) considered 'Amm?
A) Always, because all indefinite plurals are 'Amm.
B) Only when there is a qarina indicating it does not have istighraq.
C) Only when it has istighraq, i.e., simultaneous inclusion of all individuals.
D) Never, because indefinite plurals are always Khas.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of 'Amm requires istighraq, making the classification of indefinite plurals dependent on context; this differs from the Jumhur who consider all indefinite plurals as 'Amm.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
