Types of Khas: Fardi, Jinsi, and Naw'i with Logical vs Legal Distinction
Explaining the three categories of specific terms (Khas) with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three types of Khas (fardi, jinsi, naw'i) and explain the difference between logical type (naw' mantiqi) and legal type (naw' shar'i) with examples from Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Khas divides into three types: individual, generic, and specific; the specific type further splits into logical (essence-based) and legal (purpose-based) categories.

This lesson unpacks the classification of 'specific terms' (Khas) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The matn (text) states that Khas is of three types: fardi (individual, e.g., Zayd), jinsi (generic, e.g., man as a genus), and naw'i (specific, e.g., man or horse). The commentator then explains that the naw'i type can be either logical (naw' mantiqi) or legal (naw' shar'i), a distinction crucial for deriving correct rulings from legal texts.

Guided Path
1
1. Identify the three types of Khas
Recall from the matn: fardi (individual), jinsi (generic), and naw'i (specific). Each applies to a limited set but at different levels of generality.
Fardi applies to one specific individual; jinsi to a genus; naw'i to a species.
2
2. Recognize the examples given
The matn gives 'rajul' (man) and 'faras' (horse) as examples of naw'i Khas. The commentator explains why two examples were needed: to illustrate both logical and legal types.
Man is a legal type; horse is a logical type.
3
3. Distinguish logical type (naw' mantiqi) from legal type (naw' shar'i)
Logical type is based on shared essence (haqiqah) – all horses share the reality of a whinnying animal. Legal type is based on shared purposes (aghrad) – all men share the purpose of eligibility for imamate, caliphate, etc.
Men and women are logically the same species (human) but legally distinct types because their purposes differ according to the Shari'ah.
4
4. Apply the distinction to a new example
Consider cattle: logically, all cows and bulls belong to the same species (bovine), but legally, they may be treated differently for certain rulings (e.g., sacrifice rules). This shows how legal type can differ from logical type.
Always check whether a ruling is based on essence or purpose.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قولہ او باعتبار:۔ یہاں سے شاریخ نے متن کی توضیح کی ہے ماتن نے کہا تھا کہ خاص کی تین قسمیں ہیں فردی ، جنسی ، نوعی اور خاص نوعی کی دو مثالیں دی تھیں رجل و فرس تو شاریخ فرمارہے ہیں کہ ماتن نے دو مثالیں اس لئے دی تھیں تا کہ پتا چل جائے کہ خاص کا نوعی ہونا عام ہے نوعی منطقی ہو یا شرعی ہو۔ نوع منطقی :۔ وہ ہے کہ جو ایسے افراد پر بولی جائے کہ جن کی حقیقت ایک ہو جیسے گھوڑا ان کے تمام افراد کی حقیقت ایک حیوان ساہل ہے۔
نوع شرعی :۔ وہ ہے جن کا اطلاق ایسے افراد پر ہو کہ جن کی اغراض ایک ہوں مثلا رجل اور امراۃ رجل کے جتنے افراد ہیں ان کی اغراض متفق ہیں کہ امامت و خلافت اور شاہد فی القصاص والحدود ہونا رجل کا حق ہے اور امراۃ کی اغراض متفق ہیں کہ گھر کا کام کاج کرے مرد کے لئے فراش بنے وغیرہ ذالک اور رجل و امراة نوع منطقی کے اعتبار سے ایک ہی نوع شمار ہوتے ہیں تو
His saying: 'or by consideration' [or: 'or from one perspective']. From here the commentator explains the text. The author (matn) had said that Khas has three types: individual (fardi), generic (jinsi), and specific (naw'i). And he gave two examples of specific Khas: 'man' (rajul) and 'horse' (faras). So the commentator says that the author gave two examples so that it becomes known that the specific type of Khas is general – whether it is logical type or legal type. Logical type (naw' mantiqi): it is that which is applied to individuals whose reality (haqiqah) is one – like 'horse', all its individuals share the reality of 'a whinnying animal'. Legal type (naw' shar'i): it is that which is applied to individuals whose purposes (aghrad) are one – for example, 'man' and 'woman'. All individuals of 'man' share the purposes that imamate, caliphate, and being a witness in qisas and hadd are the right of man. And the purposes of women are that she does domestic work, serves as a bed for the husband, etc. And 'man' and 'woman' from the perspective of logical type are counted as one type, so...
Source pages p. 516

Commentary
This passage clarifies the threefold division of Khas (specific term) as stated by the matn: fardi (individual, e.g., Zayd), jinsi (generic, e.g., man as a genus), and naw'i (specific/species). The author gave two examples of naw'i Khas: 'rajul' (man) and 'faras' (horse). The commentator explains that these examples illustrate that the 'naw'i' type of Khas can be either logical (mantiqi) or legal (shar'i). A logical type is based on shared essence (haqiqah) – all horses share the reality of being a whinnying animal. A legal type is based on shared legal purposes (aghrad) – all men share the purposes of being eligible for imamate, caliphate, and testimony in hadd and qisas cases; all women share the purpose of domestic duties. The passage notes that logically, man and woman are considered the same species (human), but legally they are treated as separate types due to differing rulings.

Key Terms
خاص (Khas): A term applying to a limited set of individuals; divided into fardi, jinsi, and naw'i.
نوع منطقی (naw' mantiqi): A species defined by shared essence or reality (haqiqah), e.g., horse.
نوع شرعی (naw' shar'i): A category defined by shared legal purposes (aghrad), e.g., men and women treated as separate legal types despite same logical species.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What distinguishes a legal type (naw' shar'i) from a logical type (naw' mantiqi) according to the passage?
A) Logical type is based on shared purposes, legal type on shared essence.
B) Logical type is based on shared essence, legal type on shared purposes.
C) Logical type applies only to animals, legal type only to humans.
D) Both are identical in definition; the terms are interchangeable.

Key Takeaway
Khas is categorized into individual, generic, and specific; the specific type is further divided into logical (based on essence) and legal (based on purpose), which is essential for correct legal interpretation.

Understanding 'والا لجمع منکر' – When a Plural Indefinite Is Not General
Explains the term 'والا لجمع منکر' and condition for valid exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a plural indefinite noun that does not imply universality (والا لجمع منکر) and explain why exception from it is valid in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
A plural indefinite noun with a contextual indicator loses its generality, making exception valid.

This passage from the commentary clarifies a subtle but crucial point in Hanafi usul: not all indefinite plurals are general. The author introduces the term 'والا لجمع منکر' to describe those plurals that, due to a contextual evidence, do not cover all individuals. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying the rule of exception (استثناء) and avoiding the mistake of treating every indefinite plural as a true general.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key term
What is 'والا لجمع منکر'? The passage defines it as a plural indefinite noun with a context (قرینہ) that negates universality (استغراق).
The term is a technical label for this specific category.
2
Analyze the example
The example 'رأیت الیوم رجالا' shows how the context 'today' rationally prevents the plural from referring to all men.
القرینة العقلیة here is the word 'اليوم'.
3
Determine the ruling on exception
Because the plural does not imply universality, exception from it is valid and does not conflict with generality.
Exception does not require a general term; it operates on the specific scope.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
میں داخل ہے تو پھر ماتن کا والا لجمع منکر کہنے کا کیا مطلب ہے؟ یعنی جب یہ عام میں داخل ہے تو عام سے استثناء کرنے کا کیا مطلب ہوگا ؟ جواب : والا لجمع منکر سے مراد وہ جمع منکر ہے جہاں قرینہ ہو کہ اس میں استغراق نہیں ہے جیسے رایت الیوم رجالا اب یہاں الیوم پر قرینہ عقلی ہے کہ تمام رجال کو ایک دن میں نہیں دیکھا جا سکتا معلوم ہوا کہ یہاں رجال میں استغراق نہیں ہے لہذا یہ عام میں داخل نہ ہوگا تو استثناء کرنا صحیح ہے۔
What is the meaning of the author saying 'والا لجمع منکر' when it enters? That is, when this enters into the general, what is the meaning of making an exception from the general? Answer: By 'والا لجمع منکر' is meant that collective indefinite which has a context indicating that it does not imply universality, like 'I saw men today' — here 'today' is a rational context that all men cannot be seen in one day. It is known that 'men' here does not imply universality, so it does not enter into the general, thus making an exception is correct.
Source pages p. 516

Commentary
This passage is a commentary explaining the author's phrase 'والا لجمع منکر', which refers to a plural indefinite noun that does not imply complete universality. The commentator clarifies that such a plural can be excepted from a general statement because it is not truly general. The example of 'I saw men today' shows that the context (اليوم) restricts the plural to those seen that day, so it is not universal. In Hanafi usul, this is important for understanding the operation of exception (استثناء) and its validity: exception is only valid if the original term does not already imply universality. The discussion guards against the misunderstanding that all indefinite plurals are general; here the context (قرینہ) removes generality.

Key Terms
والا لجمع منکر (wa al-li jami' munkar): A plural indefinite noun that does not imply universality due to a contextual evidence (قرینہ).
استغراق (istighraq): Universality; the property of a term to cover all individuals of its category.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It must have no context at all.
B) It must have a context indicating it does not imply universality.
C) It must be a definite plural.
D) It must be used in a negative sentence.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a plural indefinite noun with a context that negates universality is not truly general, so exception from it is valid.

The Reality of General after Particularization: Refuting the Objection against ‘Āmm Khāṣṣ ‘Ind al-Ba‘ḍ
Presents and rebuts an objection regarding the definition of general with the condition of universality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a general term that has been particularized (عام خص عند البعض) remains general in Hanafi usul and apply this principle to a fiqh example.

Core Idea
A general term once particularized by evidence remains general for the remaining set; usage is real, not metaphorical.

This lesson addresses a key objection in Hanafi usul: if universality is required for general terms, can a term that has been particularized still be called general? The commentator raises this objection and the Hanafi school provides a decisive response, clarifying that excepted individuals were never part of the original general scope.

Guided Path
1
Understand the condition of universality (istighraq)
Recognize that in Hanafi usul, a general term must cover all intended individuals with universality. This condition is fundamental for the term to be considered 'āmm.
Universality does not mean every possible individual, but every individual included in the speaker's intent.
2
Identify the objection
The objection claims that if universality is a condition, then a general term that has been particularized (e.g., by rational or textual evidence) loses universality and should no longer be called general.
3
Grasp the Hanafi response
The rebuttal states that the evidence excluding individuals does not remove them from the general; rather, it shows they were never included. Thus, the remaining set still has universality, and the term remains general in a real sense.
The Hanafi position preserves the real (ḥaqīqī) nature of the term, avoiding metaphorical usage.
4
Apply to a fiqh example
Consider the Quranic verse 'الزانية والزاني فاجلدوا كل واحد منهما مائة جلدة' (24:2). It is general for all fornicators, but ijma' excludes slaves (they receive 50 lashes). The verse remains general for free persons, and the ruling applies universally to them.
This principle ensures that exceptions do not undermine the general applicability of legal texts.

Source Text

الا ان ہذا:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا تیسرا حصہ ہے یہاں سے شاریخ نے ماتن پر اعتراض کیا ہے۔ اعتراض:۔ یہ ہے کہ اگر عام میں استغراق کی شرط لگائی جائے تو وہ عام جو بعض افراد پر بند ہو عام خص عند البعض ) اور بعض افراد کا استثناء ہو دلیل عقلی کی وجہ سے یا خبر مشہور کی وجہ سے یا اجتماع کی وجہ سے یا دلیل نلنی کی وجہ سے یا دلیل قطعی کی وجہ سے بعض افراد کا استثناء ہورہا ہو جب بعض افراد عام سے مستثنی ہوں گے تو اس میں استغراق نہیں ہو گا تو اس کو عام نہیں کہنا چاہیے ۔ حالانکہ اصولی اس کو عام خص عند البعض کہتے ہیں حالانکہ جب استغراق کی شرط موجود نہیں ہے تو اس کو عام نہیں کہنا چاہیے؟ جواب:۔ یہ اعتراض برائے اعتراض ہے جب بعض افراد کو کسی قرینہ کی وجہ سے مستثنی کیا گیا ہو تو وہ افراد عام میں داخل ہی نہیں ہیں اور جو باقی ہیں ان میں استغراق کی شرط موجود ہے جب استغراق ہے تو عام کا اطلاق درست ہے اور یہ عام کا اطلاق حقیقہ ہے عام سے خارج نہیں ہے۔
However, this: This is the third part of the commentary phrase. From here the commentator objects to the author. Objection: If universality is made a condition for general, then that general which is confined to some individuals (عام خص عند البعض) and some individuals are excepted due to rational evidence, famous report, consensus, textual evidence, or definitive evidence—when some individuals are excepted from the general, then there is no universality, so it should not be called general. Yet the scholars of usul call it 'general particularized with respect to some' (عام خص عند البعض). When the condition of universality is not present, it should not be called general? Answer: This objection is for the sake of objection. When some individuals are excepted due to some evidence, those individuals were never included in the general; the remaining individuals still have universality. Since there is universality, the application of 'general' is correct and it is a real usage of 'general', not outside it.
Source pages p. 516

Commentary
This passage is a dispute (اعتراض) where the commentator raises an objection against the author (matn) regarding the definition of general (عام) with the condition of universality (استغراق). The objection argues that if universality is a condition, then a general term that has been particularized (عام خص عند البعض) should not be called general because universality is lost. The response clarifies that the individuals excepted were never part of the general (they are excluded by evidence), so the remaining individuals still have universality. Thus, the term 'عام' applies to the remaining set. In Hanafi usul, this is a key point: 'عام خص عند البعض' is still considered a general term in its remaining application, and its usage is real (حقیقی), not metaphorical.

Key Terms
عام خص عند البعض (amm khass ind al-ba'd): A general term that is particularized with respect to some individuals, applied to the remaining set as general.
استغراق (istighraq): Universality; the property of a term to cover all intended individuals.

Distinguishing Logical Type and Legal Type in Hanafi Usul
Defines types of specific and distinguishes logical vs legal type

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between logical type (نوع منطقی) and legal type (نوع شرعی) and explain why legal type is prioritized in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Specific type (خاص نوعی) includes both logical and legal types, but legal type based on shared purposes outweighs logical type.

In Hanafi usul, the term 'type' (نوع) is not limited to logical categories of shared essence. This passage clarifies that Sharia recognizes a distinct kind of type—legal type—rooted in shared legal purposes (اغراض). Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying rulings to categories like 'men' and 'women'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three kinds of خاص
From the passage, list the three kinds: فردی (individual), جنسی (generic), and نوعی (specific type). Note that each has a different scope.
The third kind is the focus of this lesson.
2
Examine the two examples of نوعی
The author gave 'رجل' (man) and 'فرس' (horse) as examples. Why two different examples? The commentator explains they illustrate two subtypes of type.
One example (horse) is a logical type; the other (man) is a legal type.
3
Distinguish logical type from legal type
Logical type (نوع منطقی): individuals share the same essential reality (e.g., all horses are 'saahil' animals). Legal type (نوع شرعی): individuals share the same legal purposes (اغراض), e.g., all men share purposes like imamate and testimony.
The same individuals can belong to both types, but Sharia prioritizes legal type.
4
Understand the commentator's emphasis
The commentator states that in 'urf al-shar' (custom of Sharia), legal type is more important than logical type. This is a key Hanafi principle for interpreting general terms.
This principle affects rulings on testimony, leadership, and other areas.
5
Apply the distinction to a new term
Consider the term 'مسلم' (Muslim). Is it a logical type (all Muslims share the same faith reality) or a legal type (all Muslims share legal purposes like prayer and zakat)? Typically it is both, but legal type may have specific implications.
In fatwa, the legal type dimension often carries more weight.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قولہ او باعتبار:۔ یہاں سے شاریخ نے متن کی توضیح کی ہے ماتن نے کہا تھا کہ خاص کی تین قسمیں ہیں فردی ، جنسی ، نوعی اور خاص نوعی کی دو مثالیں دی تھیں رجل و فرس تو شاریخ فرمارہے ہیں کہ ماتن نے دو مثالیں اس لئے دی تھیں تا کہ پتا چل جائے کہ خاص کا نوعی ہونا عام ہے نوعی منطقی ہو یا شرعی ہو۔ نوع منطقی :۔ وہ ہے کہ جو ایسے افراد پر بولی جائے کہ جن کی حقیقت ایک ہو جیسے گھوڑا ان کے تمام افراد کی حقیقت ایک حیوان ساہل ہے۔ نوع شرعی :۔ وہ ہے جن کا اطلاق ایسے افراد پر ہو کہ جن کی اغراض ایک ہوں مثلا رجل اور امراۃ رجل کے جتنے افراد ہیں ان کی اغراض متفق ہیں کہ امامت و خلافت اور شاہد فی القصاص والحدود ہونا رجل کا حق ہے اور امراۃ کی اغراض متفق ہیں کہ گھر کا کام کاج کرے مرد کے لئے فراش بنے وغیرہ ذالک اور رجل و امراة نوع منطقی کے اعتبار سے ایک ہی نوع شمار ہوتے ہیں تو ماتن نے دو مثالیں دے کر نوع کے عموم کی طرف اشارہ کر دیا کہ نوع عرف شرع میں نوع منطقی سے اہم ہے۔
His statement 'او باعتبار': From here the commentator explains the text. The author had said that specific (خاص) has three types: individual (فردی), generic (جنسی), and specific type (نوعی). He gave two examples of specific type: man and horse. The commentator says that the author gave two examples so that it becomes clear that specific type is general, whether it is logical type (نوع منطقی) or legal type (نوع شرعی). Logical type: that which is applied to individuals whose reality is one, like horse—all its individuals have the same reality, a 'saahil' animal. Legal type: that which is applied to individuals whose purposes (اغراض) are one, e.g., man and woman—all individuals of man agree in purposes like imamate, caliphate, being a witness in retaliation and fixed punishments, and individuals of woman agree in purposes like doing housework, being a bed for the husband, etc. And man and woman are considered one type from a logical aspect, but the author gave two examples to indicate the comprehensiveness of type: in the custom of Sharia, legal type is more important than logical type.
Source pages p. 516

Commentary
This passage is a definitional explanation of the types of 'خاص' (specific). The author (matn) had said that خاص has three divisions: فردی (individual, like Zaid), جنسی (generic, like man as a species), and نوعی (specific type, like the type 'horse' or 'man'). The commentator clarifies that the author gave two examples (رجل and فرس) for the third kind (نوعی) to show that 'type' here covers both logical type (based on shared essential nature) and legal type (based on shared legal purposes). Logical type is like 'horse' where all individuals share the same defining reality (e.g., being a 'saahil' animal). Legal type is like 'man' and 'woman' where individuals share the same legal objectives (اغراض) even though they are different in reality. The commentator points out that in the legal context (عرف شرع), legal type is more significant than logical type. This distinction is important in Hanafi usul for interpreting legal texts that use type terms (like 'men' or 'women')—they are often considered legal types rather than logical categories.

Key Terms
نوع منطقی (naw' mantiqi): A type based on shared essential reality (like all horses sharing the same animal nature).
نوع شرعی (naw' shar'i): A type based on shared legal purposes (اغراض), like all men sharing the purpose of imamate, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) To show that both are logical types.
B) To show that خاص نوعی includes both logical type and legal type.
C) To show that both are individuals.
D) To show that both are generic types.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, legal type (نوع شرعی) based on shared legal purposes takes precedence over logical type in deriving rulings.

Definition of Mu'awwal and Two Objections
Defines mu'awwal and addresses two objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of mu'awwal within the wording-based classification and explain why it is restricted to common terms and preponderant opinion.

Core Idea
Mu'awwal is one meaning of a common term preferred by preponderant opinion — not all interpretations.

In this passage, the commentator defines mu'awwal as per Fakh al-Islam within the fourfold division of terms by wording. Two objections are raised: (1) that mu'awwal should include other ambiguous terms, and (2) that preponderant opinion is not the only preferrer. The response clarifies that this definition is specific to this classification. We will walk through the definition, the objections, and the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
Identify the classification
Recognize that Fakh al-Islam divides terms into four types: خاص, عام, مشترک, and موول. This is the context for the definition.
The commentator is filling a gap left by the matn author.
2
State the definition of mu'awwal
Mu'awwal is the meaning of a common term that is given preference by preponderant opinion. The preferred meaning is called mu'awwal.
This is the core definition.
3
Understand the first objection
The objector argues that restricting mu'awwal to common terms is wrong because other ambiguous terms (خفی, مشکل) become mu'awwal when clarified by speculative evidence.
The objection cites the book Mizan.
4
Understand the second objection
The objector says preponderant opinion is not the only preferrer; there are others like the wording itself, citing the example of 'quru''.
This challenges the 'preponderant opinion' condition.
5
Analyze the Hanafi response
The commentator responds that the definition is specific to the division by wording and language. Other types of mu'awwal belong to other classifications. Thus, the conditions are valid for this specific division.
This resolves the objections by narrowing the scope.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قولہ ثم المشترک:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا پہلا حصہ ہے غرض شارخ موول کی تعریف کرنا ہے نظم کی با عتبار صیغہ اور لغت کے فخر الاسلام کے ہاں چار قسمیں ہیں خاص و عام اور مشترک و موول لیکن ماتن نے موول کا تذکرہ نہیں کیا اور شارخ موول کی تعریف کرتے ہیں موقول کی تعریف یہ ہے کہ مشترک کے معانی میں سے کسی معنی کو ترجیح دے دینا غالب رائے سے جس کو ترجیح دی گئی ہے وہ موول ہے۔ و اور و علیہ:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے یہاں سے شارع موول کی تعریف پر دو اعتراض کرتے ہیں۔ اعتراض (۱):۔ آپ نے موصول کی تعریف میں دو قید میں لگائیں ہیں پہلی قید کہ مشترک کے معانی میں سے کسی معنی کو تر جیح دیں اور دوسری قید کہ غالب رائے سے ترجیح دیں یہ قیدمیں درست نہیں ہیں کیونکہ موول کی بعض قسمیں مشترک ساتھ خاص نہیں ہیں جیسے خفی مشکل وغیرہ اگر خبر واحد یا قیاس وغیرہ ان کا بیان واقع ہوں اور خفا دور ہو جائے تو یہ بھی مؤول ہیں تو مشترک کے ساتھ موول کو خاص کرنا درست نہیں ہے۔ اور اس کی تائید میزان نامی کتاب سے ہوتی ہے اس میں مذکور ہے کہ اگر فی مشکل مجمل مشترک کو دلیل قطعی سے بیان لاحق ہو تو فی ان کو مفسر کہینگے اور اگر بیان دلیل ظنی (قیاس خبر واحد ) وغیرہ سے لاحق ہو تو اس کو موول کہیں گے۔ اعتراض (۲):۔ دوسری قید تھی غالب رائے کی کہ غالب رائے کو آپ نے مرجح قرار دیا حالانکہ غالب رائے کو مرجح قرار دینا درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ مربح غالب رائے کے علاوہ بھی ہیں مثلا خبر واحد یا قیاس یا نفس صیغہ میں غور و فکر کرنا جیسا کہ لفظ قروء میں تامل نی نفس الصیفہ ہے۔ کہ قردہ قرہ کی جمع ہے اور اس کا لغوی معنی اجتماع ہے اسی وجہ سے قراءت کو قراءت کہتے ہیں کہ اس میں اجتماع حروف و کلمات پایا جاتا ہے تو مناسب ہے کہ قرء سے مراد حیض ہو کیونکہ حیض رحم میں ایام حیض میں جمع ہوتا ہے ایام اطہار میں نہیں ۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔ جواب عن الاول :۔ پہلے اعتراض کا جواب یہ ہے کہ فخر الاسلام نے جو تعریف کی ہے یہ مطلق مؤوّل کی نہیں ہے بلکہ مؤوّل کی تعریف ہے جو مشترک سے حاصل ہوتا ہے کیونکہ یہ تقسیم صیغہ اور لغت کے اعتبار سے ہے اور یہی موول جو مشترک کے ساتھ خاص ہے اس تقسیم کی قسم ہے اور باقی دوسرے جو موول میں (خفی مشکل وغیرہ ) وہ اس تقسیم کے اقسام نہیں ہیں جو تقسیم صیغہ اور لغت کے اعتبار سے ہے۔ اس لئے مشترک کی قید لگائی تا کہ یہ صیغہ ولفت نظم کی قسم بن سکے۔
His statement 'then the common term (مشترک)': This is the first part of the commentary phrase. The commentator intends to define the interpreted term (موول). According to Fakh al-Islam, from the perspective of wording (صیغہ) and language (لغت), there are four types: specific, general, common, and interpreted. But the author did not mention interpreted. The commentator defines interpreted as: giving preference to one of the meanings of a common term based on preponderant opinion; what is given preference is the interpreted. 'And against it': This is the second part of the commentary phrase; from here he makes two objections to the definition of interpreted. Objection (1): You have put two conditions in the definition: first, that you give preference to one of the meanings of the common term, second, that you give preference by preponderant opinion. These conditions are not correct because some types of interpreted are not specific to common terms, like ambiguous (خفی, مشکل). If a solitary report or analogy clarifies them and removes the ambiguity, they become interpreted. So restricting interpreted to common terms is not correct. This is supported by the book 'Mizan', which states that if a clear definitive evidence clarifies a problematic, ambiguous, or common term, it is called 'explicit' (مفسر), and if clarification is by speculative evidence like analogy or solitary report, it is called 'interpreted'. Objection (2): The second condition is preponderant opinion as the preferrer, but giving preference by preponderant opinion is not correct because there are other preferrers, like solitary report, analogy, or contemplation of the wording itself, as in the word 'quru'' (قروء) where contemplation of the wording itself is used. The word 'qar' is derived from 'qara' (collection), so its literal meaning is collection; hence 'quru'' is appropriate to mean menstruation because blood collects in the womb during menstruation. Allah knows best. Answer to the first: The definition given by Fakh al-Islam is not of absolute interpreted, but of the interpreted that is derived from a common term, because this division is according to wording and language, and this interpreted specific to common terms is a type of that division. As for other types of interpreted (like خفی, مشکل), they are not part of this division. Therefore, the condition of common term was added so that it becomes a type of the classification by wording and wording order.
Source pages p. 517

Commentary
This passage defines the concept of 'موول' (interpreted term) as per Fakh al-Islam within the classification of terms based on wording (صیغہ) and language (لغت). The four types are: خاص (specific), عام (general), مشترک (common/ambiguous), and موول (interpreted). The author (matn) did not mention موول, so the commentator defines it. The definition: giving preference (ترجیح) to one meaning of a common term based on preponderant opinion (غالب رائے); the preferred meaning is called موول. Two objections are raised: (1) By restricting موول to common terms, the definition excludes other types of موول like ambiguous terms (خفی, مشکل) that become clear through evidence. The book 'Mizan' is cited to support that what is clarified by speculative evidence is موول, and by definitive evidence is مفسر. (2) The condition of preponderant opinion is not exclusive; there are other preferrers like the wording itself, illustrated by the example of 'quru''. The response to the first objection is that Fakh al-Islam's definition is specific to the classification by wording and language; it does not cover all types of موول. Thus, the restriction to common terms is intentional to fit this particular division. In Hanafi usul, this distinction is important for understanding how ambiguous terms are resolved: by definitive evidence (مفسر) or speculative evidence (موول).

Key Terms
موول (mu'awwal): A term whose preferred meaning is determined by preponderant opinion from among the meanings of a common term (مشترک).
مشترک (mushtarak): A term that has multiple meanings in language, like 'quru'' (menstruation or purity).
غالب رائے (ghalib ra'ay): Preponderant opinion; the dominant likelihood that favors one meaning over others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the response, why does Fakh al-Islam restrict the definition of موول to common terms (مشترک)?
A) Because other types of interpretation do not exist.
B) Because this definition is only for the classification by wording and language.
C) Because common terms are the only ones that need interpretation.
D) Because the author did not mention موول.

Key Takeaway
The definition of mu'awwal in Hanafi usul (Fakh al-Islam) is limited to common terms and preponderant opinion, specific to the wording-based classification.

The Hanafi Definition of Mu'awwal (Interpreted Text)
Commentary defining mu'awwal and addressing two objections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define mu'awwal in Hanafi usul, distinguish it from tafsir, and apply the definition to examples of mushtarak words.

Core Idea
Mu'awwal is a mushtarak word whose meaning is chosen by predominant opinion, not definitive proof.

In Hanafi usul, words are classified as khas, 'amm, mushtarak, and mu'awwal. The commentator (sharih) defines mu'awwal and defends it against two objections. Understanding this definition is crucial to grasp how speculative interpretation (ta'wil) works in deriving rulings from ambiguous texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Four Categories of Words
Recognize that Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi divides words into four types based on form and meaning: khas, 'amm, mushtarak, and mu'awwal. The matn only mentioned three, but the commentator adds mu'awwal.
2
State the Definition of Mu'awwal
Mu'awwal is a mushtarak word where one of its multiple meanings is given preference over others based on predominant opinion (ghalib al-ra'y). The preferred meaning is the mu'awwal.
3
Analyze the First Objection
The first objection claims mu'awwal is not limited to mushtarak because khafi and mushkil words can also become mu'awwal. The response is that the definition is specific to the division based on sigha wa lugha, not absolute mu'awwal.
Other types of mu'awwal belong to a different classification.
4
Analyze the Second Objection
The second objection questions whether predominant opinion is the only preponderating factor, since khabar wahid, qiyas, or reflection on wording also serve. The response is that 'predominant opinion' here means zann ghalib, which encompasses all these factors.
5
Distinguish Ta'wil from Tafsir
If the preference is based on definitive proof (dalil qat'i), it becomes tafsir, not ta'wil. Mu'awwal always involves speculative evidence.

ماتن نے دو مثالیں دے کر نوع کے عموم کی طرف اشارہ کر دیا کہ نوع عرف شرع میں نوع منطقی سے اہم ہے۔ قولہ ثم المشترک:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا پہلا حصہ ہے غرض شارخ موول کی تعریف کرنا ہے نظم کی با عتبار صیغہ اور لغت کے فخر الاسلام کے ہاں چار قسمیں ہیں خاص و عام اور مشترک و موول لیکن ماتن نے موول کا تذکرہ نہیں کیا اور شارخ موول کی تعریف کرتے ہیں موقول کی تعریف یہ ہے کہ مشترک کے معانی میں سے کسی معنی کو ترجیح دے دینا غالب رائے سے جس کو ترجیح دی گئی ہے وہ موول ہے۔
و اور و علیہ:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے یہاں سے شارع موول کی تعریف پر دو اعتراض کرتے ہیں۔ اعتراض (۱):۔ آپ نے موصول کی تعریف میں دو قید میں لگائیں ہیں پہلی قید کہ مشترک کے معانی میں سے کسی معنی کو تر جیح دیں اور دوسری قید کہ غالب رائے سے ترجیح دیں یہ قیدمیں درست نہیں ہیں کیونکہ موول کی بعض قسمیں مشترک ساتھ خاص نہیں ہیں جیسے خفی مشکل وغیرہ اگر خبر واحد یا قیاس وغیرہ ان کا بیان واقع ہوں اور خفا دور ہو جائے تو یہ بھی مؤول ہیں تو مشترک کے ساتھ موول کو خاص کرنا درست نہیں ہے۔ اور اس کی تائید میزان نامی کتاب سے ہوتی ہے اس میں مذکور ہے کہ اگر فی مشکل مجمل مشترک کو دلیل قطعی سے بیان لاحق ہو تو فی ان کو مفسر کہینگے اور اگر بیان دلیل ظنی (قیاس خبر واحد ) وغیرہ سے لاحق ہو تو اس کو موول کہیں گے۔
اعتراض (۲):۔ دوسری قید تھی غالب رائے کی کہ غالب رائے کو آپ نے مرجح قرار دیا حالانکہ غالب رائے کو مرجح قرار دینا درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ مربح غالب رائے کے علاوہ بھی ہیں مثلا خبر واحد یا قیاس یا نفس صیغہ میں غور و فکر کرنا جیسا کہ لفظ قروء میں تامل نی نفس الصیفہ ہے۔ کہ قردہ قرہ کی جمع ہے اور اس کا لغوی معنی اجتماع ہے اسی وجہ سے قراءت کو قراءت کہتے ہیں کہ اس میں اجتماع حروف و کلمات پایا جاتا ہے تو مناسب ہے کہ قرء سے مراد حیض ہو کیونکہ حیض رحم میں ایام حیض میں جمع ہوتا ہے ایام اطہار میں نہیں ۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔ جواب عن الاول :۔ پہلے اعتراض کا جواب یہ ہے کہ فخر الاسلام نے جو تعریف کی ہے یہ مطلق مؤوّل کی نہیں ہے بلکہ مؤوّل کی تعریف ہے جو مشترک سے حاصل ہوتا ہے کیونکہ یہ تقسیم صیغہ اور لغت کے اعتبار سے ہے اور یہی موول جو مشترک کے ساتھ خاص ہے اس تقسیم کی قسم ہے اور باقی دوسرے جو موول میں (خفی مشکل وغیرہ ) وہ اس تقسیم کے اقسام نہیں ہیں جو
تقسیم صیغہ اور لغت کے اعتبار سے ہے۔ اس لئے مشترک کی قید لگائی تا کہ یہ صیغہ ولفت نظم کی قسم بن سکے۔
جواب عن الثانی :۔ دوسرے اعتراض کا جواب یہ ہے غالب رائے سے مراد ظن غالب ہے اور ظن غالب کبھی خبر واحد سے اور کبھی غالب رائے سے اور کبھی قیاس سے حاصل ہوتا ہے خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ جتنے مرجح ہیں ظن غالب سب کو شامل ہے۔ و معنی کونہ:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا تیسرا حصہ ہے غرض شاریخ سوال مقدر کا جواب دینا ہے۔ سوال:۔ آپ نے کہا کہ مودل اس مشترک کو کہتے ہیں کہ جس میں غالب رائے سے ایک معنی کو ترجیح دیں دوسرے معانی سے
جب اس میں رائے کو دخل ہے تو یہ مؤول الفاظ کی قسم تو نہ ہوئی بلکہ مجتہد کی رائے سے اس کا تعلق ہے تو یہ صیغہ کی قسم کیسے ہوا ؟ جواب:۔ غالب رائے سے جو حکم حاصل ہوتا ہے وہ حکم لفظ کی طرف اور صیغہ کی طرف منسوب ہوتا ہے اس منسوب ہونے کے اعتبار سے مالا یہ نظم کی قسم ہے۔ وقیل المراد سے اوپر والے دوسرے اعتراض کا دوسرا جواب دیا کہ غالب رائے سے مراد صیغہ میں غور و فکر کرتا ہے جب صیغہ میں غور و فکر کریں گے تو استدلال کریں گے اور استدلال کبھی مقتل [؟] سے اور کبھی خبر واحد سے ہوتا ہے تو اس اعتبار سے مرجع عام ہے۔
وقید بالاشتراک:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا چوتھا حصہ ہے غرض سوال مقدر کا جواب دینا ہے۔ سوال : فخر الاسلام نے موقول کی تعریف میں دو قید میں لگائیں ہیں (۱) مؤوّل مشترک سے حاصل ہو (۲) ترجیح غالب رائے سے ہو یہ دو قید میں کیوں ذکر کی ہیں؟
جواب:۔ باقی اقسام چونکہ نظم کی قسمیں ہیں تو یہ قید میں اس لئے لگا ئیں تا کہ موول بھی نظم کی قسم بن جائے ہاں جب یہ دونوں
قید میں نہ ہوں تو پھر نظم کی تمیں بنا ضروری نہیں ہے کبھی نظم کی تمیں ہوں گی کبھی نہ ہوں گی۔ فان المشترک :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا پانچواں حصہ ہے غرض یہ ہے کہ یہاں سے دلیل بیان کی ہے کہ اشتراک کی قید
سے موول نظم کی قسم کیسے بنے گا؟ کہ مشترک اس لفظ کو کہتے ہیں جو معانی متعددہ کے لئے وضع کیا گیا ہو اور جب کئی معافی کے لئے لفظ وضع کیا گیا ہو تو مشترک ہے اب اجتہاد کے ذریعہ ایک معنی کومنتخب کریں گے تو جو ایک معنی منتخب ہوگا وہ بھی لفظ کی تم ہو گا بخلاف اس کے کہ اگر بعض معانی کو تر جیح کسی دوسری دلیل قطعی سے ہو تو اس کو تاویل نہیں کہتے بلکہ تفسیر کے لئے نہیں ہیں اور اگر ترجیح خبر واحد یا قیاس سے ہو تو بیان اقسام سے خارج ہو جائے گا جو ہا عتبار نظم کے میسہ ولعہ ہیں اور اسی طرح اگر وہ مشترک
The author (matn) indicated the generality of type by giving two examples, that the type in the custom of the Law is more important than the logical type. His statement: 'then the common (mushtarak)': This is the first part of the commentary's expression; the purpose is that the commentator defines mu'awwal. According to Fakhr al-Islam, there are four types of words based on form and meaning: specific (khas), general (amm), common (mushtarak), and interpreted (mu'awwal). But the matn did not mention mu'awwal, and the commentator defines mu'awwal: it is giving preference to one meaning among the meanings of a mushtarak by predominant opinion; what is given preference is mu'awwal. 'And upon it': This is the second part of the commentary; from here the commentator raises two objections to the definition of mu'awwal. Objection (1): You place two restrictions in the definition: first, that it is from the meanings of a mushtarak, and second, that preference is by predominant opinion. These restrictions are not correct because some types of mu'awwal are not specific to mushtarak, such as khafi and mushkil; if khabar wahid or qiyas etc. clarify them and the obscurity is removed, then these are also mu'awwal. So restricting mu'awwal to mushtarak is not correct. This is supported by the book Mizan: it mentions that if a difficult, mujmal, mushtarak text is clarified by definitive proof, then it is called mufassar; if clarified by speculative proof (qiyas, khabar wahid), then it is called mu'awwal. Objection (2): The second restriction is predominant opinion; you made predominant opinion the preponderating factor, but it is not correct because preponderators are other than predominant opinion, e.g., khabar wahid, qiyas, or reflection on the wording itself, as in the word 'quru' (menstrual periods); careful reflection is on the wording itself; 'quru' is the plural of 'qar' and its lexical meaning is 'gathering', therefore 'qira'ah' is called 'qira'ah' because it involves gathering of letters and words; so it is appropriate that 'qar' means menstruation because blood gathers in the womb during menses, not during purity. And Allah knows best. Response to the first: The response to the first objection is that Fakhr al-Islam's definition is not of absolute mu'awwal, but of mu'awwal that is derived from mushtarak, because this division is based on wording and meaning, and this mu'awwal specific to mushtarak is a type of this division; other mu'awwals (like khafi, mushkil) are not types of this division that is based on wording and meaning. Therefore the restriction of mushtarak was made so that this becomes a type of word form. Response to the second: The response to the second objection is that 'predominant opinion' means 'predominant conjecture', and predominant conjecture is sometimes obtained from khabar wahid, sometimes from predominant opinion itself, and sometimes from qiyas; in summary, all preponderators are included in predominant conjecture. 'And the meaning of its being': This is the third part of the commentary; the purpose is to answer an implicit question. Question: You said that mu'awwal is a mushtarak to which one meaning is preferred over others by predominant opinion; since opinion enters into it, it is not a type of word but related to the ijtihad of the mujtahid; so how is it a type of word form? Answer: The ruling obtained by predominant opinion is attributed to the word and the form; by virtue of this attribution, it is a type of word form. 'And it was said that the meaning' provides a second answer to the second objection: that 'predominant opinion' means reflection on the wording; when one reflects on the wording, one engages in deduction; deduction is sometimes from textual evidence (naql) and sometimes from khabar wahid; so in this sense the reference is general. 'And he restricted it to sharing (ishtirak)': This is the fourth part of the commentary; the purpose is to answer an implicit question. Question: Why did Fakhr al-Islam mention two restrictions: (1) mu'awwal is derived from mushtarak, (2) preference is by predominant opinion? Answer: Because other types are already types of word form, so these restrictions were made so that mu'awwal also becomes a type of word form. Yes, when these two restrictions are not present, then it is not necessarily a type of word form; sometimes it is, sometimes not. 'For mushtarak': This is the fifth part of the commentary; the purpose is to explain how the restriction of ishtirak makes mu'awwal a type of word form. Mushtarak is a word coined for multiple meanings; when it is coined for several meanings, it is mushtarak. Then through ijtihad one selects one meaning; that selected meaning is also from the word, unlike if preference is given by some other definitive proof, then it is not called ta'wil but rather tafsir; and if preference is by khabar wahid or qiyas, then it falls outside the types that are considered word forms. Similarly, if that mushtarak...
Source pages p. 517

Commentary
This passage is a commentary expanding on the definition of mu'awwal (interpreted text) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author (sharih) begins by stating that the original matn (al-Tawdih) only mentioned three types of words: khas, 'amm, and mushtarak, but Fakhr al-Islam (al-Bazdawi) added a fourth: mu'awwal. The sharih defines mu'awwal as a mushtarak word where one meaning is preferred over others based on predominant opinion (ghalib al-ra'y). Two objections are then raised against this definition. The first objection argues that mu'awwal is not limited to mushtarak, because khafi and mushkil words can also become mu'awwal when clarified by speculative evidence. The sharih responds that this definition is specifically for the division based on wording and meaning (sigha wa lugha), and other types of mu'awwal belong to a different classification. The second objection questions the use of predominant opinion as the sole preponderating factor, since other factors like khabar wahid, qiyas, or reflection on the wording can also be preponderators. The sharih clarifies that 'predominant opinion' here encompasses all these, as it means 'predominant conjecture' (zann ghalib), which can arise from various sources. The commentary then addresses an implicit question: if mu'awwal depends on opinion, how can it be a type of word form? The answer is that the ruling is attributed to the word itself. Finally, the sharih explains why both restrictions (mushtarak and predominant opinion) are necessary: to ensure that mu'awwal becomes a distinct type of word form within the sigha/lugha division. The passage emphasizes that if interpretation is based on definitive proof, it is tafsir, not ta'wil.

Key Terms
مؤول (mu'awwal): A mushtarak word to which one meaning is preferred over others based on predominant opinion (ghalib al-ra'y).
مشترک (mushtarak): A word coined for multiple meanings (homonym). It is one of the four categories of words in this Hanafi classification.
غالب رائے (ghalib al-ra'y): Predominant opinion or preponderant conjecture (zann ghalib), which includes various preponderating factors such as khabar wahid, qiyas, or reflection on the wording.
تاویل (ta'wil): Interpretation of a word when there is no definitive proof; it is the process of preferring one meaning based on speculative evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary difference between tafsir and ta'wil?
A) Tafsir is based on definitive proof, while ta'wil is based on speculative evidence.
B) Tafsir applies only to mushtarak words, while ta'wil applies to any word.
C) Tafsir is a type of mu'awwal, while ta'wil is a type of khas.
D) There is no difference; they are synonyms.

Key Takeaway
Mu'awwal is a mushtarak word whose meaning is determined by predominant opinion (zann ghalib), and it is a distinct category of word form in Hanafi usul.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
Mu'awwal: Definition and Its Status as Nazm
Explaining the definition of mu'awwal as part of nazm through objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define mu'awwal according to Hanafi usul, explain why it is classified as nazm despite involving dominant opinion, and identify its two conditions.

Core Idea
A mu'awwal is a mushtarak word where meaning is chosen by dominant opinion, yet the ruling is attributed to the word itself.

The Hanafi usul tradition categorises texts by clarity. One category, mu'awwal (interpreted text), seems to rely on the mujtahid's opinion rather than the word itself. This passage resolves that tension by showing how the ruling remains attributed to the word, making mu'awwal a genuine part of the verbal hierarchy (nazm). Understanding this definition helps you see how Hanafi jurists maintain textual grounding even when interpretation involves ijtihad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition with two restrictions
Find in the text the two conditions (qayd) placed by Fakhr al-Islam: the word must be mushtarak (common), and preference must be by dominant opinion (ghalib ra'y). These are necessary for mu'awwal to be a type of nazm.
Without both, the result may be ta'wil in a broader sense but not mu'awwal in the technical nazm sense.
2
Understand the objection: opinion vs. verbal form
The implied objection: if mu'awwal depends on the mujtahid's opinion, how can it be considered a property of the word (siyah)? The answer is that the ruling reached by dominant opinion is attributed to the word, not to the opinion itself.
This attribution is crucial: it keeps the textual hierarchy intact.
3
Analyse the response on dominant opinion
Dominant opinion (zann ghalib) comes from various sources: khabar wahid, qiyas, or reflection in the siyah. The murajjih (preferrer) is general; the ruling is always linked to the word's form.
Thus, mu'awwal is not a creation of the mujtahid's mind but a determined interpretation of the text.
4
Recognise why the second restriction is needed
The second restriction (mushtarak) ensures that the word genuinely carries multiple meanings; otherwise, the interpretation would not involve preference among equal possibilities, and mu'awwal would not be a distinct category within nazm.
If the word is not mushtarak but ambiguous (e.g., khafi, mujmal), preference by zanni proof leads to a different kind of ta'wil.
5
Distinguish mu'awwal from other ta'wil
The text clarifies that ta'wil has two meanings: one within the wad' (linguistic coinage) categories – this is mu'awwal as part of nazm; the other is removing ambiguity from difficult texts using zanni proof – this is broader and not part of the first division.
Only mu'awwal with both restrictions fits into the verbal hierarchy.

مؤول کی تعریف میں دو قید میں لگائیں ہیں (۱) مؤوّل مشترک سے حاصل ہو (۲) ترجیح غالب رائے سے ہو یہ دو قید میں کیوں ذکر کی ہیں؟ جواب:۔ باقی اقسام چونکہ نظم کی قسمیں ہیں تو یہ قید میں اس لئے لگا ئیں تا کہ مؤول بھی نظم کی قسم بن جائے ہاں جب یہ دونوں قید میں نہ ہوں تو پھر نظم کی تمیں بنا ضروری نہیں ہے کبھی نظم کی تمیں ہوں گی کبھی نہ ہوں گی۔ فان المشترک :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا پانچواں حصہ ہے غرض یہ ہے کہ یہاں سے دلیل بیان کی ہے کہ اشتراک کی قید سے مؤول نظم کی قسم کیسے بنے گا؟ کہ مشترک اس لفظ کو کہتے ہیں جو معانی متعددہ کے لئے وضع کیا گیا ہو اور جب کئی معافی کے لئے لفظ وضع کیا گیا ہو تو مشترک ہے اب اجتہاد کے ذریعہ ایک معنی کومنتخب کریں گے تو جو ایک معنی منتخب ہوگا وہ بھی لفظ کی تم ہو گا بخلاف اس کے کہ اگر بعض معانی کو تر جیح کسی دوسری دلیل قطعی سے ہو تو اس کو تاویل نہیں کہتے بلکہ تفسیر کے لئے نہیں ہیں اور اگر ترجیح خبر واحد یا قیاس سے ہو تو بیان اقسام سے خارج ہو جائے گا جو ہا عتبار نظم کے میسہ ولعہ ہیں اور اسی طرح اگر وہ مشترک سے حاصل نہیں ہوگا بلکہ خفی مجمل مشکل تو پھر بھی اگر ترجیح دلیل قطعی سے ہوگی تو یہ غیر ہوگی تاویل نہ ہوگی اور اگر ترجیح دلیل فنی سے ہوگی تو یہ اگر چہ تاویل ہی ہوگی لیکن وہ موول نہیں جو نظم کے اقسام سے صیغہ ولغتہ کے اعتبار سے ہوتے ہیں کیونکہ تاویل کے دو معنی آتے ہیں ایک وہ جو وضع کے اقسام سے ہے یہ تاویل اس مؤول میں جاری ہوتی ہے جو نظم کی اقسام میں سے ہے اور دوسرا معنی تاویل کا دلیل ظنی کے ساتھ خفی ، مشکل، مجمل وغیرہ سے خفا کا ازالہ کرنا یہ تاویل تقسیم اول کی اقسام سے نہیں ہے خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ مؤول کے لئے دو شرطیں ہیں۔
Answer to the second: The second objection's answer is that 'ghalib ra'y' means dominant conjecture (zann ghalib), and dominant conjecture is sometimes obtained from khabar wahid, sometimes from ghalib ra'y, and sometimes from qiyas. Summary: All preferences (murajjih) are included in dominant conjecture. 'Wa ma'na kunnah': This is the third part of the sharh's phrase. The commentator aims to answer an assumed question. Question: You said that mu'awwal is the common word (mushtarak) in which one meaning is given preference over other meanings by dominant opinion. Since opinion is involved, this mu'awwal is not a type of words, but rather related to the mujtahid's opinion. How then is it a type of siyah (form)? Answer: The ruling obtained by dominant opinion is attributed to the word and to the siyah. By virtue of this attribution, mu'awwal is a type of nazm. 'Wa qeel al-murad': The second answer to the second objection above is given: what is meant by dominant opinion is reflection (ghaur wa fikr) in the siyah. When they reflect in the siyah, they will perform istidlal, and istidlal sometimes occurs from naql and sometimes from khabar wahid. From this aspect, the murajjih is general. 'Wa qayyada bil-ishtirak': This is the fourth part of the sharh's phrase. The purpose is to answer an assumed question. Question: Fakhr al-Islam placed two restrictions in the definition of mu'awwal: (1) it is obtained from a common word (mushtarak), and (2) preference is by dominant opinion. Why are these two restrictions mentioned? Answer: Since the remaining categories are types of nazm, they placed these restrictions so that mu'awwal also becomes a type of nazm. If these two restrictions are not present, then it is not necessarily a type of nazm; sometimes it will be a type of nazm, sometimes not. 'Fa'inna al-mushtarak': This is the fifth part of the sharh's phrase. The purpose is to present a proof that through the restriction of ishtirak, mu'awwal becomes a type of nazm. The common word (mushtarak) is defined as a word placed for multiple meanings. When a word is placed for several meanings, it is common. Now through ijtihad one meaning is selected. The selected meaning will also be a type of word. This is unlike if preference of some meanings is by another definitive proof (dalil qata'i), then it is not called ta'wil but rather tafsir. And if preference is by khabar wahid or qiyas, then it falls outside the categories that are considered from nazm from the aspect of siyah and lughah. Similarly, if it is not obtained from a common word but from khafi, mujmal, mushkil, then if preference is by definitive proof, it is not ta'wil. And if preference is by zanni proof, then although it is ta'wil, it is not that mu'awwal which is from the categories of nazm from the aspect of siyah and lughah, because ta'wil has two meanings: one is from the categories of wad' (linguistic coinage) — this ta'wil applies to mu'awwal that is from the categories of nazm; the second meaning of ta'wil is removing ambiguity from khafi, mushkil, mujmal etc. by zanni proof. This ta'wil is not from the categories of the first division. Summary: Mu'awwal has two conditions.
Source pages p. 518

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the definition of mu'awwal (interpreted text) and its classification under nazm (structure/verbal form). The commentator addresses two objections raised against the definition by Fakhr al-Islam. The first objection concerns the role of dominant opinion (ghalib ra'y) in reaching the interpretation, questioning how mu'awwal can be considered a type of verbal form (siyah) when opinion seems to be external. The answer shows that the ruling from dominant opinion is attributed to the word, so mu'awwal remains a verbal category. The second objection asks why two restrictions (mashtarak and dominant opinion) are necessary. The reply explains that these restrictions ensure mu'awwal forms part of nazm; without them, it may or may not be. The discussion further clarifies that only when the word is mushtarak and preference is by dominant opinion does the result qualify as mu'awwal in the nazm sense. If the word is ambiguous (khafi, mujmal, mushkil) and preference is via zanni proof, it is ta'wil in a broader sense but not the specific mu'awwal under nazm.

Key Terms
مؤول (mu'awwal): A word that is common (mushtarak) and one meaning is given preference over others by dominant opinion (ghalib ra'y), thereby being classified as a type of nazm (verbal form).
ظن غالب (zann ghalib): Dominant conjecture; a strong probability that is not certainty, obtained through various means such as khabar wahid, qiyas, or preference (tarjih).
نظم (nazm): The structure or form of the wording; a category that includes clear and interpreted expressions in the hierarchy of textual clarity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary reason that mu'awwal is considered a type of nazm despite relying on the mujtahid's opinion?
A) The opinion is derived from ijma' which makes it certain.
B) The resulting ruling is attributed to the word, not to the opinion.
C) The opinion is actually a type of revelation (wahy).
D) The word itself is considered definitive (qat'i).

Key Takeaway
Mu'awwal is a mushtarak word whose preferred meaning, chosen by dominant opinion, is attributed to the word itself, making it a valid category of nazm.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
Hanafi Noun Classification in Usul al-Fiqh
Systematic classification of nouns based on meaning and definiteness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any given noun into the Hanafi usul categories (sifah, alam, ism jins; mutlaq, muqayyad; amm, ma'hood; nakira, ma'rifa) and explain the basis for each classification, particularly the distinction between nakira and ma'rifa based on the listener's knowledge at utterance.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, a noun's definiteness is determined by the listener's knowledge at utterance, not coinage — this defines nakira vs ma'rifa.

This passage lays the foundational taxonomy of nouns used throughout Hanafi usul al-fiqh to interpret legal texts. Understanding this classification is essential because the categorical status of a noun directly affects how a legal ruling is derived. The author systematically branches from 'ism zahir' into derived types, then into levels of restriction, generality, and definiteness, culminating in the critical definition of nakira and ma'rifa relative to the listener's knowledge at the time of utterance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base noun type
Begin with the general category 'ism zahir' (apparent noun) which excludes pronouns. All further classifications apply to this base.
Ism zahir is the starting point for the taxonomy.
2
Apply the first division: Sifah vs. Alam vs. Ism Jins
If the noun's meaning equals the meaning of its derived root (mushtaqq) and matches its verbal weight, it is a sifah (adjective). Otherwise, if it designates a specific individual, it is an alam (proper noun). If neither, it is an ism jins (common noun).
E.g., 'qatil' is sifah (derived from qatala), 'Zayd' is alam, 'rajul' is ism jins.
3
Classify sifah/ism jins as Mutlaq or Muqayyad
If the designated meaning (musamma) is intended without any restriction, it is mutlaq; if with a restriction, it is muqayyad.
Example: 'raqabah' (neck/slave) mutlaq vs 'raqabah mu'minah' (believing slave) muqayyad.
4
Determine Generality and Definiteness
From sifah/ism jins, further classify: if covering all individuals of the type, it is 'amm (general); if some specific individuals known from context, it is ma'hood (specified); if indefinite, it is nakira; if definite, it is ma'rifa. The key nuance: nakira indicates 'a thing not specific at utterance for the listener', while ma'rifa indicates 'a specific thing at utterance for the listener'.
This is not about coinage (wad'), but about the listener's knowledge at the time of utterance.
5
Understand the status of Mutlaq as Khas
The text explicitly states that mutlaq is a type of khas (specific) because it refers to a single individual of the type (al-wahid al-naw'i). This is a distinct Hanafi position.
Mutlaq is not general ('amm); it points to one unspecified individual.

Source Text

ثُمَّ هَهُنَا تَقْسِيمْ آخَرُ لَا بُدَّ مِنْ مَعْرِفَتِهِ وَمَعْرِفَةِ الْأَقْسَامِ الَّتِي تَحْصُلُ مِنْهُ وَهُوَ هَذَا ( وَأَيْضًا الاسْمُ الظَّاهِرُ إِنْ كَانَ مَعْنَاهُ عَيْنَ مَا وُضِعَ لَهُ الْمُشْتَقُ مِنْهُ مَعَ وَزْنِ الْمُشْتَقْ فَصِفَةٌ وَإِلَّا فَإِنْ تَشَحْصَ مَعْنَاهُ فَعَلَمٌ وَإِلَّا فَاسْمُ جِنْسِ وَهُمَا إِمَّا مُشْتَقَانِ أَوْ لَا ثُمَّ كُلٌّ مِنَ الصَّفَةِ وَاسْمِ الْجِنْسِ إِنْ أُرِيدَ الْمُسَمَّى بِلَا قَيْدٍ فَمُطْلَقٌ أَوْ مَعَهُ فَمُقَيَّدٌ أَوْ أَشْخَاصَهُ كُلُّهَا فَعَامٌ أَوْ بَعْضُهَا مُعَيَّنًا فَمَعُهُودٌ أَوْ مُنَكَرًا فَنَكِرَةٌ فَهِيَ مَا وُضِعَ لِشَيْءٍ لَا بِعَيْنِهِ عِندَ الْإِطْلَاقِ لِلسَّامِعِ وَالْمَعْرِفَةُ مَا وُضِعَ لِمُعَيَّنٍ عِنْدَ الْإِطْلَاقِ لَهُ ) أى لِلسَّامِعِ ، وَإِنَّمَا قُلْت عِندَ الإطلاقِ إِذْ لَا فَرْقَ بَيْنَ الْمَعْرِفَةِ وَالنَّكِرَةِ فِي التَّعْيِينِ وَعَدَمِ التَّعْيِينِ عِندَ الْوَضْعِ ، وَإِنَّمَا قُلْت لِلسَّامِعِ ؛ لِأَنَّهُ إِذَا قَالَ جَاءَنِي رَجُلٌ يُمْكِنُ أَن يَكُونَ الرَّجُلُ مُتَعَيَّنَا لِلْمُتَكَلّم فَعُلِمَ مِنْ هَذَا التَّقْسِيمِ حَدُّ كُلّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْ الْأَقْسَامِ وَعُلِمَ أَنَّ الْمُطْلَقَ مِنْ أَقْسَامِ الْخَاصٌ ؛ لِأَنَّ الْمُطْلَقَ وُضِعَ لِلْوَاحِدِ النَّوْعِيُّ. وَاعْلَمُ أَنَّهُ يَجِبُ فِي كُلِّ قِسْمٍ مِنْ هَذِهِ الْأَقْسَامِ أَنْ يُعْتَبَرَ مِنْ حَيْثُ هُوَ كَذَلِكَ حَتَّى لَا يُتَوَهَّمَ التَّنَافِى بَيْنَ كُلِّ قِسْمٍ وَقِسْمٍ ، فَإِنَّ بَعْضَ الْأَقْسَامِ قَدْ يَجْتَمِعُ مَعَ بَعْضٍ وَبَعْضُهَا لَا ، مِثلُ قَوْلِنَا جَرَتْ الْعُيُونُ فَمِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّ الْعَيْنَ
Then here is another classification that must be known, and knowledge of the categories arising from it. And it is this: (Also, the apparent noun (ism zahir): if its meaning is exactly what the derived word (mushtaqq) is placed for, along with the weight (wazn) of the derived word, then it is an adjective (sifah). Otherwise, if its meaning is specific (tashakhkhus), then it is a proper noun (alam). Otherwise, it is a common noun (ism jins). Both (alam and ism jins) are either derived (mushtaqq) or not. Then, each of the adjective and common noun: if the designated meaning (musamma) is intended without a restriction, it is unrestricted (mutlaq); or with a restriction, then it is restricted (muqayyad); or all of its individuals, then it is general (amm); or some of them specific, then it is specified (ma'hood); or indefinite (munkar), then it is indefinite noun (nakira). So nakira is what is placed for a thing not as a specific thing at the time of utterance for the listener; and ma'rifa is what is placed for a specific thing at the time of utterance for him—i.e., for the listener. I only said 'at the time of utterance' because there is no difference between ma'rifa and nakira in specificity and non-specificity at the time of coinage (wad'). I only said 'for the listener' because if someone says 'Jaa'ani rajulun' (A man came to me), it is possible that the man is specific for the speaker. So from this classification, the definition of each category is known, and it is known that the unrestricted (mutlaq) is among the categories of the specific (khas), because the mutlaq is placed for the individual of the type (al-wahid al-naw'i). And know that it is necessary for each category among these categories to be considered from its own perspective so that contradiction between categories is not imagined. Indeed, some categories may combine with others, and some may not, like when we say 'jarat al-'uyun' (the eyes flowed)—from the aspect that 'al-'ayn'...
Source pages p. 519

Commentary
This passage presents a systematic classification of nouns (asma) in usul al-fiqh, crucial for understanding textual indications. It starts from the 'ism zahir' (apparent noun) and branches into types based on meaning and derivation. The first division: if the noun's meaning is precisely that of its derived root with its verbal weight, it is a sifat (adjective) like 'qatil' from 'qatala'. If the meaning is a specific entity, it is an alam (proper noun) like 'Zayd'. Otherwise, it is an ism jins (common noun) like 'rajul'. Then higher-level categories: mutlaq (unrestricted) vs. muqayyad (restricted) based on whether a qualification is attached; 'amm (general) vs. ma'hood (specific by prior knowledge) vs. nakira (indefinite) vs. ma'rifa (definite). The definitions of nakira and ma'rifa are given with the nuance of the listener's knowledge at the time of utterance, not at coinage. The example 'rajul' could be specific for the speaker. The text also notes that mutlaq is a type of khas (specific) because it refers to a single individual of the type. Finally, it warns about avoiding contradiction by considering each category from its specific perspective.

Key Terms
اسم ظاهر (ism zahir): An apparent noun that is not a pronoun; it is the starting point of this classification.
صفة (sifah): An adjective derived from a verb (mushtaqq) that shares its meaning and weight, e.g., 'qatil' from 'qatala'.
علم (alam): A proper noun that is specific in meaning, e.g., 'Zayd'.
اسم جنس (ism jins): A common noun that is neither an adjective nor a proper noun, e.g., 'rajul'.
مطلق (mutlaq): Unrestricted; a noun that is not qualified by a condition, indicating any individual of the type.
مقيد (muqayyad): Restricted; a noun that is qualified by a condition or description.
عام (amm): General; a noun that covers all individuals of its category.
معہود (ma'hood): A noun referring to a specific known individual(s) but not all, e.g., 'al-rajul' (the man) if previously mentioned.
نكرة (nakira): Indefinite noun; placed for a thing not as a specific thing at the time of utterance for the listener.
معرفة (ma'rifa): Definite noun; placed for a specific thing at the time of utterance for the listener.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the classification in the text, 'rajul' (man) without any qualification is an example of which category?
A) Sifah (adjective)
B) Alam (proper noun)
C) Ism jins (common noun)
D) Ma'rifa (definite noun)

Key Takeaway
The classification of nouns in Hanafi usul proceeds from apparent noun to derived types, then to degrees of restriction and definiteness, with nakira and ma'rifa defined relative to the listener's knowledge at the time of utterance.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

Primary Classification of Al-Ism Al-Zahir: Sifah, Alam, and Ism Jins
Classifying apparent nouns into three categories based on derivation and specificity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and classify an apparent noun as a descriptive adjective (ṣifah), a proper name (ʿalam), or a genus noun (ism jins) according to the Hanafi uṣūl criteria.

Core Idea
An apparent noun is ṣifah if its meaning matches its derivative pattern; otherwise, if specified, it is ʿalam; if unspecific, it is ism jins.

This lesson introduces the foundational classification of apparent nouns (al-ism al-ẓāhir) in Hanafi uṣūl al-fiqh. Understanding whether a word functions as a descriptive adjective, a proper name, or a genus noun is essential for correctly interpreting legal texts, especially when deriving rulings (aḥkām) from the Qur'an and Sunnah. The author of Al-Tarweeh provides clear criteria based on the word's meaning and its relation to a derivative.

Guided Path
1
Identify the word as an ism ẓāhir
First, confirm that the word is an apparent noun (al-ism al-ẓāhir), meaning it is not a pronoun or hidden noun. Most Arabic nouns are ẓāhir.
2
Check if its meaning exactly matches the meaning of its derivative (mushtaqq minhu) and its pattern (wazn)
If the word's meaning is identical to what the verb or root it is derived from indicates, and it follows the pattern of active participle (fāʿil), passive participle (mafʿūl), etc., then it is a ṣifah. Example: 'ḍārib' (hitter) from 'ḍaraba' (to hit).
If the word is derived but its meaning has shifted, it may not be ṣifah.
3
If not ṣifah, check if its meaning is specified (mutashakhkhiṣ)
If the word refers to a specific individual entity that is not general, it is a proper name (ʿalam). Example: 'Makkah' refers to a specific city.
4
If not ṣifah nor ʿalam, classify it as ism jins
If the word refers to a non-specific generic entity, it is a genus noun (ism jins). Example: 'rajul' (man) refers to the genus of men, not a specific man.
5
Note that both ṣifah and ism jins may be derived or non-derived
The author adds that both ṣifah and ism jins can be either derived from a root or not. For example, 'rajul' is not derived, while 'ḍārib' is derived. This does not affect the primary classification.

وَأَيْضًا الاسْمُ الظَّاهِرُ إِنْ كَانَ مَعْنَاهُ عَيْنَ مَا وُضِعَ لَهُ الْمُشْتَقُ مِنْهُ مَعَ وَزْنِ الْمُشْتَقْ فَصِفَةٌ وَإِلَّا فَإِنْ تَشَخَّصَ مَعْنَاهُ فَعَلَمٌ وَإِلَّا فَاسْمُ جِنْسٍ وَهُمَا إِمَّا مُشْتَقَّانِ أَوْ لَا ثُمَّ كُلٌّ مِنَ الصَّفَةِ وَاسْمِ الْجِنْسِ إِنْ أُرِيدَ الْمُسَمَّى بِلَا قَيْدٍ فَمُطْلَقٌ أَوْ مَعَهُ فَمُقَيَّدٌ أَوْ أَشْخَاصَهُ كُلَّهَا فَعَامٌ أَوْ بَعْضُهَا مُعَيَّنًا فَمَعْرِفَةٌ أَوْ مُنَكَرًا فَنَكِرَةٌ فَهِيَ مَا وُضِعَ لِشَيْءٍ لَا بِعَيْنِهِ عِنْدَ الْإِطْلَاقِ لِلسَّامِعِ وَالْمَعْرِفَةُ مَا وُضِعَ لِمُعَيَّنٍ عِنْدَ الْإِطْلَاقِ لَهُ) أَىْ لِلسَّامِعِ، وَإِنَّمَا قُلْتُ عِنْدَ الْإِطْلَاقِ إِذْ لَا فَرْقَ بَيْنَ الْمَعْرِفَةِ وَالنَّكِرَةِ فِي التَّعْيِينِ وَعَدَمِ التَّعْيِينِ عِنْدَ الْوَضْعِ، وَإِنَّمَا قُلْتُ لِلسَّامِعِ؛ لِأَنَّهُ إِذَا قَالَ جَاءَنِي رَجُلٌ يُمْكِنُ أَنْ يَكُونَ الرَّجُلُ مُتَعَيِّنًا لِلْمُتَكَلِّمِ. فَعُلِمَ مِنْ هَذَا التَّقْسِيمِ حَدُّ كُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنَ الْأَقْسَامِ وَعُلِمَ أَنَّ الْمُطْلَقَ مِنْ أَقْسَامِ الْخَاصِّ؛ لِأَنَّ الْمُطْلَقَ وُضِعَ لِلْوَاحِدِ النَّوْعِيِّ. وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّهُ يَجِبُ فِي كُلِّ قِسْمٍ مِنْ هَذِهِ الْأَقْسَامِ أَنْ يُعْتَبَرَ مِنْ حَيْثُ هُوَ كَذَلِكَ حَتَّى لَا يُتَوَهَّمَ التَّنَافِي بَيْنَ كُلِّ قِسْمٍ وَقِسْمٍ، فَإِنَّ بَعْضَ الْأَقْسَامِ قَدْ يَجْتَمِعُ مَعَ بَعْضٍ وَبَعْضُهَا لَا، مِثْلُ قَوْلِنَا جَرَتِ الْعُيُونُ فَمِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّ الْعَيْنَ وُضِعَتْ تَارَةً لِلْبَاصِرَةِ، وَتَارَةً لِعَيْنِ الْمَاءِ تَكُونُ الْعَيْنُ مُشْتَرَكَةً بِهَذِهِ الْحَيْثِيَّةِ وَمِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّ الْعُيُونَ شَامِلَةٌ لِأَفْرَادِ تِلْكَ الْحَقِيقَةِ، وَهِيَ عَيْنُ الْمَاءِ مَثَلًا تَكُونُ عَامَّةً بِهَذِهِ الْحَيْثِيَّةِ فَعُلِمَ أَنَّهُ لَا تَنَافِيَ بَيْنَ الْعَامِّ وَالْمُشْتَرَكِ لَكِنْ بَيْنَ الْعَامِّ وَالْخَاصِّ تَنَافٍ إِذْ لَا يُمْكِنُ أَنْ يَكُونَ اللَّفْظُ الْوَاحِدُ خَاصًا وَعَامًّا بِالْحَيْثِيَّتَيْنِ فَاعْتُبِرَ هَذَا فِي الْبَوَاقِي فَإِنَّهُ سَهْلٌ بَعْدَ الْوُقُوفِ عَلَى الْحُدُودِ الَّتِي ذَكَرْنَا.

پھر یہاں ایک دوسری تقسیم ہے ضروری ہے اس کی معرفت اور ان اقسام کی معرفت جو حاصل ہوتی ہیں اس سے اور وہ یہ ہیں (اور پھر اسم ظاہر اگر ہو اس کا معنی بعینہ مشتق منہ کے موضوع لہ والا وزن مشتق کے ساتھ پس صفت ہے وگرنہ پس اگر متعین ہو اس کا معنی تو علم ہے وگرنہ پس اسم جنس ہے اور وہ دونوں یا تو دونوں مشتق ہوں گے یا نہیں پھر صفت اور اسم جنس میں سے ہر ایک اگر مراد لیا جائے اس سے مفہوم بغیر قید کے تو وہ مطلق ہے قید کے ساتھ پس مقید ہے یا اس کے تمام افراد پس عام ہے یا بعض افراد مستعین پس معرفہ ہے یا غیر متعین پس نکرہ ہے پس نکرہ وہ ہے جس کو وضع کیا گیا ہو غیر معین کے لئے سامع کے لئے اطلاق کے وقت اور معرفہ وہ ہے جس کو وضع کیا گیا ہو معنی معین کے لئے اطلاق کے وقت اس کے لئے (یعنی سامع کے لئے) اور سوائے اس کے نہیں میں نے کہا اطلاق کے وقت کیوں کہ کوئی فرق نہیں ہے معرفہ اور نکرہ کے درمیان تعیین اور عدم تعیین میں وضع کے وقت۔ اور جز این نیست کہ میں نے کہا سامع کے لئے کیونکہ جب کہا جاءنی رجل ممکن ہے یہ کہ ہو آدمی متعین متکلم کے لئے۔ پس جان لی گئیں اس تقسیم سے اقسام میں سے ہر ایک کی تعریفیں۔ اور جان لیا گیا کہ بے شک مطلق خاص کی اقسام میں سے ہے کیونکہ مطلق کو وضع کیا گیا ہے واحد نوعی کے لیے۔ اور جان لو کہ بے شک واجب ہے ان اقسام میں سے ہر قسم میں یہ کہ اعتبار کیا جائے اس حیثیت سے کہ وہ اس طرح ہے تا کہ نہ وہم کیا جائے منافات کا ہر ہر قسم کے درمیان کیونکہ بعض اقسام کبھی جمع ہو جاتی ہیں بعض کے ساتھ اور بعض کے ساتھ نہیں جمع ہوتیں مثل ہمارے قول جرت العیون (چشمے بہہ پڑے) پس اس حیثیت سے کہ بے شک عین کو وضع کیا جاتا ہے کبھی قوت باصرہ کے لیے اور کبھی پانی کے چشمے کے لیے تو لفظ عین مشترک ہو گا اس حیثیت سے اور اس حیثیت سے کہ بے شک عیون شامل ہیں اس حقیقت کے تمام افراد کو اور وہ عین الماء بے مثال کے طور پر تو ہو گا وہ عام اس حیثیت سے پس معلوم ہوا کہ نہیں ہے منافات عام اور مشترک کے درمیان لیکن عام اور خاص کے درمیان منافات ہے کیونکہ نہیں ہے ممکن یہ ہے کہ ہو لفظ واحد خاص اور عام دو حیثیتوں کے ساتھ۔ پس اعتبار کیا جائے گا اس کا بواقی میں کیونکہ یہ آسان ہے۔ ان تعریفوں پر واقفیت کے بعد جن کو ہم نے ذکر کیا ہے۔
[Arabic:] Also, the apparent noun (al-ism al-zāhir): if its meaning is exactly what the derivative (mushtaqq minhu) was coined for, along with the pattern (wazn) of the derivative, then it is a descriptive adjective (ṣifah). Otherwise, if its meaning is specified (mutashakhkhiṣ), then it is a proper name ('alam). Otherwise, it is a genus noun (ism jins). These two (ṣifah and ism jins) are either derived or not. Then, each of the descriptive adjective and the genus noun: if what is intended is the named (musammā) without restriction (qayd), then it is absolute (muṭlaq); or with it, then it is restricted (muqayyad); or all of its individuals, then it is common/general ('āmm); or some of them specified, then it is definite (maʻrifah); or unspecified (munkaran), then it is indefinite (nakirah). So the indefinite (nakirah) is that which is coined for a thing not specified in itself at the time of utterance for the hearer, and the definite (maʻrifah) is that which is coined for a specified thing at the time of utterance for him (i.e., for the hearer). I only said 'at the time of utterance' because there is no difference between the definite and the indefinite in specification and non-specification at the time of coining. I only said 'for the hearer' because if one says 'jā'anī rajulun' (a man came to me), it is possible that the man is specified for the speaker. So from this division, the definition of each of the divisions is known, and it is known that the absolute is among the divisions of the specific (khāṣṣ) because the absolute is coined for the generic single (wāḥid nawʻī). Know that it is necessary for each division among these divisions to be considered from the aspect that it is such, so that contradiction is not imagined between each division and another. For some divisions may combine with others, and some do not. For example, our saying 'jarat al-ʻuyūn' (the springs/eyes flowed). From the aspect that ʻayn is coined sometimes for the seeing faculty (bāṣirah) and sometimes for the spring of water, the word ʻayn is homonymous (mushtarak) in this respect. And from the aspect that ʻuyūn includes all individuals of that reality, i.e., the spring of water, it is common (ʻāmm) in this respect. So it is known that there is no contradiction between the common and the homonymous, but there is contradiction between the common and the specific, because it is not possible for a single word to be specific and common from both aspects. So this is to be considered for the rest, for it is easy after understanding the definitions that we have mentioned.

[Urdu:] Then here there is another division, knowledge of it and knowledge of the divisions that are obtained from it are necessary, and they are these: (And if the apparent noun has its meaning exactly the meaning for which the derivative was coined along with the weight of the derivative, then it is a descriptive adjective; otherwise if its meaning is specified, then it is a proper name; otherwise it is a genus noun. And both are either derived or not. Then each of the descriptive adjective and genus noun: if the intended meaning is taken without restriction, then it is absolute; with restriction, then restricted; or all its individuals, then common; or some specified individuals, then definite; or unspecified, then indefinite. So the indefinite is that which is coined for something unspecified for the hearer at the time of utterance, and the definite is that which is coined for a specified meaning at the time of utterance for him (i.e., for the hearer). And I only said 'at the time of utterance' because there is no difference between definite and indefinite in specification and lack of specification at the time of coining. And I only said 'for the hearer' because when he says 'jā'anī rajul', it is possible that the man is specified for the speaker. Then from this division the definitions of each of the divisions are known. And it is known that indeed the absolute is from the divisions of the specific, because the absolute is coined for the generic single. And know that indeed it is necessary in each division among these divisions that consideration be given from the aspect that it is such, so that no contradiction is imagined between each division and another, because some divisions may combine with some and some do not combine, like our saying 'jarat al-ʻuyūn' (the springs flowed). So from the aspect that ʻayn is coined sometimes for the power of sight and sometimes for the spring of water, the word ʻayn will be homonymous in this aspect. And from the aspect that ʻuyūn includes all individuals of that reality, i.e., the spring of water by way of example, then it will be common in this aspect. So it is known there is no contradiction between the common and the homonymous, but there is contradiction between the common and the specific, because it is not possible for a single word to be specific and common from both aspects. So this will be considered in the rest, because it is easy after acquaintance with the definitions that we have mentioned.

Commentary
This passage from Altarweeh (a super-commentary on Al-Tawḍīḥ wa Al-Talwīḥ) presents a detailed classification of the apparent noun (al-ism al-ẓāhir) in Arabic, which is foundational for Hanafi uṣūl al-fiqh when interpreting legal texts. The author begins by dividing al-ism al-ẓāhir into three primary categories: descriptive adjective (ṣifah), proper name (ʿalam), and genus noun (ism jins). The distinction hinges on whether the word's meaning matches that of its derivative (e.g., 'wāḥid' from 'waḥḥada' is ṣifah) or is specified as a proper name. Then, both ṣifah and ism jins are further subdivided based on how they refer to their meanings: absolute (muṭlaq) if no restriction, restricted (muqayyad) if with a condition, common (ʿāmm) if covering all individuals, definite (maʿrifah) if a specific subset is intended, and indefinite (nakirah) if unspecified. The text emphasizes that the absolute belongs to the category of the specific (khāṣṣ) because it refers to a single generic entity. A key methodological point follows: each division must be considered from the aspect that makes it such, to avoid false contradictions. The example 'jarat al-ʿuyūn' illustrates this: 'ayn' is homonymous (mushtarak) in having multiple meanings, but the plural 'al-ʿuyūn' can be common (ʿāmm) when referring to all springs of water. Thus, common and homonymy are compatible, but common and specific are not, as a single word cannot be both from the same aspect. This lesson trains students to correctly categorize words in legal analysis, preventing misinterpretation.

Key Terms
صفة (ṣifah): A derivative noun whose meaning matches the meaning of its root and follows the pattern of a derived word (e.g., fāʿil, mafʿūl). It functions as a descriptive adjective.
علم (ʿalam): A proper name that refers to a specific individual (person, place, etc.) regardless of derivation.
اسم جنس (ism jins): A noun that refers to a generic category or genus, not a specific individual.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a proper name (ʿalam)? A) Kātib (writer) B) Baṣrah (city) C) Insān (human) D) Ṭayyib (good)
A) Kātib
B) Baṣrah
C) Insān
D) Ṭayyib

Key Takeaway
The primary classification of apparent nouns into ṣifah, ʿalam, and ism jins is determined by the criteria of derivative meaning and pattern (for ṣifah) and specification (for ʿalam); all three are essential for correctly analyzing legal language.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
10 min
Subdivisions of Sifah and Ism Jins: Mutlaq, Muqayyad, 'Amm, Ma'rifah, Nakirah
Classifying ṣifah/ism jins into muṭlaq/muqayyad/ʿāmm/maʿrifah/nakirah and explaining the aspect principle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between muṭlaq, muqayyad, ʿāmm, maʿrifah, and nakirah, and apply the principle of aspect-consideration (iʿtibār al-ḥaythiyyah) to avoid false contradictions between categories.

Core Idea
A word can be both ʿāmm and mushtarak when viewed from different aspects, but never both ʿāmm and khāṣṣ from the same aspect.

Building on the primary classification, the passage now divides ṣifah and ism jins into finer categories based on how they refer to their meanings: without restriction (muṭlaq), with restriction (muqayyad), covering all individuals (ʿāmm), or indicating a specific individual (maʿrifah) or non-specific (nakirah). A critical methodological point is made: each category must be considered from the aspect that makes it such, to avoid false contradictions. The classic example 'jarat al-ʿuyūn' (the springs/eyes flowed) demonstrates that ʿāmm and mushtarak are compatible, but ʿāmm and khāṣṣ are not.

Guided Path
1
Start with a ṣifah or ism jins word
After having classified the word as ṣifah or ism jins, now consider its reference. Ask: Is the named entity intended without any condition (qayd)? If yes, it is muṭlaq.
Example: 'rajul' (man) is muṭlaq when no condition is mentioned.
2
If a condition is present, it is muqayyad
If the word is accompanied by a restriction (e.g., 'rajul ʿālim'), then it is muqayyad.
3
If all individuals of the meaning are intended, it is ʿāmm
Ask: Does the word intend every single individual of that category? If yes, it is ʿāmm (general).
Example: 'al-nās' (the people) can be ʿāmm if meant inclusively.
4
If some specific individual(s) are intended, it is maʿrifah; if unspecified, nakirah
Maʿrifah is definite (e.g., proper name or definite noun), nakirah is indefinite. Note that the definiteness is from the hearer's perspective at the time of utterance.
Example: 'rajulun' (a man) is nakirah; 'al-rajulu' (the man) is maʿrifah.
5
Apply the aspect principle: consider each category from its own aspect
A single word may combine categories from different aspects. For example, 'al-ʿuyūn' (the springs) when meaning 'springs of water' includes all spring-water sources (ʿāmm from that aspect) but the word 'ʿayn' itself is homonymous (mushtarak) between 'spring' and 'eye'. These two aspects are not contradictory. However, a word cannot be both ʿāmm and khāṣṣ from the same aspect.
This prevents misinterpretation when a word seems to have dual nature.
