جواب (۱):۔ اصل میں مسنون طلاق وہ ہے جو طہر میں دی جائے اور ہم اسی کی بات کر رہے ہیں اور مسنون طلاق میں عدت تین حیض ہی بنتی ہے کم یا زیادہ نہیں بنتی کیونکہ جس طہر میں طلاق ہوگی اس کے متصل بعد والے تین حیض عدت شمار کر لیے جائیں گے۔
جواب (۲):- اگر حیض میں طلاق دی جائے تو بھی خاص (ثلثہ ) کے موجب میں کمی زیادتی لازم نہیں آتی کیونکہ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ جس حیض میں طلاق ہوتی ہے اس حیض کو عدت میں شمار کیا جائے گا لیکن مکمل نہیں بلکہ جتنا حیض باقی ہے اتنا ہی شمار کیا جائے گا اور جتنے ایام گزر چکے ہیں ان کو بعد میں پورا کیا جائے گا جس کی صورت یہ ہے کہ ان بقیہ ایام کے بعد عورت دو حیض مکمل گزارے گی اور اس کے بعد جو حیض آئے گا اس میں سے اتنے دن شمار کئے جائیں گے جتنے پہلے حیض (طلاق والے حیض) میں سے رہ گئے تھے تو اس طرح تین حیض مکمل ہو جائیں گے البتہ اس عورت پر عدت گزار نے کا حکم اس وقت لگایا جائے گا جب یہ آخری حیض گزر جائے گا کیونکہ حیض تجزی کو قبول نہیں کرتا جس طرح باندی کی عدت ویسے تو ڈیڑھ حیض ہونی چاہیے لیکن حیض کی تجزی قبول نہ کرنے کی وجہ سے اس کی عدت دو حیض مکمل رکھی گئی ہے۔ تو اسی طرح یہاں بھی ہے۔ عدت گزرنے کا حکم اس وقت ہوگا جب تیسرا حیض ختم ہوگا۔
بعض طہر مکمل طہر نہیں ہو سکتا
على ان بعض الظهر ليس بطبر :۔ یہاں سے ایک اعتراض کا جواب ہے۔

اعتراض: طہر مراد لینے کی صورت میں آپ نے جو خرابی بیان کی ہے ہم کہتے ہیں کہ وہ خرابی لازم نہیں آتی کیونکہ طہر اس گھڑی کا نام ہے جس میں عورت حیض سے پاک ہو یعنی کم از کم وہ وقت جس پر طہر کا اطلاق ہو سکے وہ طہر ہے اور وہ ایک گھڑی ہے یہ ضروری نہیں کہ مکمل ایام جو دو حیفوں کے درمیان ہوں وہ ایک مکمل طہر ہے اور اگر کچھ ایام گزرجائیں تو بقیہ ایام بعض طہر ہوں گے تو اب ہم کہتے ہیں کہ جس طہر میں طلاق دی جائے گی اس کو عدت میں شمار کیا جائے گا چونکہ بعض طہر کو بھی طہر ہی کہا جاتا ہے اس لیے یہاں یہ نہیں کہا جائے گا کہ یہ بعض طہر ہے بلکہ یہ مکمل طہر ہے اور مکمل طہر ہی عدت شمار ہوگا جب مکمل طہر عدت شمار ہورہا ہے تو عدت مکمل تین طہر ہوئی کم نہ ہوئی تو ثلثہ کے موجب پر عمل ہو گیا۔
جواب (۱):۔ اس عتراض کے دو جواب دیئے ہیں۔ ایک جمہور نے دیا ہے اور ایک مائن نے جمہور نے یہ جواب دیا ہے کہ آپ کے اعتراض سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ ہر وہ گھڑی جس میں عورت حیض سے پاک رہے گی وہ مکمل طہر شمار ہو گی تو مطلب یہ ہو گا کہ دو حیضوں کے درمیان وقفہ آپ کے نزدیک ایک طہر نہیں ہے بلکہ کئی طہر ہیں یعنی جتنی گھڑیاں ہیں اتنے طہر ہیں اور اس سے یہ لازم آئے گا کہ خاوند جب بیوی کو طہر میں طلاق دے گا اس کے بعد متصل ہر گھڑی ایک طہر شمار ہوگا تو جتنی گھڑیاں متحقق ہونگی اتنے طہر متحقق ہونگے تو اس سے یہ لازم آئے گا کہ خاوند جب بیوی کو طہر میں طلاق دے گا اس کے بعد متصل ہر گھڑی ایک طہر شمار ہوگا تو تین گھڑیاں گزرنے سے تین طہر گزر جائیں گے تو گویا تین گھڑیاں گزرنے سے آپ کے نزدیک عورت کی عدت گزر جائے گی پھر تو یہ کہنا چاہیے کہ عورت کی عدت طلاق کے بعد تین گھڑیاں ہیں نہ یہ کہ اس مکمل طہر کے بعد جب حیض آئے گا اور اس کے بعد دو ہر اور گزریں گے تو پھر عدت مکمل ہو گی لیکن آپ اس بات کے قائل نہیں ہیں لہذا آپ کا یہ کہنا کہ بعض طہر بھی مکمل طہر ہی ہوتا ہے درست نہیں ہے۔
جواب (۲):۔ مائن نے جواب دیا کہ بعض طہر مکمل طہر نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ اگر ایسا ہو تو چونکہ پہلے اور تیسرے طہر میں کوئی فرق نہیں ہے اس لیے اگر پہلے طہر کا بعض حصہ مکمل طہر شمار ہو سکتا ہے تو تیسرے طہر کا بعض حصہ بھی مکمل طہر شمار ہوسکتا ہے تو اب ہم یہ کہیں گے کہ اس پہلے طہر (طلاق والے ظہر اور اس کے بعد دوسرے طہر کو گزارنے کے بعد جب تیسر اطہر آئے گا تو اس تیسرے طہر کا کچھ حصہ گزرنے کے بعد عورت کی عدت پوری ہو جانی چاہیے حالانکہ یہ اجتماع کے خلاف ہے لہذا یہ کہنا کہ بعض ہر مکمل طہر ہی ہوتا ہے درست نہ ہوا۔
جمہور و مائن کے جوابات میں فرق
فرق بین الجوابین:۔ جمہور اور مائن کے جواب میں فرق یہ ہے کہ جمہور کو یہ جواب دیا جاسکتا ہے کہ جناب ہمارا مطلب یہ
Al-Tarwih li-Halli al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih. Proof of Imam Shafi'i: Imam Shafi'i argues that there is a rule: if the number is masculine, the specification (tamyiz) is feminine; and if the number is feminine, the specification is masculine. Here the number 'thalathah' (three) is feminine, so the specification, i.e., 'quru'', will mean what is masculine. That is tuhr (purity), not hayd (menstruation) because hayd is semantically feminine. So here tuhr is intended. Response: Hayd although semantically feminine, is masculine in terms of wording, so there is no objection to taking it as intended. This does not violate the rule. Objection: The defect you mentioned when taking tuhr as meaning can also be found when taking hayd as meaning. That is, if a man divorces his wife during hayd, is that hayd counted in the iddah or not? If counted, then the iddah would be less than three hayds; if not counted, and instead the three subsequent hayds are counted, then the iddah would exceed three hayds. So the defect arises in that case too. Answer (1): Essentially, the prescribed (masnun) divorce is that given during tuhr, and we are discussing that. In masnun divorce, the iddah is exactly three hayds, no less or more, because the three hayds immediately after that tuhr are counted. Answer (2): If divorce is given during hayd, deficiency or excess does not necessarily follow from the requirement of 'thalathah', because we say that the hayd in which the divorce occurred is counted in the iddah, but not fully; only the remaining part of that hayd is counted, and the days that have passed are made up later. The method is: after those remaining days, the woman will complete two full hayds, and then when the next hayd comes, from it as many days will be counted as were left from the first hayd (the one of divorce). Thus three hayds will be completed. However, the ruling of completing the iddah is given when this last hayd ends, because hayd does not tolerate fragmentation (tajazzi). Just as for the iddah of a slave girl, it should ideally be one and a half hayds, but due to hayd's non-fragmentation, her iddah is set at two full hayds. Similarly here, the ruling of iddah completion is when the third hayd ends. Some tuhr cannot be a complete tuhr. 'Ala anna ba'd al-tuhr laysa bi-tuhr: This is a response to an objection. Objection: The defect you mentioned when taking tuhr as meaning – we say that defect does not necessarily arise, because tuhr is the name of the moment when a woman is pure from hayd, i.e., the minimum time on which the term tuhr can be applied is a moment. It is not necessary that the complete days between two hayds are one complete tuhr; if some days pass, the remaining days are part of tuhr (ba'd al-tuhr). Now we say that the tuhr in which divorce is given will be counted in the iddah. Since some tuhr is also called tuhr, it will not be said that this is some tuhr; rather it is a complete tuhr, and a complete tuhr is counted as iddah. When a complete tuhr is counted as iddah, the iddah becomes three complete tuhrs, no decrease, so the requirement of 'thalathah' is fulfilled. Answer (1): To this objection, two answers are given. One by the Jamhur (majority) and one by Main. The Jamhur answered: Your objection indicates that every moment a woman is free from hayd is considered a complete tuhr. Then it would mean that the interval between two hayds is not one tuhr but many tuhrs – as many moments, so many tuhrs. From this it would follow that when a husband divorces his wife during tuhr, immediately after that every moment would count as a tuhr. So as many moments occur, so many tuhrs occur. Then three moments passing would mean three tuhrs have passed. So in your view, the woman's iddah would pass with three moments. Then it should be said that the woman's iddah after divorce is three moments, not that after the complete tuhr, when hayd comes, and then two more tuhrs pass, then the iddah is complete. But you do not believe that. Therefore, your saying that some tuhr is also a complete tuhr is incorrect. Answer (2): Main answered that some tuhr is not a complete tuhr because if it were, then since there is no difference between the first and third tuhr, if part of the first tuhr can be counted as a complete tuhr, then part of the third tuhr could also be counted as a complete tuhr. So we would say: after the first tuhr (the one of divorce) and after the second tuhr passes, when the third tuhr comes, after part of that third tuhr passes the woman's iddah should be complete. But this is against consensus. Therefore, the claim that some tuhr is always a complete tuhr is incorrect. Difference between the answers of Jamhur and Main: The difference between the two answers is that the Jamhur can be given this reply: Our intention is...
Source pages p. 538

Commentary
This passage presents a classic usul al-fiqh dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the interpretation of the word 'quru'' (plural of qur') in the verse on iddah (Quran 2:228). The Shafi'i position, as presented first, relies on a linguistic rule (qā‘idah) about number-gender agreement between a number and its specification (tamyīz). Since the number 'thalāthah' is feminine, the specification should be masculine; thus 'quru'' must refer to something masculine. The Shafi'is argue that hayd (menstruation) is semantically feminine, so the masculine meaning is tuhr (purity period). The Hanafi response counters that although hayd is semantically feminine, the word itself is masculine in form, so it can serve as the specification without violating the rule. The text then presents an objection from the opponent: if tuhr is taken as meaning, a similar defect (deficiency or excess in the iddah count) arises when divorce occurs during tuhr. The Hanafi defense is two-fold: first, the discussion is about masnūn (sunna-compliant) divorce given during tuhr, where the iddah of three hayds is preserved. Second, for divorce during hayd, the Hanafis offer a detailed fragmentation (tajazzī) solution: the remaining part of the current hayd is counted, then two full hayds, and then the shortfall from the first hayd is made up in the third hayd. This preserves the total of three hayds without exceeding it, using the principle that hayd does not tolerate fragmentation (so the iddah is only complete when the third hayd ends). The passage then moves to a second objection: if some tuhr (ba‘ḍ al-ṭuhr) is considered a complete tuhr, absurd consequences follow. Two answers are given: the Jamhur's answer shows that this leads to the conclusion that three moments would complete the iddah, which is not the Shafi'i position. Main's answer shows that if partial tuhr can be complete, then part of the third tuhr would complete the iddah, contradicting consensus. Thus the Shafi'i objection fails. The difference between the two responses is clarified in terms of their logical implications.

Key Terms
قرء (qur' (pl. quru')): The term in the verse interpreted as either hayd (menstruation) or tuhr (purity period).
بعض الطهر (ba'd al-tuhr): A portion of the purity interval that is not considered a complete tuhr.
تجزّي (tajazzi): The principle that a legal entity (e.g., hayd) cannot be fragmented into parts; each unit must be complete.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response in the passage, why cannot ba'd al-tuhr be considered a complete tuhr?
A) Because the minimum period for tuhr is one day.
B) Because the Jamhur's answer leads to absurdity of three moments.
C) Because the Quran explicitly says so.
D) Because the Companions ruled it.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi fragmentation method and the refutation of ba'd al-tuhr demonstrate how usul principles (like non-fragmentation and absurdity) are used to defend a position against objections.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
12 min
The Particle 'Fa' and the Nature of Khul': Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Hanafi argument that khul' is a type of divorce using the particle fa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that the particle 'fa' indicates immediate succession and connection to derive that khul' is a type of divorce.

Core Idea
The particle 'fa' forces khul' to be a divorce; otherwise the Quranic sequence breaks.

This passage presents the Hanafi defense of classifying khul' as a type of divorce, using a close reading of the Quranic text. The debate hinges on a single particle: 'fa' in 'fa in tallaqahā'. The Hanafis argue that this particle requires immediate connection between the preceding khul' and the following divorce, so khul' must itself be a divorce. Imam al-Shafi'i's objection—that this would allow four divorces—is answered by explaining that khul' is not an independent divorce but a subtype.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two competing interpretations
First, state the Hanafi position (khul' is divorce) and the Shafi'i position (khul' is dissolution). Note the practical consequence: if khul' is divorce, it counts toward the three; if dissolution, the marriage ends immediately with no further divorce needed.
2
Analyze the Hanafi proof from the particle 'fa'
The Hanafi proof relies on the Quranic verse 'fa in tallaqahā' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:230). The particle 'fa' in Hanafi usul is a 'ḥarf khāṣṣ' that requires immediate succession with connection (taʿqīb maʿa al-waṣl). The preceding context mentions khul' (hiḍḍa), so the 'fa' must connect the third divorce to the khul'. If khul' were not a divorce, the connection would be broken.
The word 'hiḍḍa' in the passage refers to khul'.
3
Examine the Shafi'i objection and Hanafi response
The Shafi'i objection is that if khul' is a divorce, the total divorces could become four (two regular + khul' + third). The Hanafi response: khul' is not an independent divorce but a type of the divorce already mentioned in 'al-ṭalāqu marratān'. The verse divides divorce into two types: without compensation (regular) and with compensation (khul'). Thus, the count does not exceed three.
4
Address the subsidiary objections
Two further objections are refuted: (1) The verse mentions the woman's action (iftaqadat) while divorce is the man's action. The Hanafi answer: the woman's action is subsidiary to confirm the man's divorce, and the mention of wealth comes from her side. (2) Considering khul' as faskh would add a new ruling to the Qur'an, which is avoided by interpreting it as divorce consistent with context.
5
Synthesize the argument and identify the usul principle
The core usul principle is that the meaning of a particle ('fa') determines the relationship between clauses. The Hanafis prioritize the immediate textual connection over a hypothetical consequence (four divorces). This illustrates the Hanafi tendency to let the literal text (ẓāhir) govern unless a stronger proof overrides.

مستقل طلاق کا بیان نہیں ہے۔ لہذا چار طلاقوں کا ہونالازم نہیں آتا۔ وفی تخصیص فعلہا :۔ یہاں سے ماتن نے ایک اعتراض کا جواب دیا ہے۔ اعتراض: خلع کے ذکر میں فیما افتقدت بہ " ہے یہاں افتقدت کی نسبت عورت کی طرف ہے یعنی ضلع میں عورت کے فعل کو ذکر کیا ہے حالانکہ طلاق تو مرد کا فعل ہوتا ہے تو اگر خلع طلاق ہوتی تو یہاں مرد کا فعل مذکور ہوتا۔ جواب:۔ عورت کا فعل مستقل فعل نہیں ہے بلکہ مرد کے طلاق والے فعل کو پختہ کرنے کے لیے ہے اصل فعل مرد کا ہی ہے لیکن یہاں پر چونکہ مال کا ذکر کرنا تھا اور مال عورت کی جانب سے ہوتا ہے اس لیے یہاں عورت کا فعل ذکر کر دیا ہے۔ خلع کو فسخ قرار دینے میں کتاب اللہ پر زیادتی لازم آتی ہے لا کما یقول الشافعی :۔ یہاں سے امام شافعی کے مذہب کا رد کیا جارہا ہے کہ اگر امام شافعی کی بات کو مانا جائے اور ضلع کو نسخ نکاح قرار دیا جائے تو کتاب اللہ پر زیادتی لازم آئے گی کیونکہ آیت میں فتح کا ذکر نہیں ہے آیت میں افتداء ( فدیہ دینے ) کا ذکر ہے اور اس سے فتح والا معنی سمجھ میں نہیں آتا ہاں اگر طلاق مراد لیں تو کتاب اللہ پر زیادتی لازم نہیں آتی ہے کیونکہ اس سے پہلے طلاق کا ذکر ہے اس لیے اگر افتداء سے مراد طلاق لیں گے تو یہ قرینے کے موافق ہو گا۔ اور اس صورت میں فان طلقہا کا مطلب بنے گا۔ کہ اگر پہلے دو طلاقیں دے دی ہیں چاہے وہ بغیر مال کے ہوں یا مال کے ساتھ ہوں اس کے بعد تیسری طلاق دینے سے عورت مغلظہ ہو جائے گی۔
Second amusement and the proof of the Hanafis: The proof of the Hanafis, which is also an amusement on the ruling of the specific (particle), is that here the connection of 'fa in tallaqahā' is with 'fīmā iftaqadat bihī ... illā hiḍḍa' and not with 'al-ṭalāqu marratān' because in 'fa in tallaqahā' the letter 'fā' is a specific particle and its implication is immediate succession with connection. Its requirement is that that which follows is dependent on that which precedes. Here its preceding is 'hiḍḍa' (khul') and its following is the third divorce. So this divorce is dependent on this 'hiḍḍa'. Now if 'hiḍḍa' is not considered divorce and 'fa in tallaqahā' is made dependent on 'al-ṭalāqu marratān', then the implication of the specific would be invalidated because the follower of 'fā' would not be dependent on its immediate predecessor, but rather on something else, causing a separation between them. Therefore, to act upon the implication of the specific, it is necessary that its dependence is on 'hiḍḍa', and in that case it is necessary that khul' is divorce. Hence, if (the third) divorce occurs, it is divorce and after it divorce can occur. As for Imam al-Shāfiʿī, he said that if you make khul' a divorce, then the number of divorces would become four. We say that the occurrence of four divorces is not necessary because in khul' there is no mention of an independent divorce; rather, in 'al-ṭalāqu marratān' the divorce that was mentioned, here only one of its types is mentioned, as if indicating that there are two types of divorce: one without compensation, which is mentioned in 'al-ṭalāqu marratān', and the second type with compensation, which is mentioned in 'hiḍḍa'. So this is not an independent mention of divorce. Hence, four divorces do not necessarily occur. And regarding the specification of her action: From here the author (al-mātin) has answered an objection. Objection: In the mention of khul', there is 'fīmā iftaqadat bihī', here 'iftaqadat' is attributed to the woman, meaning in khul' the action of the woman is mentioned, whereas divorce is an action of the man. So if khul' were divorce, the action of the man would be mentioned. Answer: The woman's action is not an independent action; rather, it is to confirm the man's action of divorce. The original action is the man's, but since here the mention of wealth was intended and wealth comes from the woman's side, therefore the woman's action was mentioned here. Regarding considering khul' as dissolution (faskh), it would entail an addition to the Book of Allah, not as al-Shāfiʿī says: From here the refutation of Imam al-Shāfiʿī's school is done. That if Imam al-Shāfiʿī's statement is accepted and khul' is considered a dissolution of marriage, then an addition to the Book of Allah would be necessary because the verse does not mention separation; the verse mentions 'ifdā' (ransom), and from that the meaning of separation is not understood. However, if divorce is intended, then no addition to the Book of Allah is necessary because before it divorce is mentioned. Therefore, if by 'ifdā' divorce is meant, it will be in accordance with the context. And in that case the meaning of 'fa in tallaqahā' will be that if he has given two divorces, whether without wealth or with wealth, after that the third divorce will render the woman irrevocably divorced (mughallaẓah).
Source pages p. 542

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi defense of the position that khul' is a type of divorce and not a dissolution (faskh). The Hanafi argument is based on the Quranic verse in Surah al-Baqarah (2:229-230), specifically the particle 'fa' in 'fa in tallaqahā' (فإن طلقها). The Hanafis argue that the 'fa' is a particle indicating immediate succession and connection (taʿqīb maʿa al-waṣl). It requires that what follows (the third divorce) be directly dependent on what immediately precedes (the khul' in the previous verse). Thus, the 'fa' connects the divorce to the khul', implying that khul' itself is a divorce. If khul' were not a divorce, the 'fa' would not connect properly, causing a break in the sequence. The Shāfiʿī objection that this would lead to four divorces is answered by explaining that khul' is not an independent divorce but one of the two types of divorce (with or without compensation), thus not increasing the count. The passage then addresses two further objections: first, that the verse mentions the woman's action (iftaqadat) while divorce is the man's action, answered by saying the woman's action is subsidiary to confirm the man's divorce; second, that considering khul' as dissolution would imply adding a new ruling to the Qur'an. Instead, interpreting khul' as divorce is consistent with the context. This is a classic usul dispute about textual interpretation and the implications of linguistic particles.

Key Terms
ف (fa): A particle (ḥarf) that indicates immediate succession and connection (taʿqīb maʿa al-waṣl) between two actions.
خلع (khulʿ): A form of marital separation initiated by the wife through ransom (fidyah), considered by Hanafis as a type of revocable divorce.
فسخ (faskh): Annulment or dissolution of the marriage contract, which in Shāfiʿī law is the effect of khulʿ.
تعقیب مع الوصل (taʿqīb maʿa al-waṣl): The linguistic implication of the particle 'fa' meaning immediate succession without interruption, but with connection between two clauses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi argument, what does the particle 'fa' in 'fa in tallaqahā' indicate about khul'?
A) That khul' is a separate legal mechanism unrelated to divorce.
B) That khul' must be a type of divorce for the sequence to be consistent.
C) That khul' is a dissolution (faskh) because the woman initiates it.
D) That khul' does not involve the man's action.

Key Takeaway
The particle 'fa' forces the Hanafis to classify khul' as a type of divorce, preserving the textual sequence and avoiding the need for an additional category of faskh.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate

Minimum Mahr: Hanafi Derivation from Khass and Qiyas
Dispute on minimum mahr derived from khass and qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Hanafi usul principles (khass as qat'i and qiyas) to derive the minimum mahr from the Quranic text and contrast the Shafi'i reading.

Core Idea
Hanafi: mahr minimum set by Shariah via khass in verse and qiyas on theft; Shafi'i: no minimum, qiyas on sale.

This passage presents a key usul dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is over whether the minimum mahr is fixed by Shariah. The Hanafis argue that the Quranic word 'faradna' is khass, indicating determination, and the specific amount is derived by qiyas on the theft penalty. The Shafi'is instead rely on qiyas on sale, making mahr flexible. Understanding this debate clarifies how different usul methodologies can lead to divergent fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the positions
State the Hanafi position (minimum ten dirhams) and the Shafi'i position (no minimum). Note the practical difference: if mahr is set below ten, Hanafi enforces ten, Shafi'i enforces the agreed amount.
This thamarah al-khilaf is the concrete consequence.
2
Analyze the Quranic verse as khass
The word 'faradna' (We have ordained) is interpreted by Hanafis as 'qaddarna' (determined), making it khass (specific). This indicates the Shariah has set a quantity for mahr, though the verse does not specify the amount.
Hanafi usul holds that khass is qat'i in its indication.
3
Trace the Hanafi qiyas on theft
The Shariah fixed the hand-cutting threshold at ten dirhams (for theft). This shows a limb (hand) is valued at ten. In marriage, the husband obtains ownership of the wife's private part (bud'), which is also a limb. By qiyas, its substitute (mahr) must be at least ten dirhams.
The illa (effective cause) is that both are limbs valued by Shariah.
4
Contrast with Shafi'i qiyas on sale
Shafi'is analogize mahr to price (thaman) in a sale: anything that can be a price can be mahr. This allows any amount or item of value.
This qiyas ignores the specific text (nass) on marriage.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
Hanafis argue that qiyas is only used where no text exists. Here, the Quranic verse provides a text on marriage, so qiyas on sale is unnecessary. Instead, they use qiyas on theft because the verse itself is silent on the exact amount but indicates determination.
This shows a prioritization of textual evidence over analogy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خاص کے حکم پر چوتھی تفریح
قوله تعالى وقد علمنا ما فرضنا : یہاں سے خاص کے حکم پر چوتھی تفریح ہے اور اس سے پہلے بھی ایک مسئلہ سمجھیں اور وہ یہ ہے کہ مہر کی مقدار شرعا متعین ہے یا نہیں؟ امام شافعی کے ہاں مہر کی مقدار شرعا متعین نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ زوجین خود جتنا مہر مقررکر لیں۔ اتنالازم ہو جائے گا۔ اور ان کے ہاں ہر وہ چیز جوشن (عوض) بنے کی صلاحیت رکھتی ہے وہ مہر بن سکتی ہے لیکن احناف کے ہاں زیادتی کے اعتبار سے تو مہر کی مقدار متعین نہیں ہے لیکن کمی کے اعتبار سے متعین ہے اور وہ ہے دس در ہم کہ اگر ہو دس درہم سے کم مقرر کیا گیا ہے تو دس درہم ہی لازم ہوں گے اس سے کم جائز نہیں ہوں گے۔ دلیل و تفریح:- قرآن پاک میں ارشاد باری ہے قد علمنا ما فرضنا عليهم في ازواجهم “ یہاں فرضنا بمعنی قدرنا ہے اور یہ خاص ہے اس سے اتنا پتہ چل رہا ہے کہ شریعت نے مہر کی مقدار کو مقرر کیا ہے اگر چہ یہ بیان نہیں کیا گیا کہ کتنا مہر مقرر ہے؟ اس کے بعد اب اس تقدیر میں دو احتمال ہیں کہ یہ تقدیر یکمی کے اعتبار سے ہے یا زیادتی کے اعتبار سے زیادتی کی کوئی حد نہیں ہے بالا جماع لہذا معلوم ہوا کہ یہ تقدیر کی کے اعتبار سے ہے اور وہ تقدیر ہے کتنی؟ اس کا بیان آیت میں نہیں ہے تو تقدیر قیاس کے ذریعہ سے کی گئی ہے کہ شریعت نے چوری میں قطع ید کے لیے دس دراہم کی شرط لگائی ہے تو گویا کہ شریعت نے آدمی کے ایک عضو یعنی ہاتھ کی قیمت دس دراہم رکھی ہے اور نکاح میں بھی زوج کو آدمی کے ایک عضو یعنی بضع پر ملک حاصل ہوتی ہے تو اس کا عوض ( مہر ) بھی کم از کم دس درہم ہونا چاہیے اس لیے ہم نے مقرر کر دیا کہ مہر کی کم از کم مقدار دس در اہم ہے۔ بخلاف شوافع کے وہ قیاس کرتے ہیں بیچ پر کہ جو چیز بیچ میں شمن بنے کی صلاحیت رکھتی ہے تو وہ مہر بنے کی صلاحیت رکھتی ہے لیکن اس کا ۔ جواب:۔ یہ ہے کہ یہاں نکاح کو بیچ پر قیاس کی ضرورت نہیں کیونکہ قیاس وہاں ہوتا ہے جہاں نص موجود نہ ہو حالانکہ یہاں پر نکاح کے جواز کے بارے میں مستقل نص موجود ہے۔
The fourth branch on the ruling of the specific (khass). His saying: 'And We have already known what We have ordained for them.' From here begins the fourth branch on the ruling of the specific. Before this, understand one issue: Is the amount of mahr determined by Shariah or not? According to Imam Shafi'i, the amount of mahr is not determined by Shariah. Rather, the spouses set whatever amount they wish, and it becomes binding. In his view, anything that can serve as a substitute (iwad) can be mahr. However, according to the Hanafis, the amount of mahr is not determined with respect to excess, but it is determined with respect to deficiency, and that is ten dirhams. If less than ten dirhams is specified, ten dirhams become binding; less than that is not permissible. Proof and explanation: In the Holy Quran, Allah says: 'We have already known what We have ordained for them in their spouses.' Here 'ordained' (faradna) means 'determined' (qaddarna), and this is specific (khass). From this, it is understood that the Shariah has determined the amount of mahr, even though it is not stated how much. Then there are two possibilities: this determination is regarding deficiency or regarding excess. There is no limit for excess by consensus, so it becomes clear that this determination is regarding deficiency. And how much is that determination? The verse does not state it, so the determination was made through qiyas: the Shariah set the condition of ten dirhams for cutting the hand in theft. So the Shariah valued a person's limb, i.e., the hand, at ten dirhams. In marriage, the husband also obtains ownership over a limb of the woman, namely the private part (bud'), so its substitute (mahr) should also be at least ten dirhams. Therefore, we have decreed that the minimum amount of mahr is ten dirhams. Contrary to the Shafi'is, they make qiyas on sale: anything that can be a price in sale can also be mahr. But its answer is that here there is no need to compare marriage to sale, because qiyas is applied where there is no text, whereas here there is a specific text regarding the validity of marriage.
Source pages p. 545

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding the determination of the minimum mahr. The author begins by stating that this is the fourth branch (tafri'ah) on the ruling of the specific (khass). Before the branch, he clarifies the issue: is the amount of mahr determined by Shariah or not? Imam Shafi'i holds that it is not determined; the spouses may agree on any amount, and anything that can serve as a substitute (iwad) in a sale can be mahr. The Hanafis, however, hold that while there is no upper limit, there is a lower limit of ten dirhams. The proof is from the Quranic verse: 'We have already known what We have ordained for them in their spouses.' The word 'faradna' (ordained) here means 'qaddarna' (determined), and it is specific (khass), indicating that the Shariah has indeed determined the amount, though the verse does not specify. Since no upper limit is set by consensus, the determination must be on the lower side. The specific amount is then derived through qiyas: in theft, the hand is cut for theft of ten dirhams, so the Shariah values a limb at ten dirhams. In marriage, the husband gains ownership of the wife's private part, so the substitute (mahr) should also be at least ten dirhams. The Shafi'is instead use qiyas on sale (bay'), arguing that anything that can be a price in sale can be mahr. The Hanafi response is that there is no need for qiyas on sale because there is an explicit text (nass) about marriage, and qiyas is only used when no text exists.

Key Terms
خاص (khass): A text that is specific in its indication, leaving no room for generality. Here the word 'faradna' indicates specific determination of mahr amount.
مهر (mahr): The obligatory payment (dower) given by the husband to the wife in marriage.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning: extending a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') due to a shared effective cause (illa).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum amount of mahr, and how is it derived?
A) Ten dirhams, derived directly from the Quran.
B) Ten dirhams, derived by qiyas on the threshold for theft.
C) No minimum, derived by qiyas on sale.
D) Five dirhams, derived from the Sunnah.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi minimum mahr of ten dirhams is derived through khass (the verse indicating determination) and qiyas on theft, while the Shafi'i position uses qiyas on sale, leading to no fixed minimum.

Interpretation of Hatta and the Issue of Tahlil
Hanafi response to Shafi'i objection on tahlil after less than three divorces

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the effect of a second marriage after less than three divorces and identify the usul principle (khas, amm, takhsis) that governs the dispute.

Core Idea
The second husband resets the divorce count regardless of number—the hadith, not the verse, is the primary dalil.

This passage delves into a classic usul dispute: does a second marriage after one or two divorces make the woman fully lawful to her first husband, granting him three divorces anew? The Hanafis say yes; the Shafi'is say only after three. The debate hinges on the interpretation of the word 'hatta' in the Quran and the weight of the hadith of Rif'ah al-Qurazi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the effect of a second marriage after less than three divorces.
The Hanafis hold that the second husband resets the count; the Shafi'is hold that only the remaining divorces carry over.
2
Locate the primary source of dispute
Identify the Quranic verse (2:230) and the hadith of Rif'ah as the key texts.
The Shafi'is rely on the verse; the Hanafis rely on the hadith.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i objection using 'hatta'
Explain how the Shafi'is argue that 'hatta' is khas, indicating termination only of the severe prohibition.
They claim that the verse's word 'hatta' definitively ends the prohibition from three divorces; for fewer, there is no severe prohibition to terminate.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
Identify the Hanafi argument that the verse is not the primary dalil and that the hadith governs.
The Hanafis note that 'tankiha' means marriage contract, not intercourse, so the verse cannot establish the condition; the hadith provides the condition and is general.
5
Determine the usul principle in operation
Identify takhsis al-amm bi al-sunnah and the role of qiyas in extending the ruling to fewer divorces.
The hadith specifies the general verse, and qiyas applies the same rule to one and two divorces.

الترويج لِحَلَّ التَّوْضِيح والتلويح

ترجمہ: اور تحقیق ذکر کیے ہیں فخر الاسلام نے اس فصل میں دوسرے مسائل کہ میں نے ذکر کیا ہے ان کو نص پر زیادتی کی بحث میں فصل الصلح کے آخر میں مگر دو مسئلے کہ میں نے چھوڑ دیا ہے ان کو کلی طور پر خوف کرتے ہوئے طوالت کا اور وہ دونوں مسئلہ ہرم اور مسئلہ قطع مع الضمان ہیں۔

تشریح:۔ یہان سے ماتن علیہ الرحمہ ایک فائدہ بیان فرما رہے ہیں۔ کہ خاص پر کچھ تفریعات تو میں نے ذکر کی ہیں اور کچھ تفریعات کو امام فخر الاسلام نے تو اسی فصل میں ذکر کیا ہے لیکن میں نے ان کو شیخ کے باب میں بیان کیا ہے۔ اور دو مسئلے ایسے ہیں کہ ان کو میں نے تطویل کے خوف سے چھوڑ دیا ہے اور وہ ہیں مسئلہ ہرم اور مسلہ قطع مع الضمان ان کی تفصیل درج ذیل ہے۔

تفصیل مسئلہ ہرم:۔ اس مسئلہ کو جانے سے قبل بطور تمہید کے ایک مقدہ کو جانا ضروری ہے۔

مقدمہ:۔ اگر کوئی آدمی اپنی بیوی کو تین طلاقیں دے دے وہ عورت کسی دوسرے آدمی کے ساتھ نکاح کرے اور وہ آدمی اس کے ساتھ دخول کر لے اس کے بعد یہ زوج ثانی عورت کو طلاق دے دے یا مر جائے اور یہ عورت دوبارہ پہلے خاوند کے ساتھ نکاح کرلے تو اس زوج اول کو دوبارہ بالا تفاق تین طلاق کا حق حاصل ہو گا۔ یعنی دوبارہ یہ عورت زوج اول کے لیے نئے کرے سے حلال ہوگی گویا کہ زوج ثانی پہلی تین طلاقوں کے لیے بالا تفاق ھادم ہو گا۔ اور اگر پہلے زوج نے ایک یا دو طلاق دی ہو اور عورت دوسرے آدمی کے ساتھ نکاح کرلے وہ دوسرا آدمی دخول کرلے اور طلاق دے دے یا مر جائے تو اس صورت میں دوسرا زوج پہلے زوج کی دی ہوئی طلاقوں کے لیے ہادم ہو گا یا نہیں؟ اس میں اختلاف ہے امام شافعی اور امام محمد کے نزدیک اس صورت میں دوسر ازوج صادم نہیں ہو گا یعنی اگر یہ عورت دوبارہ زوج اول کے ساتھ نکاح کرے تو اس خاوند کو اتنی طلاقوں کا ہی حق حاصل ہو گا جتنی پہلے بچ گئی ہیں دوبارہ تین طلاقوں کا حق نہیں ہوگا اور امام ابو حنیفہ اور امام ابوسف" کے نزدیک دوسرا خاوند اس صورت میں بھی مادم ہو گا یعنی یہ عورت اگر دوبارہ زوج اول کے پاس منکوحہ بن کر آئے گی تو اس کو تین طلاقوں کا حق ہوگا۔ خواہ پہلے اس نے ایک طلاق دی تھی یا دو طلاقیں دی تھیں ۔

اعتراض:۔ امام شافعی کی جانب سے حضرت امام صاحب پر اعتراض ہوتا ہے اور یہی خاص کے حکم پر تفریح بھی ہے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ قرآن پاک میں ہے ۔ یا انسان طلقها فلا تحل له من بعد حتى تنكح زوجا غیرہ " یہاں حتی لفظ خاص ہے یہ انتہا والے معنی پر قطعا دلالت کرتا ہے یعنی حتی سے پہلے جو چیز ثابت ہوتی ہے حتی کے بعد وہ چیز منتہی اور ختم ہو جاتی ہے مثلا

الترويج لحل التوضيح والتنويج

کسی نے کہا اضربک حتی یجی حامد میں تجھ کو مارتا رہوں گا یہاں تک کہ حامد آ جائے یعنی حامد کے آنے کے بعد مار نا ختم کر دونگا پس حتی کے معنی کی روشنی میں آیت کا مطلب ہوگا کہ پہلے شوہر کے تین طلاق دینے کی وجہ سے جو حرمت غلیظہ ثابت ہوگئی تھی دوسرے شوہر کے ساتھ نکاح کرنے کی وجہ سے وہ حرمت ختم ہو گئی ہے کلمہ حتی صرف اس معنی پر دلالت کرتا ہے اس پر قطعا دلالت نہیں کرتا کہ دوسرا شوہر پہلے شوہر کے لئے جدید اور از سر نو حلت پیدا کرتا ہے۔ پس شیخین کا یہ کہنا کہ زوج ثانی زوج اول کے لئے حال جدید پیدا کرتا ہے یہ خاص (کلمہ حتی) کے موجب کو باطل کرنا ہے اور جس صورۃ میں مغیا موجود ہے یعنی تین طلاقوں کی وجہ سے حرمت غلیظہ موجود ہے اس صورت میں دوسرا شوہر پہلے شوہر کے لئے محلل یعنی حلت جدیدہ پیدا کرنے والا نہ ہو سکا تو جس صورت میں مغیا بھی موجود نہیں یعنی تین طلاقوں سے کم کی صورت میں دوسرا شوہر بدرجہ اولی پہلے شوہر کے لئے محلل ( حلت پیدا کرنے والا ) نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اگر حرمت غلیظہ ہی نہ پائی جائے تو اس کی انتہاء بھی نہیں ہوگی اس لیے یہاں اگر یہ کہا جائے کہ دو یا دو سے کم طلاقوں کے بعد ہونے والی حرمت کی انتہاء بھی زوج نانی کے ساتھ نکاح سے ہو جائے گی تو خاص کے موجب پر عمل نہیں ہو گا۔

جواب :۔ آپ کا اعتراض تب درست تھا جب ہم نے زوج اول کے لیے عورت کی حلت جدید و پر اسی آیت یعنی حتی تنکم سے دلیل پکڑی ہو حالانکہ ہم نے اس سے دلیل نہیں پکڑی بلکہ اس آیت سے دلیل پکڑنا تو درست ہی نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہاں تکح کا لفظ ہے اور اس سے مراد عقد نکاح ہے ولی نہیں کیونکہ اس کی نسبت عورت کی طرف کی ہے اور وطی عورت نہیں کرتی مرد کرتا ہے تو سیخ مراد ہے تو جب تکح سے مراد عقد نکاح ہے تو اس سے دلیل پکڑنا درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ اگر اس سے دلیل پکڑتے ہوئے اس کو حرمت غلیظہ کی انتہا ء بنا ئیں تو لازم آئے گا کہ صرف عقد نکاح ہی سے عورت زوج اول کے لیے حلال ہو جائے اور یہ درست نہیں ہے لہذا اس آیت سے دلیل نہیں پکڑی جاسکتی بلکہ اس عورت کے زوج اول کے لیے حلال ہونے کی دلیل حدیث عسیلہ ہے کہ جس میں رفاعہ قرظی کی بیوی حضور اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم کے پاس حاضر ہوئی اور آپ سے عرض کیا کہ میرے خاوند رفاعہ قرطی نے مجھے تین طلاق دیں تو میں نے عدت گزارنے کے بعد عبد الرحمن بن زہیر سے نکاح کیا لیکن میں نے ان کو نامرد پایا تو حضور نے نے فرمایا کہ تم رفاعہ کے پاس لوٹنا چاہتی ہو اس نے کہا ہاں پر آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے یہ سن کر فرمایا لاحتی تذوقی عسیلیتہ و ہو یذوق عسیلیک یعنی تم رفاعہ کے پاس اس وقت تک نہیں لوٹ سکتی جب تک تم جماع کی لذت اور حلاوت حاصل نہ کر لو۔ یہ حدیث اس بات کو بیان کرنے کے لئے لائی گئی ہے کہ حلالہ کے لئے زوج ثانی کا ولی کرنا شرط ہے اور محض نکاح جیسا کہ ظاہر آیت سے مفہوم ہوتا ہے وہ کافی نہیں اور یہ حدیث مشہور ہے
Commentary on the book Al-Tawdih wa Al-Talwih. Translation: And Fakhral-Islam mentioned other issues in this chapter that I have mentioned in the discussion on addition to the text at the end of the chapter of Sulh, except for two issues that I left out entirely for fear of prolongation, and they are the issue of Hirman and the issue of Qat' ma'a al-Daman. Explanation: Here the author, may God have mercy on him, is stating a benefit. He says: I have mentioned some furu' (branches) concerning the specific (khas) and some furu' that Imam Fakhr al-Islam mentioned in this chapter, but I have stated them in the chapter of the Shaykh. And there are two issues that I left out for fear of prolongation: the issue of Hirman and the issue of Qat' ma'a al-Daman. Their details follow. Detail of the issue of Hirman: Before understanding this issue, it is necessary to know a preliminary point as an introduction. Preliminary: If a man gives his wife three divorces, and that woman marries another man, and that man consummates the marriage with her, then this second husband divorces her or dies, and this woman remarries the first husband, then the first husband will, by consensus, have the right to three divorces again. That is, this woman will become permissible for the first husband anew, as if the second husband is, by consensus, a destroyer (hadim) for the first three divorces. And if the first husband gave one or two divorces, and the woman marries another man, that second man consummates and divorces her or dies, then in this case, is the second husband a destroyer for the divorces given by the first husband or not? There is disagreement: According to Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Muhammad, in this case the second husband will not be a destroyer. That is, if this woman remarries the first husband, that husband will only have the right to as many divorces as remain from the first time, not the right to three divorces anew. According to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf, the second husband will be a destroyer in this case as well. That is, if this woman comes back as a wife to the first husband, he will have the right to three divorces, whether he had given one divorce or two divorces before. Objection: On behalf of Imam al-Shafi'i, an objection is raised against Imam Abu Hanifa, and this is also a criticism of the ruling of the specific (khas). It is that the Holy Quran says: 'Then if he divorces her, she is not permissible for him afterwards until she marries another husband.' Here the word 'hatta' is specific (khas); it definitively indicates the meaning of termination, meaning that what is established before 'hatta' ends and ceases after 'hatta'. For example, if someone says 'I will beat you until Hamid comes,' meaning after Hamid comes I will stop beating. So in light of the meaning of 'hatta', the meaning of the verse would be that the severe prohibition (hurmat ghalizah) that was established due to the first husband giving three divorces has been terminated by marrying another husband. The word 'hatta' only indicates this meaning; it does not definitively indicate that the second husband creates a new and renewed permissibility for the first husband. So the saying of the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) that the second husband creates a new state of permissibility for the first husband invalidates the implication of the specific (the word 'hatta'). And in the case where the object of termination (mughta) exists, i.e., severe prohibition due to three divorces exists, if the second husband cannot be a muhallil (creator of new permissibility) for the first husband, then in the case where the object of termination does not exist, i.e., less than three divorces, the second husband will a fortiori not be a muhallil for the first husband, because if severe prohibition does not exist, its termination also does not occur. Therefore, if it is said here that the termination of the prohibition that occurs after two or less than two divorces also occurs by marrying the second husband, then the implication of the specific would not be acted upon. Response: Your objection would be valid if we took evidence from this same verse, 'hatta tankiha', for the new permissibility of the woman for the first husband. But we have not taken evidence from it. Rather, taking evidence from this verse is not correct because here the word is 'tankiha' and it refers to the marriage contract, not intercourse, because its attribution is to the woman, and a woman does not perform intercourse; a man does. So the meaning is marriage contract. And when 'tankiha' means marriage contract, then taking evidence from it is not correct because if we take evidence from it and make it the termination of severe prohibition, then it would necessitate that a woman becomes permissible for the first husband merely by the marriage contract, and that is not correct. Therefore, evidence cannot be taken from this verse. Rather, the evidence for the woman being permissible for the first husband is the hadith of 'Usaila (honey), in which the wife of Rifa'ah al-Qurazi came to the Holy Prophet, peace be upon him, and said to him: 'My husband Rifa'ah al-Qurti gave me three divorces, so after completing the 'iddah, I married 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Zuhayr, but I found him impotent.' The Prophet said: 'Do you want to return to Rifa'ah?' She said: 'Yes.' Upon hearing this, the Prophet said: 'No, until you taste his honey [sweetness] and he tastes your honey.' This hadith is brought to state that for tahlil (making lawful), it is necessary for the second husband to have intercourse, and mere marriage contract, as is apparent from the verse, is not sufficient. And this hadith is famous.
Source pages p. 546

Commentary
This passage discusses the Hanafi position on the effect of a second marriage after less than three divorces. The author first introduces two issues: the 'issue of Hirman' and the 'issue of Qat' ma'a al-Daman'. He notes that he omitted them for brevity but now explains the first. The issue revolves around whether a second husband acts as a 'muhallil' (one who makes the woman lawful again) for the first husband when the first divorce was less than three. The Hanafi school (Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf) holds that even after one or two divorces, the second husband, if he consummates the marriage, makes the woman completely lawful anew for the first husband, granting him the right to three divorces again. This is analogous to the case of three divorces. In contrast, Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Muhammad argue that only the severe prohibition from three divorces is removed by a second marriage; for fewer divorces, the remaining count carries over. The Shafi'i objection is based on the word 'hatta' in the Quranic verse (Surah al-Baqarah 2:230). They argue that 'hatta' indicates termination of the severe prohibition only, not the creation of a new permissibility. The Hanafi response is twofold: first, they do not rely on this verse for their evidence because the word 'tankiha' in the verse means marriage contract, not intercourse. If mere contract sufficed, the woman would become lawful without consummation, which contradicts the consensus that consummation is required. Instead, the Hanafis base their ruling on the famous hadith of Rif'ah al-Qurazi, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) explicitly stated that the woman cannot return to her first husband until she tastes the 'honey' (sexual intimacy) of the second husband. This hadith is well-known and establishes that intercourse is a necessary condition for tahlil. The Hanafis argue that the second husband's role as a 'hadim' (destroyer of previous divorces) applies regardless of the number of divorces, based on the general evidence of the hadith and the overall objective of Shari'ah to protect the institution of marriage.

Key Terms
خاص (khas): A word that is specific in meaning, here referring to the word 'hatta' which definitively indicates termination of prohibition.
حتى (hatta): A particle indicating the end or termination of a preceding matter. In the verse, it indicates that after the second marriage, the previous prohibition ends.
محلل (muhallil): One who makes a woman permissible for her first husband after divorce; technically, a second husband who marries a divorced woman and consummates the marriage, thereby allowing her to remarry her first husband.
نكاح (nikah): In this context, the word is debated: the Shafi'is argue it means 'marriage contract', while the Hanafis discuss that it can mean both contract and intercourse, but the verse uses it in the sense of contract because it is attributed to the woman.
حرمت غليظة (hurmat ghalizah): Severe prohibition that results after three divorces; such a woman cannot remarry her first husband without a muhallil.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the effect of a second marriage with consummation if the first husband had given only one divorce?
A) The first husband has the right to the remaining one divorce.
B) The first husband has the right to two divorces (since one was already used).
C) The first husband has the right to three divorces anew.
D) The marriage is invalid because tahlil is only for three divorces.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school relies on the hadith of Rif'ah to conclude that a second marriage with consummation resets the divorce count, regardless of the number of previous divorces.
